1601 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sch. Bd. v. King


CASE NO. 1D05-4521, 1D05-4524, and 1D05-4526 (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


940 So. 2d 593; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 18216; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2718



October 31, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 16, 2006.
Review denied by Spiegel v. King, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 610 (Fla., Mar. 27, 2007)
Review denied by Sch. Bd. v. King, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 614 (Fla., Mar. 27, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. P. Kevin Davey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school boards sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Leon County, which denied appellants' challenge to the 2004-2005 General Appropriations Act, ch. 2004-268, Laws of Fla (Act). The Act changed the method used to calculate the Florida Price Level Index (FPLI), and appellants received a smaller increase in their public school funding than they would have received under the previous calculation method.


OVERVIEW: In the 2004-2005 Act, the Florida Legislature approved state appropriations for school districts, and the Act adopted a new FPLI index recommendation that took into consideration the role of amenities in the FPLI. Appellants brought an action for declaratory judgment, naming appellees the Florida Department of Education, the Florida Legislature, and the State Board of Education as defendants. Other parties intervened as both plaintiffs and defendants in the proceedings. The lawsuit challenged the authority of the state entities, under § 1011.62(2), Fla. Stat. to select and designate a particular version of the FPLI and challenged the attempt to implement the amenities-based price level index. The trial court eventually dismissed all of the counts in the complaint. The court agreed with the trial court that no evidence had been presented to support the contention that the Florida Legislature violated Art. III, § 12, Fla. Const. when it passed the Act. The court agreed with the trial court that Art. IX, § 1, Fla. Const. was not violated in this case, but disagreed that Art. IX, § 1, Fla. Const. never provided for a private right of action against the State.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the rulings of the trial court.

 

1602 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Baycare Health Sys., Inc. v. Agency for Health Care Admin.


Case Nos. 2D05-1691, 2D05-1692, 2D05-1693, 2D05-2586, 2D05-2587, 2D05-2591, 2D05-2593, CONSOLIDATED


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


940 So. 2d 563; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 17932; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2705



October 27, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 15, 2006.
Review denied by Baycare Health Sys. v. Fla. Agency for Healthcare Admin., 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1308 (Fla., July 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Agency for Health Care Administration.
Health Options, Inc. v. Agency for Health Care Admin., 889 So. 2d 849, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17313 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated matters, appellant corporation sought review of eight orders entered by appellee, the Florida Agency for Health Care Administration (AHCA), in four separate administrative actions. The orders effectively denied reimbursement to the corporation for approximately $2 million in medical services that the corporation's hospitals provided to patients insured by appellee health maintenance organization (HMO).


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose between the corporation and the HMO about the rates that the HMO would be required to reimburse the corporation after the contract between the parties was terminated. The corporation voluntarily agreed to submit the matters to the resolution organization pursuant to § 408.7057, Fla. Stat. (2002). The resolution organization agreed with the HMO about the reimbursement rates, and the AHCA entered orders that were consistent with the resolution organization's recommendations, pursuant to § 408.7057, Fla. Stat. (2002). The court held that the corporation's due process rights were not violated because its due process rights did not extend to the voluntary private conduct of the dispute resolution procedure, even when the dispute resolution process was created by statute. The due process requirements normally afforded to administrative proceedings under §§ 120.569 and 120.57, Fla. Stat. (2002) were not applicable to the proceeding initiated under § 408.7057, Fla. Stat. (2002). The court also found that the orders of the AHCA should not be reversed, under the limited scope of review afforded to the court under § 120.68, Fla. Stat.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders made by the AHCA.

 

1603 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Farm Bureau Cas. Ins. Co. v. Cox


CASE NO. 1D05-4111


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


943 So. 2d 823; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 17891; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2679



October 26, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Question certified by, On rehearing at, Rehearing denied by, in part, Rehearing denied by, En banc, in part Fla. Farm Bureau Cas. Ins. Co. v. Cox, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20865 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 15, 2006)
Review granted by Fla. Farm Bureau v. Cox, 948 So. 2d 758, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 52 (Fla., 2007)
Later proceeding at Fla. Farm Bureau Cas. Ins. Co. v. Cox, 948 So. 2d 759, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 174 (Fla., 2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Fla. Farm Bureau Cas. Ins. Co. v. Cox, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1678 (Fla., Sept. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Santa Rosa County. R. V. Swanson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sued appellee insureds, seeking a declaratory judgment that the loss to the insureds' home resulting from a hurricane was caused primarily by flooding. The insureds counterclaimed for policy limits pursuant to former § 627.702(1), Fla. Stat. (2004), of the Florida Valued Policy Law (VPL). The Circuit Court for Santa Rosa County, Florida, granted the insureds judgment on the pleadings. The insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: A hurricane left the insureds' home a total loss. As wind and water both contributed, and the policy excluded flood damage, the insurer argued that its liability should be reduced. The trial court held that under the version of § 627.702(1) in effect at the time of the loss, as there was a total loss of a structure that was insured as to a covered peril, the insurer's liability was in the amount for which the property was insured, even if a non-covered peril also contributed to the total loss. The appellate court agreed. Though the legislature amended § 627.702 to change such a result, it specifically made the amendment prospective only. The language of former § 627.702(1) was unambiguous, and the appellate court lacked the authority to amend the VPL to render it nugatory when multiple perils combined to destroy an insured structure. Any provisions of the insurance policy that conflicted with the former VPL were nugatory.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1604 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Collazo v. McDonough


CASE NO. 1D06-0583


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


943 So. 2d 816; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 17417; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2556



October 18, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 28, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Collazo v. McDonough, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 22084 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Dec. 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County, Judge Thomas H. Bateman, III.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which denied his petition for writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the inmate raised three arguments. In the third argument, the inmate challenged the propriety of the trial court order placing a lien on his inmate trust account as a condition of his going forward with his petition for writ of mandamus. The inmate's petition for writ of mandamus challenged the disciplinary action taken against him by the Florida Department of Corrections (DOC), which resulted in the inmate's forfeiture of 30 days of gain-time. Under the circumstances, the inmate's petition qualified as a collateral criminal proceeding and his indigency determination should have been made pursuant to § 57.081, Fla. Stat. The trial court order incorrectly relied on § 57.085, Fla. Stat. to justify the imposition of a lien on the inmate's trust account. In addition to the lack of statutory authority for imposing a lien, case law indicated that such a lien was unauthorized, and appellee, the Secretary of the DOC, conceded that point.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed, without comment, the inmate's first and second arguments on appeal. To the extent that the trial court's order called for the imposition of a lien on the inmate's trust account, it was reversed. The matter was remanded to the trial court for entry of an order removing the lien from the inmate's trust account.

 

1605 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Nicol v. State


Case No. 5D05-2607


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


939 So. 2d 231; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 17011; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2542



October 13, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 1, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Lisa Munyon, Judge.
Nicol v. State, 892 So. 2d 1169, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1008 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) that, inter alia, denied his motion to suppress; defendant claimed that he had been detained without a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity.


OVERVIEW: The deputy observed two black males at a closed strip mall, looking around the corner towards a convenience store. When the deputy attempted to make contact, the men took off running. As they neared their vehicle, the deputy observed that they were wearing dark colored bandanas tied "Old West style" around their noses and covering the lower half of their faces. After backup arrived, the men were arrested on the scene for loitering and prowling. A pat-down search of defendant yielded a magazine for a semiautomatic style handgun. The handgun was found under the driver's seat and a BB style or pellet gun was found on the ground outside the passenger door. The appellate court found that the initial encounter between the deputy and defendant constituted a valid investigatory stop because the deputy had a reasonable suspicion that defendant was loitering in violation of § 856.021(2), Fla. Stat. (2001). Even if defendant's arrest for loitering and prowling were invalid, the arrest was still valid since the facts known to the officer would have supported his arrest on a valid, alternative basis. Consequently, the trial court properly denied his motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1606 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Mays v. State


CASE NO. 3D06-1314


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


944 So. 2d 397; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 16420; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2482



October 4, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 4, 2007.
Rehearing, en banc, denied by Mays v. State, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 816 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Jan. 4, 2007)
Review denied by Mays v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1498 (Fla., Aug. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal under Florida Rule of Appellate Procedure 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, William Thomas, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 90-16412.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) denied defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence, in which he claimed that (1) the statute relied upon to enhance his sentence was declared unconstitutional as violative of the single-subject rule in 1993, and (2) there was insufficient evidence presented to establish that he qualified to be sentenced as an habitual violent felony offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Upon a review of the record on appeal and as to defendant's first claim, the instant court held that because defendant was sentenced pursuant to a negotiated plea, the claim amounted to an attack regarding the voluntariness of his plea which had to be brought pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 as a motion to vacate his sentence. But, given that more than two years had passed since defendant's conviction became final, he was procedurally barred from raising such a motion. Further, the court held that even if it were to rule that the claim was properly before the court, the sentence was an habitual offender's sentence which was not affected by the amendment to § 775.084, Fla. Stat. Second, because the prior felony convictions, two robberies, occurred within five years of the sentencing at issue and were qualifying offenses for purpose of enhancement under § 775.084, the trial court correctly denied defendant relief on this claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1607 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Coleman


CASE NO.: 1D05-2734


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


937 So. 2d 1226; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 15807; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2426



September 25, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 11, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Kathleen F. Dekker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED for further proceedings consistent with this opinion; conflict certified with DuFresne I and Munao.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) granted defendant's motion to dismiss the information filed against him which charged three counts of felony child abuse, under § 827.03(1)(a), Fla. Stat. (2004), finding that defendant's verbal conduct against the three minor victims was not actionable under said statute. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State challenged the judgment entered. The instant court held that it disagreed with the Fourth District Court of Appeals case relied on by the trial court, as well as a later Fourth District case on the same issue, that to withstand an overbreadth challenge to § 827.03(1), Fla. Stat. (2004), it had to construe the statute to avoid its application to all speech. If § 827.03(1) could be construed to be applicable only to specifically described unprotected speech, it could withstand an overbreadth challenge. Further, the trial court was not asked to, nor did it, address the question of whether the information filed against defendant could withstand a challenge on these grounds. Thus, the judgment entered was reversed, and the trial court was directed to address this issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded. Further, a conflict was certified to the Florida Supreme Court with two Fourth District opinions.

 

1608 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Parrish v. State


CASE NO. 1D05-2162


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


937 So. 2d 1231; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 15832; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2425



September 25, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 11, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from a final order from the circuit court for Okaloosa County. Thomas T. Remington, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Okaloosa County (Florida) convicted defendant of possession of cannabis, possession of a controlled substance without a prescription, and resisting arrest without violence. The court also entered a final order denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized from his person upon an arresting officer's detention. Defendant appealed said order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved to suppress all the evidence seized, arguing that the deputy had no legal justification to detain him, or once detained, the deputy had no legal justification to continue to detain him. The trial court disagreed, explaining that it was reasonable for the deputy to require each party the deputy confronted, including defendant, to produce identification before being released. When defendant failed to produce any identification and lied about his name, the deputy was authorized to arrest him and to conduct a search incident to the arrest. Further, believing that a minor collision had occurred, that the deputy had probable cause to investigate. On appeal, the court agreed with this reasoning. Because the deputy had probable cause to detain defendant, it was irrelevant that his primary concern during his investigation was the prevention of domestic violence.


OUTCOME: The order denying suppression was affirmed.

 

1609 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Feliciano v. State


CASE NO. 1D05-3740


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


937 So. 2d 818; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 15458; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2395



September 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 6, 2006.
Review denied by Feliciano v. State, 948 So. 2d 758, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 23 (Fla., 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Feliciano v. State, 982 So. 2d 1180, 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 7455 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Feliciano v. McNeil, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 130865 (N.D. Fla., May 8, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Thomas H. Bateman, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) was convicted of statutory rape, in violation of Fla. Stat. § 794.05 (2003). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction, contending that the "statutory rape law" was facially unconstitutional, in that it violated due process by failing to require proof that a defendant knew the minor's age. The appeals court disagreed, given the clear and unambiguous language in Fla. Stat. § 794.021 (2003), which provided that ignorance or belief as to a victim's age was no defense. In keeping with the statute, the jury instructions did not require any finding that defendant knew the victim's age, and defendant voiced no objection to the instructions given. But, defendant filed, and the trial court denied, a motion to dismiss, urging the unconstitutionality of the statute for failure to require the State to prove scienter. Further, cases cited by defendant concerning whether, in construing a criminal statute that was silent on the subject, a mens rea requirement should be inferred, were inapposite. Even in jurisdictions where statutes were written so that courts had to decide whether legislatures intended to make knowledge of the minor's age an element of the offense, decisions on the point overwhelmingly sided against defendants.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1610 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


J.C.J. v. Heart of Adoptions, Inc. (In re Baby R.P.S.)


Case No. 2D05-2582


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


942 So. 2d 906; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 15505; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2393



September 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at J.C.J. v. Heart of Adoptions, Inc., 2008 Fla. App. LEXIS 9900 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., July 2, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; J. Kevin Carey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee agency filed a petition to terminate appellant father's parental rights pending adoption pursuant to § 63.087, Fla. Stat. The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) terminated the father's parental rights. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the father's consent to adoption was not required as he failed to comply with § 63.054, Fla. Stat. and that, since his consent was not required, the agency was entitled to the judgment terminating his parental rights. The appellate court held that, since the father failed to register, his consent to the adoption was not required and the grounds for termination listed in § 63.089(3), Fla. Stat. did not apply to him. In its petition, the agency admitted that the father was not a parent as defined by statute. Section 63.087(5), Fla. Stat. did not contemplate that one such as the father would have been a party to a termination action. While the trial court found that the father's consent was not required due to his failure to register, it nevertheless terminated his parental rights pursuant to § 63.089(3), Fla. Stat. This was error. Section 63.089(3), Fla. Stat. did not apply to the father since his consent was not required and he was not a parent. Thus, the trial court erred in terminating the rights, if any, of a party not properly contemplated by the statute stated. Due to the fundamental nature of the error, it was addressed although it was unpreserved.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded with direction to the trial court on remand to first consider the pending paternity action to determine whether the father met the statutory definition of a parent, which would have determined whether his consent to the adoption was required. Only then could the termination and adoption proceedings have been addressed.

 

1611 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Vill. of Wellington v. Palm Beach County


Nos. 4D05-2666 and 4D05-2687


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 15517; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2414



September 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication November 22, 2006.
Rehearing denied by, Rehearing, en banc, denied by, Motion granted by, Opinion replaced by Vill. of Wellington v. Palm Beach County, 941 So. 2d 595, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 19600 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2006)
Review denied by Village of Wellington v. Palm Beach County, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 494 (Fla., Mar. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals and cross-appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Jonathan D. Gerber, Judge; L.T. Case No. 502004CA9387XXXXMBAB.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipalities sued appellee charter county in the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief in a challenge to the validity of an amendment to the county's charter. The trial court, at summary judgment, found that the charter amendment was partially valid but contained three invalid provisions which the trial court severed. The parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county commission approved an ordinance to amend the county's charter to provide an exclusive method of voluntary municipal annexation for the county. A majority of the electorate of the county approved the amendment. The trial court ruled that certain portions of the amended charter contained a valid voluntary municipal annexation method but found that three provisions of the amendment were invalid. On appeal, the court found that the trial court correctly interpreted § 171.044(4), Fla. Stat. (2004) to allow charter counties to provide their own method of voluntary annexation. Moreover, the trial court correctly found that the requirement in § 171.044(4) that the exclusive method of voluntary annexation be contained in the charter itself was violated by allowing the county commission to use an ordinance to accomplish the same goal. Thus, three provisions of the charter amendment were correctly severed because they were invalid as they allowed the county commission to define the exclusive method of voluntary municipal annexation for unincorporated areas not designated as either an unincorporated protection area or an unincorporated rural neighborhood by ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

1612 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Ramsubhag v. State


No. 4D05-2621


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


937 So. 2d 1192; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 15148; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2371



September 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 20, 2006.  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Ramsubhag v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 17617 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Jack H. Cook, Judge; L.T. Case No. 04CF005009A02.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifteenth Judicial Circuit Court, Palm Beach County (Florida), entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of possession of cocaine and possession of a schedule IV substance, Xanax. Defendant was then sentenced. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Paramedics found defendant passed out and slumped over the steering wheel of a parked car. Police officers who responded noticed an odor of alcohol, bloodshot eyes, and clammy skin. The officers decided to take him into custody. Incident thereto, the officers found a clear plastic baggie containing cocaine and pills known as Xanax. Defendant told the officers that the pills belonged to his girlfriend. At trial, however, he testified that he found the pills in the car, which belonged to his boss, and he pocketed them to prevent his children from exposure, with the intention of returning them to his boss. The trial court declined to give defendant's requested jury instruction on lawful disposition--brief possession plus an innocent intent to dispose of them--since his children had been picked up by their mother 10 hours before the Xanax was discovered. The jury convicted defendant on the possession of cocaine and of a controlled substance. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court did not err in declining to give his requested lawful disposition instruction since the facts did not support a finding of brief possession and an innocent intent to dispose.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments of conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1613 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Wovas v. Tousa Homes, Inc.


Case No. 2D06-2407


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


940 So. 2d 1166; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 14954; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2330



September 8, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 16, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Wovas v. Tousa Homes, Inc., 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 21716 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Oct. 11, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Writ of Prohibition to the Circuit County for Lee County; Jay B. Rosman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner lot owners sought a writ of prohibition to the Circuit County for Lee County (Florida) stopping it from ruling upon a petition for writ of prohibition filed by appellee developers; the lot owners claimed that the circuit court lacks jurisdiction to issue the writ to the developers.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to § 720.311, Fla. Stat. (2005), the lot owners sought mandatory binding arbitration to require the developers to relinquish control of a homeowners' association to the residents. Claiming that, among other things, § 720.311 was unconstitutional, the developers sought to prohibit an agency from conducting arbitration. The circuit court issued an order to show cause why the writ should not be issued. The district court found that a petition for issuance of an extraordinary writ challenging matters in an administrative action was properly filed in a district court of appeal, not a circuit court. Therefore, the lot owners correctly argued that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction under Fla. Const. art. V, § 5(b), § 26.012, Fla. Stat. (2005) to issue a writ to the developers.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted, and the circuit court's order to show cause was quashed.

 

1614 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. State


No. 4D05-531


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


937 So. 2d 742; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 14643; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2538



September 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 20, 2006.
Review denied by Foster v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 520 (Fla., Mar. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Ilona Holmes, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-1580 CF 10A.
Foster v. State, 875 So. 2d 1253, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 6995 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment and sentence of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), entered upon her conviction pursuant to § 859.01, Fla. Stat. (2000), for poisoning by food or water.


OVERVIEW: At trial, a chemist testified that the substance defendant was charged with using was commercially available as rat poison. Defendant admitted pouring the poison into the victim's drink, and it was captured on videotape. She testified that she did it to make the victim sick, but not to hurt him. The appellate court affirmed the trial court judgment and sentence. The absence of a definition of poison did not make § 859.01 unconstitutionally vague. Relying upon dictionaries that defined poison, in effect, as a substance that causes injury, illness, or death, the appellate court concluded that the term had a plain, ordinary, and accepted meaning that could be understood by a person of ordinary intelligence to place that person on notice of forbidden conduct. The failure to indicate a required dosage did not make § 859.01 unconstitutionally vague or encourage arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement because the legislature could not be expected to list every possible harmful substance. Defendant's argument regarding unconstitutional application was waived because it was not raised before her motion for a new trial, but in any event § 859.01 was not unconstitutional as applied to her.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment and sentence.

 

1615 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Munao v. State


No. 4D05-2460


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


939 So. 2d 125; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 14656; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2268



September 1, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 31, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Munao v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 18842 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 31, 2006)
Review denied by State v. Munao, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 501 (Fla., Mar. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County; Gary L. Sweet, Judge; L.T. Case No. 562003CF004822A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded with Directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, St. Lucie County (Florida) of child abuse and solicitation to commit aggravated battery. He was sentenced to five years on each count, to be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The allegations in the case stemmed primarily from two telephone conversations between defendant and his son, who said defendant asked him twice to go in the kitchen, get a knife, and stab his mother. Defendant argued that his child abuse conviction had to be vacated because oral statements alone could not support a conviction for child abuse under § 827.03(1)(b), Fla. Stat. (2003). The appeals court agreed. Section 827.03(1)(b) prohibited "an intentional act" which was seemingly an attempt to outlaw the act that inflicted the harm, not the actual harm itself. However, the statute contained no parameters or guidelines as to what constituted an act under the statute. Therefore, in reference to speech which constituted an intentional act or conduct, any statements by a parent or teacher directed towards a child which could cause mental injury would be subject to prosecution as child abuse. Thus, it appeared that the statute actually outlawed a result derived from any act, making the statute applicable to a wide range of acts causing a "physical or mental injury upon a child."


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded and the trial court was directed to enter a judgment of acquittal for the child abuse charge. Defendant's other issues on appeal concerning prejudicial evidence were not preserved and did not represent fundamental error. Accordingly, his conviction for solicitation to commit aggravated battery was affirmed.

Baker v. Fla. Dep't of Agric. & Consumer Servs.


No. 4D05-3922


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


937 So. 2d 1161; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 14668; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2271



September 1, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 17, 2006.  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Baker v. Dep't of Agric., 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 17601 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Oct. 17, 2006)
Review denied by Baker v. Fla. Dep't of Agric. & Consumer Servs., 2007 Fla. LEXIS 538 (Fla., Mar. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the State of Florida, Division of Administrative Hearings, Department of Agriculture and Consumer Services; L.T. Case No. 05-0023.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a disciplinary proceeding, appellee State of Florida, Division of Administrative Hearings, Department of Agriculture and Consumer Services, found that appellant pest-control technician applied a deficient concentration of a pesticide used for the prevention of subterranean termites in violation of Fla. Stat. §§ 482.051(5), 482.161(1)(e), and Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 5E-14.106(6). The technician sought review.


OVERVIEW: The technician alleged, inter alia, that the rule was applied inconsistently. The appellate court found that there was no specific rule detailing how staff, under these circumstances, should have conducted internal procedure in investigating, reviewing, and deciding to bring a complaint, but that each case was processed on a case by case basis. There was no dispute that the department required compliance with the rule as to pesticide concentration, or that the technician failed to comply. The technician did not contend he was without notice that his failure to apply the required concentration could have resulted in a penalty. There was no deviation from internal policy in the process followed in preparing and deciding to file the complaint. A person subject to department discipline had no statutory right to have the case investigated and reviewed in a specific manner. Baker objected to administrative discussions during the investigation and charging process. There was no meeting of a public collegial body. Communication among administrative staff in fulfilling investigatory, advisory, or charging functions did not constitute a "Sunshine" Law violation.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Avrich v. State


CASE NO. 3D05-1100


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


936 So. 2d 739; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 14034; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2208



August 23, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 8, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Barbara Areces, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 04-24894.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) convicted defendant of 37 counts charging him with extortion, in violation of Fla. Stat. § 836.05 (2004), and making obscene and harassing telephone calls, in violation of both Fla. Stat. §§ 365.16(1)(a) and (1)(b) (2004), after denying his motion for a judgment of acquittal. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his convictions as to counts 2 through 9 had to be reversed for insufficient evidence because the State failed to prove that the victim enjoyed a reasonable expectation of privacy on his business telephone line. The appeals court agreed. It was evident from the record evidence that defendant made telephone calls to the victim's business telephone line, located in the victim's home where he conducted his business. Although the victim enjoyed a reasonable expectation of privacy in his home, that expectation was not extended to his business phone, despite such being in his home.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences as to counts 1 and counts 10 through 37 were affirmed. But, convictions and sentences as to counts 2 through 9 were reversed.

Montejo v. Martin Mem'l Med. Ctr., Inc.


No. 4D05-652


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


935 So. 2d 1266; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 14039; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2212



August 23, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 8, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; William L. Roby, Judge; L.T. Case No. 04-715 CA.
Montejo v. Martin Mem'l Med. Ctr., Inc., 874 So. 2d 654, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 6263 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Marion County (Florida), dismissed appellant guardian's false imprisonment claim, involving the guardian's ward, filed against appellee hospital. The guardian appealed.


OVERVIEW: The guardian challenged the judgment entered. While the appeals court found that he had standing to bring the false imprisonment claim, at issue was whether the hospital was entitled to immunity from said claim for actions it took in reliance upon an order that was later determined to have been entered in the absence of subject matter jurisdiction. The appeals court held that it was not. Its actions were taken neither during the course of the judicial proceedings nor in an effort to prosecute or defend its lawsuit. Additionally, the appeals court disagreed with the hospital's claim that because it acted in reliance on a court order, it should be cloaked with qualified or quasi-judicial immunity to the same extent as that afforded to state agents executing the order of a trial court, as the hospital was not an agent of the government executing an order of the court. Instead, by procuring and obtaining the order allowing the deportation of the ward so that he could receive the much needed medical care in Guatemala, the hospital was seeking the vindication or enforcement of a purely private right.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Citizens for Responsible Growth v. City of St. Pete Beach


Case No. 2D06-550


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


940 So. 2d 1144; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 13813; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2196



August 18, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 22, 2006. As Corrected August 25, 2006. Released for Publication September 7, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Citizens for Responsible Growth v. City of St. Petersburg, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 21719 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Sept. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Walt Logan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city sued appellant citizens, seeking declaratory relief under Fla. Stat. ch. 86 (2005), claiming the citizens' proposed amendments to the city charter that they intended to place on the ballot were invalid. The Circuit Court for Pinellas County, Florida, ruled that three of the four proposed amendments were preempted by Fla. Stat. ch. 163 (2005). The city and citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: The proposed amendments stated that unanimous city commission approval would be required to approve comprehensive land use plans or plan amendments affecting five or fewer parcels (petition II); that voter approval was required for approval of or effectiveness of a community redevelopment plan (petition I), an increase in allowable height of structures (petition III), or a comprehensive land use plan or comprehensive land use plan amendment (petition IV). The trial court held that petitions I, III, and IV were preempted by Fla. Stat. ch. 163. The appellate court initially held that the trial court had jurisdiction to make a pre-election determination of the facial constitutionality of the proposed amendments. None of the amendments were facially unconstitutional or unconstitutional in their entirety, not because they merely added another step in an already detailed process, but because they were inferentially permitted by Fla. Stat. § 163.3167(12) (2005). Petition II would establish only an internal procedural rule as to the number of commissioners who had to agree on an amendment affecting five or fewer parcels; this requirement was not a "referendum" proscribed by § 163.3167(12)


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment approving petition II, reversed the judgment invalidating petitions I, III, and IV, and remanded with instructions for the trial court to enter judgment in favor of the citizens and to order the city to place all four of the proposed amendments on the ballot.

Ward v. State


CASE NO. 3D05-1277


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


936 So. 2d 1143; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 13682; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 2160



August 16, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 1, 2006.
Review granted by Ward v. State, 939 So. 2d 96, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2436 (Fla., 2006)
Approved by, Certified question answered by Ward v. State, 986 So. 2d 479, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 39 (Fla., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 05-1287.
Ward v. State, 433 So. 2d 1221, 1983 Fla. App. LEXIS 19494 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 1983)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner sought a writ of prohibition to bar the lower court from commencing a trial to have him declared a "sexually violent predator" and involuntarily committed to the custody of the Florida Department of Children and Families for care, control, and treatment pursuant to the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. §§ 394.910-930 (2005).


OVERVIEW: The question was whether the State was authorized under the Ryce Act to seek to involuntarily commit to the Department for care and treatment, a person who had been convicted of a sexually violent crime in the past and who was brought into "total confinement," as that term was defined, after January 1, 1999, for any crime, sexual or non-sexual in nature. The prisoner had been convicted of several rapes in the past. His most recent crime was for burglary. The appellate court held the scope of the second clause of the Ryce Act encompassed otherwise qualifying sexual offenders whether or not they were then incarcerated for a sexual or non-sexual offense. Although the appellate court believed a sound reading of the text and correct application of the rules of statutory construction impelled the result it reached, it also believed its construction of the statute comported with the history and purpose behind the Ryce Act. Thus, the prisoner could be declared a "sexually violent predator" and involuntarily committed to the Department under Fla. Stat. § 394.925.


OUTCOME: The writ was denied. The issue was certified as of great public importance.

Brevard County v. Stack


Case No. 5D05-2935


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


932 So. 2d 1258; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 11802; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1895



July 14, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 2, 2006.
Review denied by Brevard County v. Stack, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 169 (Fla., Jan. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Non Final Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, George W. Maxwell III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part; REVERSED and REMANDED in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida), which granted partial summary judgment in favor of appellee investors in the investors' lawsuit brought against the county under the Bert J. Harris, Jr. Act (Act), Fla. Stat. § 70.001 (2004).


OVERVIEW: In 1984 and 1987, the investors purchased two adjoining parcels of land. The property was over four acres, with a wetlands area in the center of about one acre. In September 2000, the county adopted an ordinance that restricted commercial land development activities on property, such as the investors', which contained wetlands. The investors submitted a notice of claim to the county when they could not sell the property to a developer, pursuant to the Act, because they claimed that the value of the property was reduced by the county ordinance. The trial court granted the investors' motion for partial summary judgment on the issue of liability. The court found that the Act was constitutional and did not violate due process. The Act did not affect the inherent power of the county to exercise its sovereign power, but merely required the government to provide relief to a property owner when the action reduced property values. The Act did not violate the separation of powers because it contained sufficient provisions to enable a court to make the determinations required under the Act. The trial court did not make sufficient findings as required by Fla. Stat. § 70.001(6).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court to the extent that it found that the Act was constitutional. The court reversed the decision of the trial court to the extent that it did not make findings of fact as required under the Act, and remanded the matter for additional findings.

Hughes v. State


CASE NO. 3D05-1767


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


943 So. 2d 176; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 11604; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1872



July 12, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 22, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Hughes v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 22443 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Dec. 22, 2006)
Review denied by Hughes v. State, 959 So. 2d 716, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1070 (Fla., 2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Cloyd v. McDonough, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 125729 (S.D. Fla., Jan. 7, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, David H. Young, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 02-19207.
Cloyd v. State, 943 So. 2d 149, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 11605 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) finding him guilty with a codefendant of operating an aircraft while intoxicated or in a careless or reckless manner, in violation of Fla. Stat. § 860.13 (2002).


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found that as applied to defendant, who attempted to pilot a commercial aircraft with an estimated blood alcohol level of between .113 and .145 at the time defendant was performing preflight checks on board the aircraft, Fla. Stat. § 860.13 was not unconstitutionally vague, and defendant lacked standing to facially attack the statute on vagueness grounds. Defendant's conduct was clearly prohibited by the statute and he could not seriously contend that he was not on notice that his conduct was illegal based on the statute's failure to define "under the influence." Since (1) the State was required to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant did operate the aircraft (an essential element of the crime charged); (2) the State's case was premised on whether defendant violated the statute by taking control of the aircraft and performing the preflight functions while under the influence of alcohol; and (3) there was no evidence of any mechanical or other problem which rendered the aircraft incapable of being operated without substantial mechanical repairs, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by failing to instruct on inoperability.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cloyd v. State


CASE NO. 3D05-1816


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 22, 2006.  [**1]
Related proceeding at Hughes v. State, 943 So. 2d 176, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 11604 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2006)
Rehearing denied by Cloyd v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 22444 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Dec. 22, 2006)
Review denied by Cloyd v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1058 (Fla., June 4, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, David H. Young, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 02-19207.
Hughes v. State, 882 So. 2d 392, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 13984 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was criminally prosecuted with a codefendant and convicted in the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) of operating an aircraft while intoxicated or in a careless or reckless manner, in violation of Fla. Stat. § 860.13 (2002). Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found that as applied to defendant, who attempted to pilot a commercial aircraft with an estimated blood alcohol level of between .121 and .15 at the time he was performing preflight checks on board the aircraft, § 860.13 was not unconstitutionally vague, and defendant lacked standing to facially attack the statute on vagueness grounds. Holmes v. State


Case No. 2D06-1772


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


933 So. 2d 1205; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 10786; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1803



June 30, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus to the Circuit Court for Polk County; Ronald A. Herring, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed for a writ of habeas corpus to a Florida Circuit Court, challenging his pretrial detention in relation to two cases. Petitioner, a homeless man, had been cited for soliciting without a permit, a violation of Lakeland, Florida, Code, § 78-4, (1960), a municipal ordinance. Petitioner had failed to appear at his scheduled hearing, a capias was issued and when arrested, he had two legend drug pills without a prescription.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had made an initial appearance on both offenses and had been ordered held in the county jail after his arrest. Petitioner subsequently filed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus, after being held for 60 days. The court observed that the maximum penalty for a violation of Lakeland, Florida, Code, § 78-4, (1960), was 60 days, and that the record did not reflect that petitioner had been arraigned. The court therefore held that because petitioner had been held for as long as possible on the panhandling charge had he been convicted of the ordinance violation, the granting of his petition was required as to that case. The court declined to address petitioner's contention that the municipal ordinance was unconstitutional, holding that because the case could be disposed of on other grounds, the constitutional question should not be addressed.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition.

Rollins, Inc. v. Butland


Case No. 2D05-368


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT

June 30, 2006, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted opinion at, Remanded by Rollins, Inc. v. Butland, 951 So. 2d 860, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20861 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2006)
Rehearing granted by, Opinion withdrawn by Rollins, Inc. v. Butland, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 20856 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Dec. 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from nonfinal order of the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Emmett Lamar Battles, Judge.
Rollins, Inc. v. Butland, 852 So. 2d 895, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11735 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Hillsborough County Circuit Court (Florida) certified a class and a subclass after appellee putative class representatives filed a class action complaint against appellants, a parent company and a subsidiary, alleging claims arising from the subsidiary's contractual undertakings related to the control of subterranean termites and the putative class representatives moved for class certification. The parent company and subsidiary appealed.


OVERVIEW: The putative class representatives filed a class action complaint against the parent company and the subsidiary for multiple claims arising from subsidiary's contractual undertakings related to controlling subterranean termites. The claims included deceptive and unfair trade practices, misleading advertising, Florida RICO-criminal racketeering, breach of contract, unjust enrichment, and for declaratory and injunctive relief. The putative class representatives moved for class certification. The trial court certified a class and one subclass under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(2) and Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(b)(3). On appeal, the appellate court found that the putative class representatives' claims did not meet the requirements for class certification under either of those rules. For instance, the appellate court found that some proposed members sustained damages to their residence while some sustained no such damage. It also found that the putative class representatives alleged no less than 14 separate deceptive or unfair practices, and that the trial court's solution for proving damages was a potential denial of the parent company and subsidiary's substantive due process rights.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that certified the class was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court with directions to decertify the class.

Lundy v. Four Seasons Ocean Grand Palm Beach


CASE NO. 1D05-0109


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


932 So. 2d 506; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 10425; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1663



June 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 6, 2006.
Review denied by Lundy v. Four Seasons Ocean Grand Palm Beach, 939 So. 2d 93, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1844 (Fla., Aug. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Judge of Compensation Claims. Shelley M. Punancy, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of a final order of the Florida Judge of Compensation Claims (JCC), which denied the stipulated attorney's fees requested. The claimant and appellees, the employer and the insurance carrier had entered into a stipulated agreement concerning the fees to be paid. The JCC found that the fees were in excess of those allowed by Fla. Stat. § 440.34(1) (2004). Instead, the JCC approved the fee permitted by § 440.34(1).


OVERVIEW: The claimant contended that Fla. Stat. § 440.34(1) should be construed to allow a fee that exceeded the mandated percentage on the benefits secured, and that § 440.34 violated the Florida Constitution. The court held that the JCC properly construed § 440.34(1), because the statute clearly set forth the formula for setting the fees based upon the amount of benefits secured. The JCC could not accept the stipulation when § 440.34(1) expressly prohibited the approval of the fee that was in excess of the fee provisions. Fla. Stat. § 440.34(1) did not violate the equal protection clause or the due process clause because the statute had a reasonable relationship to the state's interest in regulating fees to preserve the benefits awarded to the claimant. Section 440.34(1) was not discriminatory, arbitrary, or oppressive because it applied to all workers' compensation claimants and did not impinge upon the right to be represented by counsel. Fla. Stat. § 440.34 did not impermissibly restrict the right to freely contract, because the section was enacted to protect claimants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the JCC. The court certified a question for review by the Florida Supreme Court.

Lee County v. Brown


Case No. 2D05-2711


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


929 So. 2d 1202; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 9095; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1581



June 9, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 28, 2006.
Review denied by Brown v. Lee County, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 275 (Fla., Feb. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lee County; Jay B. Rosman, Judge.
Brown v. Lee County, 912 So. 2d 1223, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 8037 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, a class of persons who executed land development or sale contracts but did not qualify for a school impact fee exemption, and determined that the county's school impact fee ordinance, Lee County, Fla., Ordinance No. 01-21, constituted a facially unconstitutional impairment on construction contracts.


OVERVIEW: The declaratory judgment action sought a determination that the assessment of the fee constituted an unconstitutional impairment of plaintiffs' contract rights under the contract clause of Fla. Const. art. I, § 10, both facially and as applied. The trial court granted summary judgment to plaintiffs upon a finding that Lee County, Fla., Ordinance No. 01-21 was facially unconstitutional because it impaired the contract clause. The Ordinance allegedly placed an impermissible burden on contracts as to all plaintiffs who executed contracts prior to the effective date for purposes of fee payment. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred, as there were circumstances under which the Ordinance validly required payment of the fee prior to the issuance of building permits. Further, the facial validity determination was not limited to contracts executed prior to the effective date, and there were instances after such time where the fee was valid. The as-applied challenge had not been reached by the trial court. On remand, the court directed the trial court regarding which balancing test to apply from varying judicial precedents for purposes of a contract impairment determination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

T.A. Enters. v. Olarte, Inc.


Nos. 4D05-829 and 4D05-3052


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


931 So. 2d 1016; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 8940; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1548



June 7, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at, Remanded by T.A. Enters. v. Olarte, Inc., 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 3728 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Mar. 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Consolidated appeals from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Miette K. Burnstein, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-17597CACE21.
T.A. Enters. v. Olarte, Inc., 835 So. 2d 1235, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 751 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss the appeal and quash a portion of the trial court's orders is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action filed under Florida's Lemon Law, Fla. Stat. § 681.10 et seq. (2001), the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit Court, Broward County (Florida), entered judgment in favor of appellee buyer, adopting the arbitration award. In an amended final judgment, the court awarded the buyer double damages, pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 681.1095(13) (2001) and attorney's fees. The seller appealed from both orders, and the buyer moved to dismiss the same.


OVERVIEW: The buyer moved to dismiss the seller's two appeals unless the seller complied with the trial court's order to pay its attorney's fees. The appeals court stayed the appeals on the merits to consider the seller's contention that Fla. Stat. § 681.1095(14) was unconstitutional. The court held that it was, finding a violation of both Fla. Const. art. V, § 4 and Fla. Const. art. I, § 21, as the statute failed to provide a manufacturer with an alternative remedy for appeal or a commensurate benefit. A manufacturer's appeal was heard only after paying the consumer's attorney's fees; the manufacturer received no benefit from paying the fees. Second, the statute lacked reciprocity because it did not require consumers to pay a manufacturer's attorney's fees if the appeal proved meritorious. Third, imposing an onerous attorney's fee requirement on the right to appeal was not the only method that a statute could utilize to encourage a timely resolution of a consumer problem with a motor vehicle. The requirements of Fla. Stat. § 681.1095(14) went well beyond those minimal appellate cost bonds that the Florida Supreme Court upheld as a valid exercise of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss the appeal was denied, and that portion of the trial court's order compelling the seller to pay the buyer's attorney's fees as a condition to further appeal was quashed.

 

1633 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Dep't of Revenue v. Bridger


CASE NO. 3D05-1784


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


935 So. 2d 536; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 8889; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1573



June 7, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 28, 2006.  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Dep't of Revenue v. Bridger, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 15227 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Sept. 5, 2006)
Review denied by Fla. Dep't of Revenue v. Bridger, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 294 (Fla., Feb. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Leon M. Firtel, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 96-0901.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action lawsuit seeking tax refunds, the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) denied summary judgment to appellant, the State of Florida Department of Revenue (Department), and granted the same, in part, to appellee taxpayers. The Department and the taxpayers both appealed from the decisions entered against them.


OVERVIEW: The Department appealed the judgment entered against it but merely reiterated issues already considered and rejected by the instant court. Thus, the law of the case doctrine precluded reconsideration of these issues. The taxpayers' cross-appeal contended that the final judgment improperly limited the relief granted to appellee husband and wife and those who filed individualized claims with the Department or affirmatively intervened in the action within three years of paying the unconstitutional tax. Thus, they argued that the relief granted should have extended to those who had paid the unconstitutional tax within the three years after the instant action had commenced, regardless of whether an administrative remedy had been pursued. The appeals court found that the trial court did not apply the law of the case when it limited the relief to members of the class who had timely filed for a refund. Hence, the matter was remanded so that the final judgment applied to all taxpayers who paid the unconstitutional tax within the three years when this action was commenced, regardless of whether they filed an administrative action.


OUTCOME: That portion of the final judgment, insofar as the doctrine of the law of the case prevented the Department from reasserting its previously rejected positions, was affirmed. However, that portion of the taxpayers' cross-appeal that conflicted with the instant court's prior decision in Leon was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1634 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Citizens for Reform v. Citizens for Open Gov't, Inc.


CASE NO. 3D05-2168


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


931 So. 2d 977; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 8544; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1512



May 31, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Miami-Dade County v. Citizens for Reform, 939 So. 2d 93, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1922 (Fla., Aug. 31, 2006)
Review denied by Citizens for Open Gov't, Inc. v. Citizens for Reform, 939 So. 2d 92, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1918 (Fla., Aug. 31, 2006)
Review denied by S. Fla. AFL-CIO v. Citizens for Reform, 939 So. 2d 1060, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2171 (Fla., Sept. 12, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Michael A. Genden, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 05-11996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens' group sought to submit to voters a referendum on a proposed amendment to the Miami-Dade County Charter. Appellees, another group and two unions, opposed the amendment. The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) enjoined a county elections department from placing the proposed amendment on the ballot, although it found that the ballot summary and a petition were proper. Both parties challenged the trial court's rulings.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the trial court's findings that the ballot met the requirements of Fla. Stat. § 101.161 (2005) and that the petition in support of the referendum was properly notarized. As for the proposed amendment, the trial court had found that it removed the Miami-Dade County Commission as the "governing body" under Fla. Const. art. VIII, § 6(e), n.3. The court held that the trial court erred. Under the proposed amendment, the Commission retained all of the powers afforded to it under the present charter. Moreover, Fla. Stat. § 125.01(1) (2005) enumerated the powers of a "legislative and governing body." There was no dispute that the Commission presently possessed the bulk of those powers, and it would continue to exercise them under the proposed amendment. The proposed changes would transfer to the mayor a great deal of control over the administration of county government; however, these administrative powers, which were currently held by the county manager, were not "governing body" powers. The elimination of the Commission's power to remove the county manager also did not change its status as "governing body." Its power to remove the county manager was already limited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings as to the ballot summary and the notarization of the petition. It reversed the finding that the proposed amendment was unconstitutional. It remanded the case.

Fulmore v. Charlotte County


Case No. 2D04-3179, Case No. 2D04-3283, Case No. 2D04-3293, Case No. 2D04-3429, Case No. 2D04-3430, Case No. 2D05-13, Case No. 2D05-17, Case No. 2D05-24, Case No. 2D05-29, Case No. 2D05-2708, Case No. 2D05-3315, Case No. 2D05-4156, Case No. 2D05-4159 CONSOLIDATED


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


928 So. 2d 1281; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 8562; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1490



May 31, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 16, 2006.
Review dismissed by Fulmore v. Charlotte County, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1676 (Fla., July 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from final and nonfinal orders of the Circuit Court for Charlotte County; William L. Blackwell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After certain eminent domain takings began, appellant landowners brought a declaratory judgment action against appellees, Charlotte County, Florida, and a community redevelopment agency, challenging the Community Redevelopment Act of 1969, Fla. Stat. §§ 163.330-.463 (2003). The Circuit Court for Charlotte County, Florida, dismissed the facial challenge and ruled that the Act was not unconstitutional as applied. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under Fla. Stat. § 163.356, the agency was created, and a finding of necessity report was issued, finding, as the Act required, that the area was blighted. The landowners argued that the condemnations did not serve a public purpose, as Fla. Const. art. X, § 6(a) required, that their land was not blighted, and that the definition of "blighted area" in Fla. Stat. § 163.340(8) was unconstitutionally vague. Upholding the Act's constitutionality, the court on appeal ruled that the landowners' acknowledgment that several of the factors in § 163.340(8) were objective and quantifiable showed that § 163.340(8) was not vague in all of its applications; the facial challenge thus had to fail. The court also ruled that the agency, in focusing on the roads, had satisfied the deteriorated structures requirement in the definition of a "blighted area" because "structures" included buildings and infrastructure, which included roads. Moreover, § 163.340(8) required that two or more of the enumerated blight factors had to be shown, and the trial court found that the evidence supported five of them. The Act also was not unconstitutional as applied to the case, as more than one blight factor was proven.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders.

1638 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Hines v. State


CASE NO. 1D05-5228


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


931 So. 2d 148; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 6901; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1277



May 8, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 28, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Hines v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 11343 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., June 12, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a mentally retarded defendant, sought a writ of certiorari to review an order rendered by a Florida trial court denying his motion to dismiss his pending second-degree murder charge, pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 916.303(1) (2002). This matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the instant court was whether Fla. Stat. § 916.303(1) created a substantive right requiring dismissal of criminal charges, without prejudice, against a mentally retarded defendant who remained incompetent to proceed to trial for more than two years. Because the court held that the Florida legislature granted a defendant a substantive right to dismissal of the criminal charge after two years when it enacted § 916.303(1), defendant herein was entitled to the relief he requested. Moreover, the court held that because § 916.303(1) conferred a substantive right, it took precedence over Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.213(a). However, nothing in Fla. Stat. § 916.303(1) prohibits the civil commitment of defendant to protect defendant and the public from harm.


OUTCOME: The writ was granted, and the matter was remanded. On remand, the trial court was to allow defendant to be involuntarily admitted to residential services under Fla. Stat. § 393.11 (2002), or such other appropriate action as the court determined. In addition, the State was not precluded from pursuing any other appropriate action regarding defedant as authorized by law.

Davis v. State


Case No. 5D05-4322


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


928 So. 2d 442; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 6164; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1192



April 28, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 17, 2006.
Review denied by Davis v. State, 950 So. 2d 413, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 183 (Fla., 2007)
Complaint dismissed at Davis v. Kvalheim, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 39922 (M.D. Fla., June 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Davis v. State, 898 So. 2d 949, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5252 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Petition for Habeas Corpus DENIED On The Merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus, claiming, among other things, the ineffective assistance of his appellate counsel. This matter followed.


OVERVIEW: Upon reviewing the inmate's claims, the court found that they either lacked merit, were not preserved for review, or should have been raised on direct appeal. First, a credibility of the witnesses claim was for the jury, not the appellate court, to consider. Second, a claim that counsel failed to make additional arguments when challenging the constitutionality of the state statutes and ordinances the inmate was found to have violated lacked merit because the inmate failed to allege the specific acts and omissions he claimed amounted to a serious deficiency in counsel's performance. Third, the inmate failed to identify which evidence was illegally seized and how it was used to obtain a search warrant. Further, he failed to allege that a motion to suppress said evidence was filed, which might have preserved the issue for review. If not preserved, appellate counsel could not raise such issues on appeal, and could not be deemed deficient for not raising them. The same was true for the inmate's personal and subject matter jurisdiction claims. Finally, the inmate's sufficiency of the evidence challenge was improperly part of his petition and a double jeopardy claim lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The writ was denied on the merits.

St. Vincent's Med. Ctr. v. Mem'l Healthcare Group


CASE NO. 1D05-1727


DISTRICT COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


928 So. 2d 430; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 6201; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1171



April 28, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 16, 2006.
Affirmed by St. Vincent's Med. Ctr., Inc. v. Mem'l Healthcare Group, Inc., 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1595 (Fla., Sept. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from a declaratory judgment of the Circuit Court for Leon County. P. Kevin Davey, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee hospitals filed an action against the Agency for Health Care Administration in which they argued that Fla. Stat. § 408.036(3)(l) (2004) was a special law. Appellant hospital intervened. The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) held in a declaratory judgment that the statute violated Fla. Const. art. III, § 10. Appellant challenged the decision. Appellees filed a cross-appeal arguing that the statute violated equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The statute exempted any adult open-heart surgery program meeting its criteria from a certificate-of-need requirement. It had a "sunset date" of January 1, 2008. Appellees argued that appellant was the only hospital that could meet the criteria. The trial court concluded that the statute was a special law passed in the guise of a general law and thus was unconstitutional because the legislature had not adhered to the notice requirements of Fla. Const. art. III, § 10. The court stated that the determination of whether the statute was a special law boiled down to the issue of whether it could prospectively apply to parties other than appellant. The trial court had applied the correct legal standard by stating that the test was whether there was "some potential for the statute to be applied to any other hospital." It had then heard conflicting expert testimony on whether other hospitals could reasonably qualify for the exemption before the sunset date, and its determination that no hospital besides appellant could do so was supported by competent substantial evidence, particularly the testimony of appellees' experts. The court found no merit to appellees' equal protection argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree.

Save Our Beaches v. Fla. Dep't of Envtl. Prot.


CASE NO. 1D05-4086


DISTRICT COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


27 So. 3d 48; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 6244; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1173



April 28, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
As Corrected May 5, 2006.
Rehearing denied by, Rehearing, en banc, denied by, Question certified by Save Our Beaches, Inc. v. Fla. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 10950 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., July 3, 2006)
Review granted by Fla. Dep't of Envtl. Prot. v. Save Our Beaches, Inc., 937 So. 2d 1099, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2254 (Fla., 2006)
Review granted by Walton County v. Save Our Beaches, Inc., 937 So. 2d 1100, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2253 (Fla., 2006)
Quashed by, Certified question answered by Walton County v. Stop the Beach Renourishment, Inc., 998 So. 2d 1102, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1646 (Fla., Sept. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Department of Environmental Protection.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Florida Department of Environmental Protection (Department), determined that a joint permit allowing renourishment of 6.9 miles of beaches and dunes within appellee city and county was properly issued, contrary to the claims of appellants, two non-profit groups (groups). The groups appealed, bringing only an as-applied constitutional challenge, and did not challenge the Department's standing or other rulings.


OVERVIEW: The groups argued that the final order unconstitutionally applied the Beach and Shore Preservation Act. But, the appeals court found that the first group lacked standing to argue that it was adversely affected by the Department's order. Thus, its appeal was dismissed. As to the second group, it was clear that all the members therein owned property in the affected area, and thus had standing to challenge the order on appeal. Finding that the second group could bring constitutional challenges, the appeals court agreed that the second group's riparian rights to: (i) receive accretions and relictions to the property, and (ii) have the property's contact with the water remain intact, were eliminated by the Department's final order. Because their riparian rights were unconstitutionally taken without an eminent domain proceeding. as required by Fla. Stat. § 161.141, those rights were infringed upon, requiring satisfactory evidence of sufficient upland interest pursuant to Fla. Admin. Code r. 18-21.004(3). Hence, under § 161.141 (2005), if the project could not reasonably be accomplished without the taking of private property, the taking had to be made through eminent domain.


OUTCOME: The judgment approving the permit was reversed, and the case was remanded for the Department to provide satisfactory evidence of sufficient upland interest pursuant to Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 18-21.004(3)(b).
