Wegner v. State


Case No. 2D04-2486


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


928 So. 2d 436; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 6207; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1206



April 28, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 22, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Dick Prince, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) convicted defendant of receiving computer transmissions of descriptive or identifying information about a minor for the purpose of sexual conduct with a child, in violation of Fla. Stat. § 847.0135(2)(d) (2000), and for showing obscene material to a minor, in violation of Fla. Stat. § 847.0133 (2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that Fla. Stat. § 847.0135(2)(d) was unconstitutional as it: (1) violated his due process rights by lacking a mens rea element, requiring the offender to know that the person from whom computer transmissions were received was a minor; and (2) violated the First Amendment by encompassing protected expression. First, despite the statute's lack of an explicitly stated mens rea element, the appeals court construed the statute as requiring knowledge by the accused that the person from whom or about whom he received the computer transmissions was a minor. Because the State charged defendant with knowledge of that fact, and the trial court required the State to prove it, no due process violation resulted. Moreover, reading a mens rea requirement into § 847.1035(2)(d) similarly required defendant to possess actual knowledge, or to believe that the person from whom he received computer transmissions of descriptive or identifying information was a minor, and that defendant did so for one purpose of facilitating sexual conduct with that minor. As a result of this holding, the court rejected defendant's First Amendment overbreadth contention.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kish v. A.W. Chesterton Co.


CASE NO. 3D05-1538


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


930 So. 2d 704; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5950; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,449; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1139



April 26, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Kish v. AW Chesterton Co., 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 11596 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., June 27, 2006)
Review denied by Kish v. A.W. Chesterton Co., 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2563 (Fla., Oct. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Joseph P. Farina, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 04-18285.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) entered a final summary judgment in favor of appellee insurer on grounds that the statute of repose for fraud claims, as described in Fla. Stat. § 95.031, barred said claims filed by appellants, a husband and wife. The husband and wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife alleged that the trial court's failure to apply a delayed manifestation exception to the fraud statute of repose resulted in an unconstitutional denial of access to the courts. The appeals court disagreed. Although the Legislature, through Fla. Stat. § 95.031(2)(a), foreclosed the now stale fraud claim, it provided the husband and wife with a reasonable alternative remedy under Fla. Stat. §§ 95.031(2)(c) and (d). In light of this reasonable alternative remedy, the Kluger factors were satisfied. Second, the public necessity that justified cutting off a stale fraud claim which manifested before expiration of the statute of repose was equally applicable to the instant late manifesting claim, as such was the type of claim which was most susceptible to concerns of stale memories, and most deserving of the observation that a defendant ought not to be called on to defend a claim when the evidence has been lost, memories have faded, and witnesses have disappeared.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Clearview Imaging, L.L.C. v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


Case No. 2D05-491


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


932 So. 2d 423; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5757; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1120



April 21, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 8, 2006.
Review denied by State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Clearview Imaging, L.L.C., 2007 Fla. LEXIS 536 (Fla., Mar. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Perry A. Little, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) dismissed the second amended complaint filed by appellant medical service provider (provider) against appellee insurer seeking the balance it was owed for services it provided to the insurer's insured, pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 627.736(5)(b)(5) (2002). The provider appealed.


OVERVIEW: The provider challenged the judgment entered. The appeals court noted that shortly after the provider filed its original complaint, the Florida Legislature amended Fla. Stat. § 627.736(5)(b)(5) so that the annual adjustment described therein involving the Florida Consumer Price Index would occur on August 1, and be based on the annual Medical Care Item of the Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers in the South Region as determined by the Bureau of Labor Statistics of the United States Department of Labor. Borrowing from a decision in the Third District, the appeals court adopted the holding in that case, and reasoned that the statutory amendment fit within that category of amendments that could serve as legislative interpretation of the original law rather than a substantive change thereof. In other words, the amendment clarified the original legislative intent, which was that the Consumer Price Index to be applied was the Medical Care Item of the Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers in the South Region. Thus, in light of this, reversal of the trial court's order was warranted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Notami Hosp. of Fla. v. Bowen


CASE NO. 1D05-4149


DISTRICT COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


927 So. 2d 139; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5760; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1110



April 21, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 9, 2006.
Later proceeding at Fla. Hosp. v. Buster, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 137 (Fla., Jan. 23, 2007)
Approved by, Sub nomine at Fla. Hosp. Waterman, Inc. v. Buster, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 371 (Fla., Mar. 6, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Certiorari is DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After ruling that Fla. Const. amend. VII, codified as Fla. Const. art. X. § 25, was self-executing, and that Fla. Stat. § 381.028 (2005), enacted to implement art. X, § 25, was unconstitutional, a Florida trial court ruled that respondent, a personal representative, a doctor, and a clinic could access previously confidential peer review, risk management, and credentialing documents. Petitioner hospital then sought a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that: (1) Fla. Stat. § 381.028 restricted rights granted under the Florida Constitution and, consequently, was unconstitutional; (2) Fla. Const. amend. VII was not unconstitutionally retrospective because there was no vested right in maintaining confidentiality of adverse medical incidents; and (3) the amendment was self-executing and prospective in operation, but retrospective as to extant records. On appeal, the court held that because § 381.028 drastically limited or eliminated discovery of records the amendment expressly allowed, and limited a patients qualified to access those records, it was unconstitutional. Second, the statute provided that Fla. Const. amend. VII had no effect on existing privilege statutes, which was contrary to the stated purpose of the amendment. Further, because the hospital's expectation that previously existing statutory law would not change was not a vested, substantive right, applying the amendment to records created prior to its passage was not unconstitutionally retrospective, especially when the amendment expressed a clear intent that it be applied to include records created prior to its effective date.


OUTCOME: Certiorari was denied and a conflict was certified with a decision in the Fifth District.

Smith v. State


No. 4D04-3709


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


925 So. 2d 465; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5325; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1053

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County, (Florida) that convicted him of possession of cocaine and drug paraphernalia; defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress drugs and paraphernalia found when the police officer searched him.


OVERVIEW: Upon being dispatched to a certain address, a deputy heard screaming and yelling and saw defendant swinging a mop stick at another individual. The deputy never saw defendant actually hit the other man with the stick; however, defendant was close enough to the other man so that he could have hit him. When defendant ultimately let go of the stick, the deputy placed him in handcuffs and patted him down. Upon feeling a pipe in defendant's pocket that he believed it was a hitter pipe, the deputy reached into the pocket and seized the pipe and a package of cocaine. The appellate court found that defendant's earlier possession of the stick, which he was using as a club, provided the deputy with the necessary reasonable suspicion to conduct a weapons pat-down under the Fourth Amendment and Fla. Stat. § 901.151(5).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Martinez v. Rodriguez


CASE NO. 3D04-1560 & 3D04-662


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


927 So. 2d 93; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5361; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1042



April 12, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 28, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Joel H. Brown, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 98-19738.
Martinez v. Rodriguez, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 3602 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Mar. 15, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee mother petitioned for modification of child support. In consolidated appeals, appellant father challenged orders of the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) that denied his motions to vacate an order that adopted a hearing officer's recommendation recalculating support and a final judgment awarding attorney's fees and costs to the mother. The opinion was substituted for a withdrawn previous opinion on the court's own motion.


OVERVIEW: On the mother's modification petition, the hearing officer recommended that the father pay 81% of the child's support and tuition, found that he could provide health insurance at no cost, and set the amount of the mother's attorney's fees and costs. The trial court ratified and approved the order. On the father's first motion to vacate, the trial court denied his objections to the hearing officer's jurisdiction to consider attorney's fees and the findings on insurance and tuition but remanded the case to credit the father with another child's support. The father appealed from the trial court's order denying his second motion to vacate on the attorney's fees issue and from an order denying his third such motion, in which he argued that Fla. Fam. L.R.P. 12.491 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed both orders. Only the father's claim that the hearing officer lacked jurisdiction to consider attorney's fees because the father did not consent to the referral was properly before the court. He waived that objection by failing to raise it at the hearing. Claims related to health insurance, tuition, and guideline departures did not relate to the orders on appeal and were not considered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court orders.

State v. Sachs

1650 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bjorkland


Case No. 2D06-47


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


924 So. 2d 971; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5068; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 1017



April 7, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 28, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari or Mandamus to the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Robert B. Bennett, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of certiorari or mandamus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants in driving under the influence cases sought to obtain "source codes" used in a breath test instrument. A county court authorized supplemental discovery concerning the codes. The State filed a petition for a writ of certiorari. The Circuit Court for Sarasota County (Florida) dismissed the petition on the ground that it was actually an untimely appeal. The State sought a writ of certiorari or mandamus directed to the circuit court.


OVERVIEW: Fla. Stat. § 924.07(1)(h) authorized the State to appeal from pretrial orders. The court stated that under Fla. Const. art. V, § 4(b), the statute in the context of appeals from circuit courts to district courts had been held to be an unconstitutional legislative intrusion into the supreme court's rule-making authority. This was probably why the State had not acted under it. The circuit courts, however, obtained their appellate jurisdiction from Fla. Const. art. V, § 5(b), and only the legislature could authorize circuit court jurisdiction over nonfinal orders entered in county courts. Thus, in the context of appeals from county court to circuit court, Fla. Stat. § 924.07(1)(h) was essential to give the circuit court jurisdiction, and the State should have appealed under the statute. As an appeal had to be filed within 15 days under Fla. R. App. P. 9.140(c)(3), the circuit court could not have treated the petition for certiorari as an appeal because an appeal would have been untimely. Next, the court rejected the State's argument that it could seek review either through appeal or certiorari. Certiorari was not intended to provide review when an error could be repaired on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for writ of certiorari or mandamus.

 

1651 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rothauser


Case No. 2D04-5515


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


934 So. 2d 17; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 4914; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 973



April 5, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 22, 2006.
Rehearing denied by State v. Rothauser, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 13158 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., June 6, 2006)
Review denied by Rothauser v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 66 (Fla., Jan. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Roger Allan Alcott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) dismissed the information which charged defendant with driving while his license was permanently revoked, in violation of Fla. Stat. § 322.341 (2004), on grounds that the statute was unconstitutional as a result of a single subject violation that occurred in the process of its enactment. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State challenged the judgment entered, claiming error. The appeals court held that although the trial court would have been correct had the issue arisen in Illinois, Florida followed the codification rule under which a single subject violation during the enactment of a law was cured by the legislature's later act of adopting the law as an official statute that was published in the Florida Statutes. Because defendant allegedly violated Fla. Stat. § 322.342 after it had become an official statute, the appeals court had to reverse the trial court's ruling and reinstate the information.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Hadi v. Liberty Behavioral Health Corp.


CASE NO. 1D05-3264, CASE NO. 1D05-4663


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


927 So. 2d 34; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 4385; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 912



March 29, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 22, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Hadi v. Liberty Behavioral Health Corp., 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 8443 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., May 4, 2006)
Review denied by Liberty Behavioral Health Corp. v. Hadi, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2901 (Fla., Dec. 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County, Judge L. Ralph Smith. (1D 05-3264). An appeal from an order of the Department of Children & Families. (1D 05-4663).



DISPOSITION: The order granting the temporary injunction in the first appeal is REVERSED, and DCF's order denying Liberty a formal hearing in the second appeal is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Leon County Circuit Court (Florida) temporarily enjoined appellee, the Department of Children and Families (Department), from enforcing a requirement that appellant contractor post a protest bond prior to challenging the Department's construction specifications. The Department also conducted an informal hearing to resolve the dispute arising from the contractor's challenge to two specifications. Appeals from each order were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: In the first appeal, the contractor sought to uphold the injunction issued against the Department, arguing that an amendment to Fla. Stat. § 287.042(2)(c) (2002), removing the option of posting a $ 5,000.00 bond prior to challenging a bid specification, but continuing the 1 percent bond requirement, was unconstitutional. In the second appeal, the contractor challenged the Department's decision to conduct an informal rather than a formal hearing, to resolve the dispute arising from the contractor contesting two of the Department's specifications as arbitrary and capricious. The appeals court found no merit to either argument. Instead of posting the statutorily required bond, the contractor filed a declaratory judgment action and a motion seeking a temporary injunction, and the temporary injunction was facially deficient. As to the decision to conduct an informal hearing, the contractor's failure to cite with specificity any material facts in dispute, meant that the Department did not abuse its discretion by refusing to refer the matter to the Division of Administrative Hearings, and by proceeding informally pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 120.57(2) (2005).


OUTCOME: The order granting the temporary injunction in the first appeal was reversed, while the Department's order denying the contractor a formal hearing in the second appeal was affirmed.

Jarrett v. State


Case No. 2D04-5223


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


926 So. 2d 429; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 4240; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 893



March 24, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Motion granted by Jarret v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1370 (Fla., June 13, 2006)
Rehearing denied by Jarret v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2344 (Fla., Sept. 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; R. Timothy Peters, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) denied his motion to suppress and motion for rehearing, defendant pleaded to the charges, reserving his right to appeal the denial of the motion to suppress. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding in the Town of Redington Shores by a police officer who was employed by the Town of Indian Shores. The officer was on patrol in Redington Shores because the town had entered into an agreement by which Indian Shores was providing it with law enforcement services. Defendant argued that, absent an underlying statute, Indian Shores could not exert extra-territorial jurisdiction over Redington Shores by agreeing to have its officers provide law enforcement services for Redington Shores. The appellate court found that defendant's legal allegation was sufficient to confer standing to bring his motion to suppress. However, his challenge to the agreement was not grounded on a Fourth Amendment violation by the officer but rather was aimed at the actions of the municipal governments in allegedly failing to follow the statutory procedures applicable to the execution of interlocal agreements. No police misconduct was alleged. Thus, application of the exclusionary rule was not justified. The agreement between the two towns conferred at least de facto status on the officer who stopped defendant notwithstanding any alleged procedural infirmity in the agreement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Butler v. State


No. 4D03-3095


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


923 So. 2d 566; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 4060; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 845



March 22, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 7, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Lucy Chernow Brown, Judge; L.T. Case No. 02-886 CFA02.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pled guilty to sexual battery on a person less than 12 years of age by a person 18 years of age or older, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which denied his motion to declare Fla. Stat. § 775.21 (2002) unconstitutional after the State moved to declare him a sexual predator.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued there was a substantive due process violation because § 775.21 placed an unreasonable burden on his liberty interests without affording him the opportunity to disprove his dangerousness and it established an irrebuttable presumption that certain offenders were to be designated as "sexual predators" without providing an opportunity to disprove dangerousness. He asserted, inter alia, that the statute would affect his liberty interests by limiting his right to move and travel. The appellate court held the relevant affected right was his right to be free from registration requirements. Defendant did not argue that the rights he was asserting were fundamental and deeply rooted in Florida's legal tradition. Thus, because no claim of infringement of a fundamental right was alleged, the reasonable basis analysis of the irrebuttable presumption was the appropriate test to apply. The statute met that test. The sexual predator designation provisions of the Florida Sexual Predator Act challenged by defendant were constitutional as there was no violation of the right to travel and the legislative determination of an irrebuttable presumption was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Behm v. Campbell


Case No. 5D05-2200


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


925 So. 2d 1070; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 3453; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 752



March 10, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 29, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Putnam County, A.W. Nichols, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an arrestee and his wife, sued defendants, a sheriff and deputies, alleging battery, false arrest and imprisonment, and trespass. The Circuit Court for Putnam County (Florida) granted summary judgment to defendants. Plaintiffs appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The police followed the arrestee to his home, believing that he might have been involved in a shooting. The arrestee told the deputies that they were trespassing, and attempted to go to his house. When the deputies stopped him, the arrestee tried to hit a deputy, and the deputies forced him to the ground and pepper sprayed him. The arrestee pled no contest to resisting arrest without violence, Fla. Stat. § 843.02, and adjudication of guilt was withheld. The appellate court held that under Florida law, the arrestee's no contest plea constituted a conviction even though adjudication of guilt was withheld. A judgment of conviction was conclusive evidence of probable cause, unless the judgment was obtained by fraud, perjury, or other corrupt means. Here there was no evidence or even an allegation that the guilty plea was obtained by any corrupt means. Thus, the conviction established probable cause for the arrest. Because all the claims against the deputies were related to the lawfulness of the arrest, the appellate court held that all of the claims were precluded by defendant's guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Guetzloe v. Fla. Elections Comm'n


CASE NO. 5D05-4


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


927 So. 2d 942; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 3474; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 757



March 10, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 19, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Guetzloe v. Fla. Elections Comm'n, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 8696 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., May 2, 2006)
Review denied by Fla. Elections Comm'n v. Guetzloe, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2099 (Fla., Sept. 12, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Administrative Appeal from the Florida Elections Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Florida Elections Commission (Commission), found that appellant advertiser violated Florida's campaign finance laws by failing to include disclaimers in, and report expenditures for, certain independent political advertisements. The advertiser appealed.


OVERVIEW: The advertiser first contended that the Commission erred in finding him guilty of violating provisions of Fla. Stat. § 106.071(1) that required advertisements to display the name and address of the person who paid for the advertisements because those provisions were unconstitutional. The appeals court agreed, given the holding by the Florida Supreme Court in Doe stating that in order to comport with the First Amendment, the last sentence in § 106.071(1) had to be truncated to read: Any political advertisement paid for by an independent expenditure shall prominently state "Paid political advertisement." The Supreme Court did not intend to strike the identification requirement in § 106.071(1) as it applied to individuals using modest resources, as such an interpretation would raise significant questions as to whom the truncated part of the statute applied. However, the Commission correctly found that the advertiser violated Fla. Stat. § 106.143(4)(b) by failing to disclose that no candidate approved of the advertisement. Finally, the question of whether the advertiser acted willfully, as a question of fact, required an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: That part of the order finding a violation of the statute requiring advertisements to display the name and address of the person who paid for said advertisements was reversed, but that part of the order finding a violation of the statute requiring that the identity of the advertisement's sponsor was affirmed.

Zeigler v. State


CASE NO. 1D05-314, CASE NO. 1D05-315


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


922 So. 2d 384; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 3206; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 706



March 7, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 23, 2006.
Review granted by Zeigler v. State, 935 So. 2d 500, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1752 (Fla., 2006)
Review improvidently allowed by Zeigler v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 576 (Fla., Apr. 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from a final order from the circuit court for Columbia County. Paul S. Bryan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Columbia County (Florida) denied both defendants' motions to suppress contraband seized after an officer smelled the odor of burnt marijuana coming from the vehicle being operated by the first defendant and occupied by the second. Both defendants appealed, and their appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants argued that the seized contraband should have been suppressed because the officer was not allowed to ask for their identification once it was established that the license tag was properly displayed. However, though a continued detention of a driver was improper once the officer fully satisfied the purpose for the initiated stop, that officer could lawfully make personal contact with the driver to explain the reason for said stop. As a result, the officer, in informing the driver his reason for the stop, had the legal authority to make personal contact with defendants and be in a position to smell the marijuana. Once the officer smelled the marijuana, he was entitled to detain both defendants. Moreover, even if the officer had immediately explained the reason for the stop when he made personal contact with defendants, rather than first asking them for their identification, he would have still smelled marijuana and thus developed probable cause to detain them. Finally, the officer was not constitutionally required to make personal contact through a closed vehicle window.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1658 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Peachtree Cas. Ins. Co. v. Prof'l Massage Servs.


CASE NO. 1D05-2145


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


923 So. 2d 548; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 3210; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 708



March 7, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 23, 2006.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurer brought a petition against respondent healthcare provider, seeking certiorari review of a circuit court ruling which affirmed a county court's summary judgment. The county court had ruled in favor of the healthcare provider in its claims seeking payment pursuant to former Fla. Stat. § 627.736(5)(b) (1998) for treatment rendered to the insurer's insured.


OVERVIEW: The insured patient was covered by a policy issued by the insurer. When the patient sought treatment, she incorrectly gave the name of a different insurance company to the healthcare provider. The healthcare provider timely billed that other insurance company, instead of the insurer, for the services. When the healthcare provider discovered the error, and billed the insurer, the insurer denied the claims as untimely. The lower courts found that allowing the healthcare provider to recover did not frustrate the legislature's purpose behind former Fla. Stat. § 627.736(5)(b) (1998), was consistent with a 2001 amendment to that statute, and was equitable. In ruling on the certiorari petition, the court found that § 627.736(5)(b) (1998) required claims to be billed to the insurer, and it was improper for the circuit court to apply the exception to the claims initially submitted to the wrong insurance company. The circuit court also departed from the essential requirements of law by affirming the county court's consideration of the 2001 amendment. Former Fla. Stat. § 627.736(5)(b) (1998) was unambiguous, so the lower courts were without power to diverge from its plain language.


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of certiorari was granted, the circuit court's order was quashed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Sorrentino v. River Run Condo. Ass'n


Case No. 5D05-836


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


925 So. 2d 1060; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 2992; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 679



March 3, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 5, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Sorrentino v. River Run Condo. Ass'n, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 7506 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Apr. 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hernando County, Richard Tombrink, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED in part; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant condominium association filed suit against appellee residents, alleging they breached the condominium declaration and seeking an injunction to have the skylights removed. The residents counterclaimed and sought an injunction preventing the removal of the skylights. The Circuit Court for Hernando County, rendered judgment in the residents' favor but denied them attorney's fees. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the residents argued that they were entitled to a reasonable attorney's fee award as the prevailing party, and that the trial court breached its discretion in failing to make an award pursuant to Fla. Stat. §§ 718.303, 163.04(3), as well as provisions of the condominium declaration. The appellate court found that the association stipulated that the skylights were protected by § 163.04, and they had been properly installed; thus, it followed that the association could not have forbidden permission to install the skylights and that although the residents should not have installed them without prior written permission, no damage was done. As the residents obtained the result they sought (to prevent the association from requiring removal of the skylights), while the association did not obtain the results it was seeking (removal of the skylights), there was no valid legal reason to deny the residents a prevailing party attorney fee award.


OUTCOME: That part of the judgment denying the residents an attorney fee award was reversed and remanded to the trial court to determine a reasonable attorney fee and costs, to be assessed against the association.

State v. Subido


Case Nos. 5D04-3922; 5D04-4228


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


925 So. 2d 1052; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 3014; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 684



March 3, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Subido, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 7227 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Apr. 12, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Seminole County, Kenneth R. Lester, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Seminole County, Florida, convicted defendant of sexual battery while he was in a position of familial authority and while his stepdaughter was asleep, committing a first-degree felony in violation of Fla. Stat. §§ 794.011(4)(a), (8)(b) (2003). Defendant was sentenced to two years' community control and nine years' probation. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State contended the reasons set forth by the trial court as the basis for defendant's downward departure sentence were not legally invalid and not supported by the evidence. The appellate court agreed, finding that the record did not support the trial court's finding that the offense was committed in an unsophisticated manner: defendant waited for the victim to fall asleep, then, in a stealth-like manner, crept into the bed alongside her and proceeded to commit sexual battery upon her. He went through several distinctive and deliberative steps in order to commit the sexual battery, including walking upstairs, opening and closing his stepdaughter's door, getting on the bed with her, and moving his hands under the bedcovers. These steps were further evidence that this crime was not committed in an unsophisticated manner. Defendant's alleged inebriation during the incident did not justify the downward departure sentence as such a reason contravened the language of Fla. Stat. § 921.0026(3), which forbid the use of intoxication to justify a downward departure. Nor did the law support downward departure merely for committing an offense less heinously than other defendants.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and designation as a sexual predator were affirmed; defendant's sentence was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing.

Perkowski v. State


No. 4D05-217


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


920 So. 2d 836; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 2234; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 581



February 22, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert B. Carney, Judge; L.T. Case No. 89-8952 CF10A.
Perkowski v. State, 616 So. 2d 26, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 500 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a final order entered by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which reimposed his sentence based upon his 1991 convictions for two counts of armed kidnapping, two counts of robbery with a firearm, and one count of armed burglary. Those crimes were committed in 1988.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his habitual violent felony offender sentence, claimed he was erroneously denied jail credit for time he spent in prison out of state, and argued that a scoresheet error was made based on the inclusion of points for convictions for crimes committed after the offenses at issue. On direct appeal, defendant had raised the issue of the legality of his habitual violent felony offender sentence, and the court affirmed; thus, the law of the case applied. While defendant asserted that he was entitled to credit for time spent in custody in Pennsylvania after he was first sentenced for the offenses at issue, the court held that the term "county jail" as used in Fla. Stat. § 921.161(1) (1987) only referred to Florida jails and was not applicable to obtain credit while a defendant was incarcerated in another state on unrelated charges. However, the court agreed that a scoresheet error occurred as the plain language of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.701(d)(5) indicated that a sentencing court could not score as a prior conviction an offense which was committed after the primary offense; thus, the use of defendant's 1990 convictions for offenses committed in Pennsylvania was improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as to the legality of defendant's habitual violent felony offender sentence and the denial of sentencing credit. The court reversed defendant's sentence on counts I and II based on the scoresheet error and remanded with directions to impose a sentence based upon a corrected scoresheet without points from convictions for offenses occurring after the offenses at issue in the instant case.

Thompson v. Napotnik


Case No. 5D05-434


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


923 So. 2d 537; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 1642; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 431



February 10, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Thompson v. Napotnik, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5843 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Mar. 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Donald E. Grincewicz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commissioner sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), which entered judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendants, the chairperson of a recall committee and a city clerk, in an action challenging the adequacy of a recall petition pursuant to Fla. Stat. § 100.361(1)(a), (b) (2005).


OVERVIEW: The chairperson filed a petition seeking the commissioner's recall from office. The city clerk delivered the petition to the commissioner. The petition alleged that the commissioner violated provisions of Florida's Sunshine Law by engaging in an unauthorized meeting with other city commissioners regarding the closing of a local trailer park, thereby committing malfeasance in office. The commissioner brought an action against defendants, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. The commissioner alleged that the recall petition failed to set forth facts that, if true, would demonstrate malfeasance in office. The trial court entered judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendants. On appeal, the court found that compliance with Florida's Sunshine Law was required by all elected officials. Thus, the commissioner's failure to so comply would be unlawful. As such, the trial court properly concluded that the petition adequately alleged a claim of malfeasance.

Tolbert v. State


Case No. 5D04-2785


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


922 So. 2d 1013; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 1644; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 432



February 10, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Tolbert v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5376 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Mar. 16, 2006)
Review denied by Tolbert v. State, 934 So. 2d 451, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1428 (Fla., 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Tolbert v. State, 2011 Fla. App. LEXIS 6422 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Apr. 26, 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Dismissed by Tolbert v. Sec'y, Dep't of Corr., 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 6540 (M.D. Fla., Jan. 16, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Bob Wattles, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of, inter alia, home invasion robbery with a firearm, kidnapping with intent to commit a felony with a firearm, and aggravated battery causing great bodily harm by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida). Defendant argued that erroneous jury instructions entitled him to a new trial. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred in allowing testimony of his drug sales to be presented to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a codefendant, and a third individual entered a home at gunpoint, battered the residents, and stole a safe. Defendant was eventually identified as one of the robbers. The police proceeded to his home where they found the contents of the safe located in the attic above defendant's bedroom. Defendant argued that insertion of "and/or" between his name and the name of the codefendant in the jury instructions allowed the jury to wrongfully convict him for the criminal conduct of codefendant. The appellate court held that because the codefendant was acquitted, the fundamental instructional error rule did not apply. Defendant never obtained a ruling from the trial court regarding his motion in limine. Therefore, the evidentiary issue was not preserved under Fla. Stat. § 90.104(1) (2003). Accordingly, his failure to do so, along with his failure to timely object at the time the testimony concerning his drug sales was introduced, effectively waived his objection and the appellate court could not review any claimed error resulting from admission of that testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1666 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Pass v. State


Case No. 2D04-4522


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


922 So. 2d 279; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 1683; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 448



February 10, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 3, 2006.  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Pass v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5278 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Mar. 16, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Pass v. McDonough, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33281 (M.D. Fla., May 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Daniel Perry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an inmate, appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief (PCR) pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The inmate had been convicted of felony DUI, driving while his license was permanently revoked, and carrying a concealed weapon by a convicted felon.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was charged with, inter alia, driving while his license was permanently revoked, in violation of Fla. Stat. § 322.341 (2001). He entered an open plea of guilt and he was sentenced to concurrent terms of imprisonment. Thereafter, the inmate filed his motion for PCR, which was denied by the trial court. On appeal, the court held that the inmate's convictions and sentences on those charges should have been vacated because § 322.341 was unconstitutional at the time of the alleged offenses. As the inmate was convicted of a nonexistent crime due to violation of the single subject rule of 1998 Fla. Laws 223, within which Fla. Stat. § 322.341 was created, he was entitled to vacatur of those convictions and sentences. The issue of whether the inmate's counsel was ineffective in pursuing a trial strategy of not raising a Critchfield argument was irrelevant because the inmate was entitled to relief. However, as the inmate entered an "open plea" and had no agreement with the State, there was no basis to set aside the plea in its entirety. The other charges and convictions were valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court with respect to denial of the inmate's PCR motion as to all charges except the driving with a revoked license convictions. As to those convictions, the court reversed the trial court decision. The matter was remanded for the vacatur of the revoked license convictions and sentences.

Cranney v. Coronado


Case No. 2D04-2609


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


920 So. 2d 132; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 1094; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 337



February 1, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 17, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Ralph C. Stoddard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of certiorari is granted. Trial court's orders is quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After petitioner father's ex-wife died, he obtained custody of his children and sought an injunction to prohibit respondent grandmother from visitation with them; the grandmother filed a counterpetition seeking termination of the father's parental rights. The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County, Florida, ordered the parties to meet with its appointed parental coordinator to resolve the visitation issues. The father sought certiorari review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the father argued that the trial court's orders violated his constitutional right to privacy under Fla. Const. art. I, § 23. The appellate court agreed, finding first that there was no facially constitutional statutory provision authorizing the granting of visitation to the grandmother. In the absence of a constitutionally valid basis for an order concerning grandparent visitation, the trial court's orders appointing the parental coordinator and requiring the father to meet and consult with the coordinator concerning visitation subjected him to an unwarranted inquiry into his private decision-making process concerning the best interests of his children. Furthermore, the trial court made no finding that the children would suffer harm as a result of the absence of grandparent visitation and no evidence was presented to support such a finding. The appellate court concluded that the trial court's orders designed to facilitate grandparent visitation over the father's objection manifestly violated his fundamental right as a parent to raise his children.


OUTCOME: The petition for certiorari was granted and the trial court's orders regarding the parenting coordinator were quashed.

City of Pompano Beach v. Forman


No. 4D04-3737


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


919 So. 2d 692; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 1157; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 357



February 1, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Dorian K. Damoorgian, Judge; L.T. Case No. 04-10305 (12).



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cities brought an action for declaratory relief in which they argued that Fla. Stat. §§ 28.2402 and 34.045 were unconstitutional in view of Fla. Const. art. V, § 14. The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), found the statutes constitutional. The cities appealed.


OVERVIEW: The statutes required the cities to pay nominal filing fees to the clerks of court when prosecuting local ordinance violations through the court system. The cities argued that such payments amounted to "funding" for the clerks of court and were prohibited by Fla. Const. art. V, § 14. The appellate court found that the use of the term "funding" within the language of Fla. Const. art. V, § 14 was ambiguous with regard to the cities' exemption or exclusion from the payment of filing fees, and the trial court erred in not considering extrinsic evidence regarding legislative history and background of the constitutional amendment to aid in interpretation. Based on the trial court's pronouncement at the hearing that there was no ambiguity and that extrinsic evidence would not be considered, the cities did not present extrinsic evidence concerning intent. The appellate court concluded that they should be given the opportunity to do so.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

Cox v. Crosby


CASE NO. 1D05-3857


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


27 So. 3d 45; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 832; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 310



January 26, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Review granted by McDonough v. Cox, 924 So. 2d 809, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 489 (Fla., 2006)
Certified question answered by, Approved by McNeil v. Cox, 997 So. 2d 343, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2320 (Fla., 2008)
Subsequent appeal at Cox v. McNeil, 6 So. 3d 55, 2009 Fla. App. LEXIS 3127 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Apr. 1, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Leon County. Janet E. Ferris, Judge.
Cox v. State, 737 So. 2d 1080, 1999 Fla. App. LEXIS 5062 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR REVIEW GRANTED; ORDER REVERSED; and QUESTION CERTIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) that found him to be an indigent appellant and therefore, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 57.085, imposed a lien on his inmate trust account to cover the costs of filing an appeal from an underlying order upholding the constitutionality of a method by which respondent corrections department calculated his gain time.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's underlying petition challenged the manner in which his gain time was calculated. He claimed that the calculation had deprived him of five years of potential freedom. When he appealed the denial of his petition, the trial court imposed a lien on his inmate account to cover the fees for filing his appeal. The court held that under a rule announced by the state supreme court in its Schmidt decision, a petition that involved the length of an inmate's incarceration was a collateral criminal proceeding within the meaning of Fla. Stat. ch. 57.081, and in such a proceeding, a lien could not be imposed on an inmate's trust account. Since such an application of Schmidt could potentially affect many inmate proceedings, the court certified a question to the supreme court, inquiring as to whether it had actually intended Schmidt to apply this broadly.


OUTCOME: The court granted the inmate's motion for review, and reversed the order that imposed the lien. The court certified a question of great public importance to the state's highest court, asking whether this result was what that court had intended.

Wakeman v. Dixon


CASE NO. 1D05-0103


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


921 So. 2d 669; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 659; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 263



January 24, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 16, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Wakeman v. Dixon, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 4327 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Feb. 28, 2006)
Review denied by Wakeman v. Dixon, 931 So. 2d 902, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 973 (Fla., May 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Terry P. Lewis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Leon County Circuit Court (Florida) entered a final judgment that dismissed with prejudice appellant first domestic partner's amended complaint seeking to enforce several agreements with appellee second domestic partner under which the first domestic partner argued she was granted certain parental rights and responsibilities regarding two minor children born to the second domestic partner. The first domestic partner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first domestic partner and the second domestic partner began to live together. Thereafter, they jointly entered into a sperm donation agreement with the sperm donor. As a result, the second domestic partner became pregnant. After the birth of the child, they entered into another agreement known as a "co-parenting agreement." Pursuant to an amended sperm donation agreement, the second domestic partner became pregnant with a second child. The parties then executed a "co-parenting agreement" regarding the second child. A few years later, the parties ceased residing together. The first domestic partner sought what was essentially a declaration of parental rights to the two children born to the second domestic partner, based on the agreements. The trial court granted the second domestic partner's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the appellate court found that under Florida law and absent evidence of detriment to a child, courts did not have any authority to grant custody or compel visitation by a person who was not a natural parent and that agreements providing for visitation by a non-parent, such as the first domestic partner, were unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Gargano v. Lee County Bd. of County Comm'rs


Case No. 2D04-4799


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


921 So. 2d 661; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 468; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 250



January 20, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 22, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lee County; R. Thomas Corbin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent herewith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county resident sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida), which dismissed her third amended complaint with prejudice against appellee county board of county commissioners. The resident sought damages and injunctive relief, based on her claim that a bridge toll was an unconstitutional tax and was unreasonable, and that the disrepair of the bridge resulted in increased garbage fees.


OVERVIEW: The basis for the complaint was that the county had failed to adequately maintain the bridge despite receiving ample bridge toll revenue for that purpose. The trial court dismissed the action, finding that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction, that the resident lacked standing, and that the complaint failed to state a cause of action. On appeal, the court held that the trial court had limited subject matter jurisdiction over the action pursuant to Fla. Const. art. V, § 20(i) and Fla. Stat. ch. 26.012(2)(e) (2004). Further, as a county resident who alleged a special injury, there was standing to assert the claims regarding reasonableness of the toll, but no standing to challenge the underlying political decisions. The complaint was disorganized and deficient, but it was not incapable of amendment to state a valid claim. The resident had no entitlement to an order requiring the county to improve the maintenance to the bridge, to claim damages from a garbage surcharge, or to seek refunds for previously paid tolls. However, she could attempt to obtain a prospective injunction as to future tolls. The court determined that the toll was a user fee, rather than a tax.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of dismissal of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings, including an opportunity to amend the complaint.

Palm Beach Polo, Inc. v. Vill. of Wellington


No. 4D04-2839


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


918 So. 2d 988; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 385; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 202



January 18, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Palm Beach Polo, Inc. v. Vill. of Wellington, 929 So. 2d 1053, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 780 (Fla., Apr. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Catherine M. Brunson, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-3914 AH.
Palm Beach Polo, Inc. v. Vill. of Wellington, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18573 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Nov. 23, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), granted an injunction against appellant developer finding that, pursuant to a planned unit development (PUD) with the developer's predecessor in title, it was obligated to restore, enhance, and preserve an area known as the Big Blue Reserve. Thus, it rejected the developer's taking claims. The developer appealed.


OVERVIEW: Upon the developer's challenge, the court first rejected its claim that it was entitled to compensation under the Bert J. Harris Act, Fla. Stat. § 70.001, as there was no reasonable, investment-backed expectation for an existing use of the Big Blue reserve. From 1972 forward, it was designated as a natural reserve and extraordinary efforts were made to preserve this important pristine forest. At the time the developer purchased the surrounding property, Big Blue was designated as a nature reserve, and the town's redesignation of it as a "conservation area" in its comprehensive plan changed nothing regarding the property. Second, the PUD was not unconstitutionally applied to the Big Blue property, was not overly broad and vague, and defined critical and technical terms used therein. Further, the trial court was correct in deferring to the agency's interpretation of its zoning code. Finally, the court rejected the developer's takings claim, although the Big Blue property would be flooded and thus unusable for development, as that was precisely the condition of the property that the developer's predecessors agreed to in exchange for developing other property with higher densities.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lakeland Reg'l Med. Ctr., Inc. v. Agency for Health Care Admin.


CASE NO. 1D04-5585


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


917 So. 2d 1024; 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 38; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 141



January 6, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 23, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Honorable P. Kevin Davey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical center, which had previously been the only hospital with an open heart surgery program in a county, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which found Fla. Stat. § 408.039a was constitutional and thus, had the effect of granting appellee hospital a license to also perform open heart surgery. The medical center argued a grandfather clause violated procedural due process and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The hospital's application for a certificate of need (CON) to establish an open heart surgery program in the same service district as the medical center was approved. The Florida Legislature amended Fla. Stat. §§ 408.036 and 408.0361 to create a new licensure scheme for adult interventional cardiology services with 2004 Fla. Laws ch. 383, §§ 6, 7 at 2922-36. The legislature added a licensure grandfather clause applicable to the hospital's application. The appellate court held that appellee Agency for Health Care Administration's interpretation was not clearly erroneous and did not conflict with the intent of Fla. Stat. § 408.0361(3)(a), as amended, was entitled to great deference. Accordingly, adult interventional cardiology services included open heart surgery. There was no due process violation because the medical center had no constitutionally protected property right in pursuing its non-final administrative hearing challenge to the hospital's CON application after the enactment of the grandfather amendment. The medical center had only a mere expectation of a continuing right under the statute. There was no equal protection violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Rubio


Case No. 5D05-846


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


917 So. 2d 383; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 20575; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 108



December 30, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 19, 2006.
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Rubio, 967 So. 2d 768, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1248 (Fla., 2007)
Opinion withdrawn by, On remand at, Remanded by State v. Rubio, 2007 Fla. App. LEXIS 19613 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Dec. 5, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) which dismissed most of the charges against defendant dentists and struck the predicate incidents used by the State to support the remaining charges. In so doing, the trial court declared Florida's patient brokering law, Fla. Stat. § 817.505(1)(b), and the version of Florida's Medicaid provider fraud law, Fla. Stat. § 409.920, applicable to the case unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The State filed an information against defendants and three co-defendants, including racketeering and conspiracy to commit racketeering, Medicaid provider fraud in violation of Fla. Stat. § 409.920(2)(a), patient brokering in violation of Fla. Stat. § 817.505, and with violating the White Collar Crime Victim Protection Act, Fla. Stat. § 775.0844. Two defendants solicited children primarily from public housing areas and transported them to and from the clinic. The dentists billed Medicaid and split the fees. The trial court held that Fla. Stat. § 409.920(2)(a), as written at the time, was preempted by federal law. The appellate court agreed that Congress mandated a knowing and willful standard for Medicaid fraud violations. Thus, the prior definition of "knowingly" in § 409.920(1)(d) rendered it unconstitutional and those counts were properly dismissed. However, Fla. Stat. § 817.505 did not pose the same constitutional concerns as it was not vague and clearly prohibited fees based on the referral of patients. Thus, the trial court erred in declaring it unconstitutional. The multiple charges of patient brokering filed against defendants exceeded the allowable unit of prosecution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed as to the patient brokering charge. It was affirmed as to the remainder of the judgment.

Forbes v. Chapin


No. 4D05-371


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


917 So. 2d 948; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 19966; 31 Fla. L. Weekly D 30



December 21, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 6, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of non-final orders from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Kathleen J. Kroll, Judge; L.T. Case No. 501997DR005611XXCDFB.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), entered two non-final orders, the first of which denied appellant father's exceptions to the general master's report upholding the trial court's 1998 order granting appellee maternal grandmother visitation rights with her minor grandchild. The second order held the father in contempt. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father challenged the judgments entered on constitutional grounds based on his right to privacy, which he contended that he did not waive by signing an agreement allowing the grandmother visitation. At issue was the question of whether a parent's agreement to visitation by a grandparent with the parent's minor child waived the parent's right to later enforce his constitutional privacy right to raise his child free from government intrusion and thus, prevented him from later revoking his agreement for visitation. The court answered this question in the negative. Second, the court declared Fla. Stat. ch. 752.07 unconstitutional. Thus, in the absence of a constitutional statute upon which the court could base its order, it could not order such visitation in favor of a non-parent. Moreover, because the court's granting of visitation rights to a non-parent over the parent's objection was an unenforceable order, the finding that the grandmother was an interested party was erroneous. Thus, the grandmother had no right to notice of the adoption proceedings. For that reason, the order of contempt could not stand and was ordered vacated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for the orders therein to be vacated.

The trial court denied the requested relief. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court erred in issuing the confidentiality order but that the company was not entitled to relief because it invited the error and the Act was constitutional.

Marshall v. State


No. 4D03-2797


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


915 So. 2d 264; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 19615; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2736



December 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 23, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Charles M. Greene, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-003928(12).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Seventeenth Judicial Circuit Court, Broward County (Florida), entered a judgment, based on a jury's finding, that defendant was a sexually-violent predator. The trial court then ordered his civil commitment as such. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant served prison time for a sex crime and was scheduled for release. Before the release date, the State petitioned to civilly commit him. A jury trial revealed his lengthy history of sex crimes. One of the crimes involved defendant's sexual assault of the nine-year-old daughter of a woman. At defendant's civil commitment hearing, the State introduced evidence of the mother's account about what the daughter had told her about the assault. Defendant called the daughter as a witness; she testified that she could not remember what happened. In rebuttal, the State called a clinical psychologist who testified about why the daughter might not remember such an event. The jury determined that defendant was a sexually-violent predator and the trial court ordered him committed as such. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court did not err in admitting victim hearsay statements to establish the factual basis for his underlying sex crimes because the hearsay exception under the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 394.910 et seq. (Act), the trial court did not err in finding the Act to be constitutional, and the clinical psychologist's testimony was properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1679 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kees


Case No. 5D05-589


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


919 So. 2d 504; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18888; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2717



December 2, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Kees, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 2170 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Jan. 27, 2006)
Review denied by Kees v. State, 930 So. 2d 621, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 848 (Fla., May 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Certiorari Review of Decision from the Circuit Court for Seminole County Acting in its Appellate Capacity.



DISPOSITION: Petition GRANTED; Order QUASHED; Case REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State of Florida, sought certiorari review of a decision rendered by the Circuit Court for Seminole County (Florida), acting in its appellate capacity, affirming dismissal by the county court of criminal charges filed against respondent suspects.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that, since the lewd activity at issue occurred in a public place, it was not required to prove that someone was offended by the suspects' conduct in order to establish a prima facie case. The instant court agreed. If the courts required the State to prove that a party other than a law enforcement officer was offended by a defendant's lewd and lascivious conduct when said conduct occurred in a public place, such a ruling would lead to absurd results. Even if the instant court were to have concluded that an element of offensiveness was contained in the statutes at issue, dismissal of the State's charges was unwarranted because, in order for the offensiveness element to be constitutionally valid, an objective reasonable person standard, not a subjective standard, had to be used. The application of a subjective standard would allow an overly sensitive member of the public, or a member of the police force, to object to conduct which was not objectively offensive, thereby exposing a criminal defendant to arbitrary and capricious prosecution. Similarly, potentially criminal conduct could go unpunished if the observer of the conduct was particularly insensitive to it.


OUTCOME: Certiorari was granted, the circuit court's order was quashed, and the matter was remanded for reinstatement of the charges.

K.A.S. v. R.E.T.


Case No. 2D04-4973


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


914 So. 2d 1056; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18762; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2669



November 30, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 30, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lee County; G. Keith Cary, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida) held that it lacked the power to order appellees, the non-parental guardians of the person of a minor ward (maternal grandparents), to permit visitation between the ward and appellant, his paternal grandmother. It also denied motion filed by appellant, the guardian or the property (guardian), for the appointment of a guardian ad litem. The paternal grandmother and the guardian appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented was whether the probate court had the power to order the non-parental guardians of the person of a minor ward to permit visitation between the ward and his paternal grandmother. The appeals court held that it did. The paternal grandmother was not asking the probate court to order the parents to permit her to visit the ward, she was asking the court to compel the maternal grandparents to permit such visitation, who obviously were not the ward's parents. Moreover, the focus of the probate court's analysis should have been on whether such visitation was in the ward's best interests instead of the respective rights of the parties to demand or to withhold visitation. Second, because the probate court incorrectly ruled that it had no power to interfere with the decision of the guardians of the person to deny the paternal grandmother any visitation with the ward, the probate court failed to consider her visitation petition based on the ward's best interests. The court also held that the probate court properly refused to appoint a guardian ad litem, as the petition for appointment was not timely presented.


OUTCOME: The order denying an appointment of a guardian ad litem was affirmed. But, the order prohibiting visitation between the paternal grandmother and the ward was reversed, and the case was remanded on this issue. If it decides to grant the paternal mother visitation, it should do so considering the ward's best interest. If visitation was denied, the paternal grandmother was to be allowed to petition again for visitation if circumstances changed.

 

1681 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Palm Beach Polo, Inc. v. Vill. of Wellington


No. 4D04-2839


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18573; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2660



November 23, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL DISPOSITION OF TIMELY FILED MOTION FOR REHEARING.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Clarified by Palm Beach Polo, Inc. v. Village of Wellington, 918 So. 2d 988, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 385 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Jan. 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Catherine M. Brunson, Judge; L.T. Case No. 01-3914 AH.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), found that appellee village did not engage in an unlawful "as applied" taking in requiring appellant developer to restore, enhance, and preserve an area known as Big Blue Reserve in connection with the 1972 Wellington Planned Unit Development (PUD). The developer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court properly ordered the developer to comply with the PUD Master Plan's restrictions by preserving the Big Blue Reserve (Big Blue) and protecting it from alteration and development activities, to enhance it by removing exotic vegetation, and to preserve and enhance it by increasing the property's water levels by one foot above existing levels. As a result, the developer's claim that a violation of the Bert J. Harris Act (Act) occurred, was frivolous, as it was fairly obvious from the abundant history of Big Blue that there was no reasonable, investment-backed expectation for an existing use of the area at all. Since 1972, it was designated as a natural reserve and extraordinary efforts were made to preserve this important pristine forest. At the time the developer purchased the property it sought to develop, Big Blue was designated as a nature reserve, and its redesignation as a conservation area changed nothing. Second, the PUD master plan was not void for vagueness or overbreadth, as the developer's predecessors-in-title, as well as the regulating agencies, gave specific meanings to the terms used therein, and said meanings were well understood by the parties.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Sarasota Herald-Tribune v. State


Case No. 2D05-5408


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


924 So. 2d 8; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18464; 34 Media L. Rep. 1719; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2637



November 22, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 28, 2005. Released for Publication March 27, 2006.
Question certified by Sarasota Herald-Tribune v. State, 924 So. 2d 17, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18569 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Nov. 23, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari dismissed by Florida v. Sarasota Herald-Tribune, 126 S. Ct. 1139, 163 L. Ed. 2d 943, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 761 (U.S., 2006)
Rehearing denied by Sarasota Herald-Tribune v. State, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 5274 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Jan. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Sarasota County; Andrew D. Owens, Jr., Judge.
Sarasota Herald-Tribune v. State, 916 So. 2d 904, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18215 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Petition is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner media outlets (the media) sought certiorari review of an order entered by the Circuit Court for Sarasota County (Florida) that excluded them from viewing and inspecting crime scene photographs, crime scene videotapes, and autopsy photographs which were admitted into evidence in open court during defendant's criminal trial.


OVERVIEW: The order entered against the media prevented all members of the public from viewing the exhibits at issue. The instant court concluded that the statutes relied upon by the trial court to bar examination of this evidence by the media did not apply to the exhibits at issue, which had been formally introduced into evidence. Instead, the trial court was required to apply the analysis set forth in Fla. R. Jud. Admin. 2.051(c). Under that analysis, the court held that the four members of the media who asked to view the evidence were improperly excluded from viewing it. But, because the media was not seeking to copy or publish that evidence, they were not entitled to do so. Further, the trial court was not required to make this evidence generally available for easy viewing by large numbers of people. Finally, because the photographic evidence had already been viewed by various people in law enforcement, court personnel and lawyers, the criminal trial jury, and presumably by the grand jury, less restrictive measures existed to protect the victim's family while also protecting the competing interests engendered by a public trial.


OUTCOME: The petition for review of the order excluding the media was granted.

Wilson v. State


Case No. 2D05-3440


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


913 So. 2d 1277; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18253; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2627



November 18, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 6, 2005.
Related proceeding at Wilson v. State, 935 So. 2d 11, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 12464 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.141(b)(2) from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; William Fuente, Judge.
Wilson v. State, 902 So. 2d 161, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5793 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to several counts of sexual battery and lewd and lascivious acts and was sentenced. Later, after defendant was released, the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) revoked his probation and imposed further prison terms. Defendant moved to correct sentencing error, but the motion was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sentences were based on a 1994 scoresheet. He argued that his scoresheet was incorrectly calculated at both his original sentencing and at the sentencing on the violation of probation. He claimed that his sexual battery convictions were scored as level 9 offenses when they were actually level 7 offenses. The appellate court held that the sexual battery offense in Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(8)(b) was required to be scored as a level 7 offense. For all relevant times Fla. Stat. ch. 921.0012 required that defendant's sexual battery offenses be scored as level 7 offenses. It was clear that defendant's scoresheet contained a sizable error. Since, however, it was not clear whether defendant's sentence was the result of a plea agreement or the result of an open plea, it was necessary for the trial court to determine what, if any, relief was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the case was remanded for the trial court to calculate a correct scoresheet and then to determine what, if any, relief was appropriate as a result of that scoresheet.
