In re Doe


Case No. 2D05-5321


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


932 So. 2d 278; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 17715; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2575



November 10, 2005, Decided  
November 10, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 10, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Ellen Masters, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) entered a final order dismissing appellant minor's petition for a judicial waiver of the statutory requirement that her physician notify her parent or guardian prior to terminating her pregnancy. The minor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The minor challenged the judgment entered. The appeals court first held that the factual findings by the trial judge were insufficient as no evidence supported a conclusion that the minor was not sufficiently mature to decide to terminate her pregnancy or that she failed to prove that notifying her parents of her decision would not be in her best interest. The fact that the minor lived with her parents, learned of her pregnancy through a home pregnancy test, and feared that divulging this decision would damage her relationships with her parents, standing alone, bore no logical relationship to the statutory grounds for a judicial bypass of the parental notification requirement. However, the instant court decided against remand because (1) remand for the purpose of supplying appropriate findings of fact would violate the legislative intention that judicial bypass petitions progress through the justice system without delay; and (2) the record before the circuit court was not likely to yield findings sufficient to deny the waiver petition. Moreover, under the criteria outlined by the Texas Supreme Court, notifying the minor's parents of her decision was not in her best interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the petition was granted.

City of Kissimmee v. Fla. Retail Fed'n, Inc.


Case No. 5D04-4065


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


915 So. 2d 205; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 16665; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2457



October 21, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by City of Kissimmee v. Fla. Retail Fed'n, Inc., 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 20385 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Dec. 1, 2005) Released for Publication December 19, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Osceola County, R. James Stroker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Osceola County (Florida) declared a local shopping cart retention ordinance unconstitutional because it purportedly conflicted with Fla. Stat. Ann. § 506.5131(2) (2000). Appellant, a city, appealed.


OVERVIEW: Many businesses installed retention systems in compliance with the ordinance. The appellees, members of the Florida Retail Federation (Federation), however, refused to install a retention system, electing instead to submit an alternative plan to retrieve their own carts. Because these plans represented a reactive approach rather than a preventative plan, the city rejected these proposals and demanded compliance with the ordinance. The Federation sued the city for declaratory and injunctive relief, Both sides moved for summary judgment. The trial court denied the city's motion, granted the Federation's. The appellate court agreed with the city that the ordinance was constitutional. A municipality could, under its broad home rule powers, enact local ordinances that were not inconsistent with general law pursuant to Fla. Const. art. VIII, § 2(b). The court rejected the contention that when the legislature prohibited the assessment of any fee, fine or cost against a retailer whose cart had been retrieved from public property, it effectively immunized retailers from all efforts by local government to encourage owners to keep carts under control.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Whitsett v. State


Nos. 4D03-1625 and 4D03-1747


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


913 So. 2d 1208; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 16612; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2442



October 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 22, 2005.
Post-conviction relief denied at Whitsett v. State, 94 So. 3d 604, 2012 Fla. App. LEXIS 12035 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated appeals and cross-appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; Robert R. Makemson, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-777 CFA.
Whitsett v. State, 671 So. 2d 799, 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 3397 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County (Florida), that convicted him of armed escape from a civil commitment facility pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 394.927(1); defendant claimed, inter alia, that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated the single subject rule in Fla. Const. art. III, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was being held as a pretrial civil detainee pending a jury determination of whether he qualified for commitment for involuntary commitment as a sexually violent predator. Prior to his trial, defendant attempted to escape from the facility. The appellate court found that the object and purpose of 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 222 was to protect the public from sexually violent predators. Making it a crime for sexually violent predators to escape from their commitment promoted the purpose of the legislation through the additional measure to protect the public. Therefore, Fla. Stat. ch. 394.927(1) was constitutional under the single subject provision of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. Because defendant's allegation that the prosecutor breached a promise to recommend a lesser sentence was conclusively refuted by the plea agreement and colloquy, the trial court did not err in refusing to hold an evidentiary hearing on the motion. Finally, since the trial court's order on the State's motion in limine was not dispositive of the case, and it was not designated as a motion being reserved for appeal, the issue was not preserved under Fla. R. App. P. 9.140(b)(2)(A)(i).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cornelius v. State


No. 4D04-4433


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


913 So. 2d 1176; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 16248; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2412



October 12, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 22, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of order denying rule 3.850 motion from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Jack H. Cook, Judge; L.T. Case No. 97-3634 CFA02.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion, challenging an earlier plea as involuntary. The Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), summarily denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into a plea to resolve a felony DUI charge. As part of his plea, he agreed to a lifetime revocation of his driver's license. In the motion under review, defendant alleged that he did so because counsel advised him that he could apply for a work permit license after five years. This was a correct statement of law at the time. Later, the legislature changed the law to eliminate the opportunity to apply for a work permit license for individuals with lifetime suspensions. Defendant was precluded from reinstatement. The appellate court held that a trial court was required to inform a defendant only of the direct consequences of the plea but was under no duty to advise the defendant of any collateral consequences. The possibility of a reinstatement of driving privileges was not a direct consequence of a plea. The trial court informed defendant that his license was revoked for life and, thus, informed him of the direct consequence of his plea. Nothing in the plea hearings or plea agreement even mentioned reinstatement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Connelly v. Old Bridge Vill. Co-Op, Inc.


Case No. 2D04-4905


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


915 So. 2d 652; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 16307; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2390



October 12, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lee County; John S. Carlin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners, sued defendants, neighbors, a trailer park, and others, seeking a declaratory judgment concerning the borders of the owners' property. The owners dismissed the action as against the neighbors after the action was sent to mediation. The Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida) awarded attorney's fees to the neighbors pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 57.105(1) (2003). The owners appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The property owners purchased a mobile home in a mobile home park. The owners sought to build a fence around their property, and the neighbors claimed that the proposed fence would impose on their property. Fla. Stat. ch. 57.105(1) (2003) authorized an award of attorney's fees when plaintiffs or their counsel knew or should have known that their claim against a defendant was not supported by material facts, or would not be supported by the application of then existing law to those material facts. The property interests in this case were complex. The only means of determining where one's leased property began and another ended was by reference to sketches and drawings. The court held that it was possible that jurisdiction under the Declaratory Judgment Act would exist against the neighbors. Certainly, if this suit were to proceed without the neighbors, who initially complained about the fence, and if the court decided that the fence should be placed in a position that the neighbors would deem adverse to them, then their omission as parties would be glaring. Thus, the voluntary dismissal did not constitute adequate justification for Fla. Stat ch. 57.105 (2003) fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

OVERVIEW: Three police officers observed defendant engaging in hand to hand transactions with passengers in cars. The officers then stopped in front of the house where that activity was occurring. Defendant ran to the rear of the property, but other officers were located there, and when they identified themselves, defendant tried to run but was arrested. On appeal, the appellate court found a new trial was required because the State's comment violated defendant's constitutional right to remain silent following his arrest.

Hillsborough County Sch. Bd. v. Ward


CASE NO. 1D04-5042


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


913 So. 2d 39; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 14870; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2279



September 23, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hillsborough County Sch. Bd. v. Ward, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18711 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Nov. 2, 2005) Released for Publication November 18, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Judge of Compensation Claims. Joseph Murphy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Florida Judge of Compensation Claims (JCC) granted a petition for benefits filed by appellee claimant in which she requested the reinstatement of permanent total disability (PTD) supplemental benefits. Appellants, an employer and its insurer (E/C), sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court held that in order to terminate the claimant's supplemental benefits, the E/C had the burden of showing, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 440.15(1)(e), that the claimant would be eligible for both social security retirement benefits and social security disability benefits. Because the E/C failed in this burden, it was ordered to reinstate the claimant's supplemental benefits. On appeal, the E/C argued that (1) the claimant's entitlement to supplemental benefits automatically ceased when she turned age 62 because she became permanently and totally disabled prior to reaching age 62; and (2) even if the claimant's entitlement did not automatically cease at age 62, she was no longer entitled to supplemental benefits because she was eligible for social security disability benefits. The appeals court held that the claimant was eligible for social security disability benefits if she was insured for disability insurance benefits, was younger than age 65, and was under a disability. Thus, as the JCC found, the E/C failed to show that the claimant was eligible for social security disability benefits and declined a continuance so that the issue could be addressed in more detail.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Olive v. Maas


CASE NO. 1D04-3436


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


911 So. 2d 837; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 13869; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2096



September 2, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Olive v. Maas, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 16915 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Sept. 27, 2005)
Related proceeding at Maas v. Olive, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 483 (Fla., Mar. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Leon County. L. Ralph Smith, Judge.
Olive v. Maas, 811 So. 2d 644, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 219 (Fla., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attorney appealed the final order from the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which granted defendant state officials' motion to dismiss his complaint seeking a declaration that the statute governing the statewide registry of private attorneys available for court appointment to represent death row inmates in postconviction proceedings (Registry Act) violated Fla. Const. art. V, art. II, § 3, and art. I, §§ 16, 9, 2, 13, and 17.


OVERVIEW: For six years, the attorney represented a death row inmate on a pro bono basis in capital postconviction proceedings. He filed suit alleging that he believed he had a right under the Florida constitution to seek compensation in excess of the capped fee schedule set forth in Fla. Stat. ch. 27.7002 of the Registry Act. The trial court dismissed the complaint, finding that the fee challenge was dealt with in the attorney's prior case (Olive I) and that the attorney's constitutional claim did not present a justiciable controversy because there was no state constitutional right to counsel in capital postconviction relief proceedings. On appeal, the court disagreed with the trial court that the constitutional challenges to the Registry Act were decided in Olive I and found that Olive I addressed only the constitutionality of the capped fee schedule in the Registry Act. The court then found that there was enough confusion in the Florida law to raise a question as to the existence of a right to counsel in capital postconviction relief proceedings under the Florida constitution; therefore the trial court erred in finding that the case did not present a justiciable controversy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings.

Orlando Reg'l Healthcare Sys. v. Alexander


Case Nos. 5D04-802 and 5D04-2904


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


909 So. 2d 582; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 13877; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2074



September 2, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 21, 2005.
Writ granted by Orlando Reg'l Healthcare v. Alexander, 932 So. 2d 598, 2006 Fla. App. LEXIS 10782 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., June 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Administrative Appeal from the Division of Administrative Hearings.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part, REVERSED in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An administrative law judge (ALJ) in the Division of Administrative Hearings (Florida) held, among other things, that appellant hospital was not exempted from providing pre-delivery notice in violation of Florida's Birth-Related Neurological Injury Compensation Act (NICA). The hospital appealed and appellee mother cross-appealed as to the issues of compensability and notice.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court disagreed with the ALJ's conclusion that the mother was entitled to notice under the NICA, as notice to a patient when the patient had an emergency medical condition, or when notice was not practicable, was not required under Fla. Stat. ch. 766.316. The ALJ misapplied the law by interpreting the statute to require both: (1) a finding of an emergency medical condition, and (2) a finding that the provision of notice was not practicable. The statute contained two distinct exceptions, each of which independently provided an exception to the pre-delivery notice requirement. As to the mother's cross-appeal, insufficient evidence was presented to conclude that the mother was not in labor following the abruption and prior to delivery, or that the oxygen deprivation the child suffered during the course of delivery and resuscitation did not contribute significantly to his brain injury. Finally, the terms "labor," "substantial impairment," and "permanent injury," were certain enough that a reasonable and practical construction could be given to the language by reference to other definable sources, such as the medical literature.


OUTCOME: The ALJ's ruling that the hospital was not exempted from providing pre-delivery notice was error, and that portion of the order was reversed. In all other respects, the order was affirmed.

Dep't of Bus. & Profl Regulation, Div. of Pari-Mutuel Wagering v. Gulfstream Park Racing Ass'n


CASE NO. 1D04-4094, CASE NO. 1D04-3819


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


912 So. 2d 616; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 13663; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2033



August 31, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 8, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Hartman-Tuner, Inc. v. Gulfstream Park Racing Ass'n, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18369 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Oct. 21, 2005)
Rehearing denied by State Dep't of Bus. & Prof'l Regulation v. Gulfstream Park Racing Ass'n, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 18368 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Oct. 21, 2005)
Affirmed by Fla. Dep't of Bus. & Prof'l Regulation v. Gulfstream Park Racing Ass'n, 967 So. 2d 802, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1597 (Fla., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Judge Jonathan E. Sjostrom.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) declared Fla. Stat. ch. 550.615(6) was unconstitutional and determined that the statute was a special law, invalid on the ground that it was not enacted according to the applicable procedures in Fla. Const. art. III, § 10, in favor of the request of appellee racing association. Appellant Florida Department of Business and Professional Regulation sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Fla. Stat ch. 550.615(6) prohibited the holder of a thoroughbred horse racing permit from engaging in inter-track wagering in an area of Florida where there were at least three horse racing permit holders within 25 miles of each other, but the conditions that triggered the prohibition of ch. 550.615(6) against inter-track wagering applied only in one small geographic area straddling the border between Dade County and Broward County. On appeal, and after a review of the evidence in the record, there was no reasonable possibility that those conditions would ever exist in any other part of the state. Moreover, the decision to exclude a limited class of thoroughbred permit holders from the privilege of engaging in inter-track wagering was an arbitrary decision that did not promote any valid public policy. For these reasons, the appeals court agreed with the circuit court that ch. 550.615(6) was a special law enacted in the guise of a general law, and thus invalid. Finally, the class created by ch. 550.615(6) was closed. The statute applied only in a limited part of Florida, and therefore, it should have been enacted under the procedures that applied to special laws.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Griffin


CASE NOS. 4D03-4890, 4D04-933, 4D04-1603 & 4D04-1637


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


909 So. 2d 538; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 14464; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2065



August 31, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 31, 2005.
Review denied by Johnson v. Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1563 (Fla., June 29, 2006)
Review denied by Griffin v. Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1602 (Fla., June 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated petitions for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Miette K. Burnstein and Barry E. Goldstein, Judges; and to the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Catherine M. Brunson, Kenneth D. Stern and Elizabeth T. Maass, Judges: L.T. Case Nos. 03-14122 CACE (Broward), 03-19957 11 (Broward), 04-4107 (Broward), and 502004CA003141XXXXM (Palm Beach).
Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Griffin, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9307 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., June 15, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Florida Department of Highway Safety and Motor Vehicles (Department) sought certiorari review as to the question of whether using non-lawyers as hearing officers in formal hearings under Fla. Stat. ch. 322.2615(6) violated the due process rights of motorists arrested for driving under the influence. In four other cases, respondent motorists sought review. After the cases at issue were consolidated, the instant matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that if the Florida Constitution allowed for non-lawyers to sit on the county court bench, it surely allowed for non-lawyers to sit as hearing officers in driver's license suspension hearings. Further, if there was no due process violation for the use of non-lawyers as county court judges, there could be no similar violation in the use of these same non-lawyers as hearing officers pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 322. Thus, as to three of the cases on review, the circuit court afforded the motorists due process and applied the correct law. As to the last case, the hearing officer acted as an advocate for the Department when she stopped the hearing and located a missing document, and quashed the hearing officer's order of suspension, set aside and vacated the suspension of that motorists' license, and directed the Department to expunge the suspension from his driving record. Thus, she departed from her neutral role as magistrate. Further, the finding as to the hearing officer's abandonment of neutrality meant that the decision to quash the suspension order and to reinstate driving privileges remained, and rendered moot the other errors asserted by the Department.


OUTCOME: The question was answered in the negative, the Department's petition was granted in the first case, but the motorists' petitions for review in the related, consolidated cases were denied.

Rosado v. Vosilla


Case No. 5D04-2617


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


909 So. 2d 505; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 13384; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 2018



August 26, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 14, 2005.
Review granted by Vosilla v. Rosado, 924 So. 2d 811, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 392 (Fla., 2006)
Affirmed by Vosilla v. Rosado, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2612 (Fla., Nov. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Seminole County, Marlene M. Alva, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant original property owners (OPOs) sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Seminole County (Florida), which granted judgment to appellee subsequent property owners (SPOs) in the SPOs' quiet title action, arising from their acquisition of the property after it was sold to another at a tax deed sale.


OVERVIEW: The OPOs failed to pay their taxes, and the tax collector issued a tax certificate for the property. The OPOs notified the tax collector and the court clerk that they had moved and they supplied him with their new address. However, the address information was not updated. The OPOs did not receive notice of the application for a tax deed or the date of the proposed sale. The property was sold at the tax deed sale, and that purchaser deeded the land by quit claim deed to the SPOs. The SPOs brought their quiet title action, and the OPOs claimed that they did not receive notice of the tax sale. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the SPOs, finding that the notice was sufficient under Fla. Stat. ch. 197.522(1)(a) and 197.502(4)(a) (2000). On appeal, the court found that the clerk's notice of the tax deed sale to the OPOs' old address was not "reasonably calculated under all of the circumstances" to apprise them of the sale. Accordingly, their constitutional due process rights were violated. To the extent other case law conflicted, it was noted and a conflict was certified on that issue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court. It receded from Eurofund to the extent that it conflicted with the court's holding, and it certified a conflict with Alwani.

Morris v. State


Case No. 5D04-3688


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


909 So. 2d 428; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 12765; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1967



August 19, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 8, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Bob Wattles, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), which convicted and sentenced him for sexual battery with a deadly weapon or physical force and burglary of a dwelling with an assault or battery, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(3), 810.02(2)(a), which were entered pursuant to his no contest pleas.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled no contest to criminal charges. He was convicted and sentenced. On appeal, defendant raised three issues: (1) the trial court erred by denying his motion to withdraw his pleas based on defense counsel's failure to advise him that the burglary charge was barred by the statute of limitations, (2) his conviction for burglary had to be vacated because it was barred by the statute of limitations, and (3) the condition of probation requiring him to submit biological specimens for DNA testing was unconstitutional. The court found that defendant failed to preserve his issue regarding the statute of limitations. Also, his counsel's alleged ineffectiveness regarding that issue had to be presented in a motion for post-conviction relief because there were factual issues to be resolved through an evidentiary hearing. Based on a prior conclusive decision, the court rejected the argument that the DNA testing requirement under Fla. Stat, ch. 943.325 violated his constitutional right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. Finally, the court concluded that defendant's other constitutional challenges to DNA testing as a probation condition were not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentences without prejudice to his right to seek post-conviction relief on a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel.

Hobson v. State


CASE NO. 1D04-2781


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


908 So. 2d 1162; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 12772; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1958



August 19, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 7, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Peter L. Dearing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part, REVERSED in part, and REMANDED with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida), which convicted him of one count of armed robbery and one count of aggravated fleeing or eluding (AFE) in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(4) (2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant participated in the robbery of a convenience store by serving as the get-away driver. While driving away from police pursuit, he caused an accident. Instead of stopping, he continued his flight. He was convicted for AFE in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(4) (2002) as well as armed robbery. On appeal, he argued that he was wrongfully convicted of AFE because the State could not prove essential elements of the offense. He also brought other challenges, but the court rejected them without discussion. The court found that it was undisputed that officers began their pursuit because defendant had participated in robbing a convenience store, not because he left the scene of an accident involving injury, death, or property damage. Therefore, the first element of ch. 316.1935(4) was absent from the evidence. Also absent was the third element of further property damage or injury after striking the car and continuing flight. Consequently, the AFE conviction was not supported by the evidence. However, defendant did commit the lesser included offense of misdemeanor fleeing or eluding in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1935(1) (2002) and could be sentenced for that crime.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence for AFE, and the court remanded for the entry judgment and a sentence for the lesser included offense of misdemeanor fleeing or eluding. Otherwise, the judgment and sentence was affirmed without discussion.

Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Rosenthal


Case No. 2D04-1108


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


908 So. 2d 602; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 12794; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1964



August 19, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 9, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Thirteenth Judicial Circuit for Hillsborough County; sitting in its appellate capacity.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted, order quashed, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Highway Safety and Motor Vehicles sought certiorari review of the order of the Circuit Court for the Thirteenth Judicial Circuit for Hillsborough County (Florida), which granted a writ of certiorari and quashed the Department's order revoking respondent driver's operator's license. The Department argued that the trial court failed to apply the correct law in determining that the offense was not a qualifying offense.


OVERVIEW: Acting under Fla. Stat. ch. 322.27(5) (2002), the Department revoked the driver's operator's license for five years as a habitual traffic offender. The Department based its determination on one offense of driving under the influence and two offenses of driving while his license was suspended (DWLS). The trial court ruled that one of the offenses on which the Department relied was not a qualifying offense under the pertinent statutory provisions since it was based on a nolo contendere plea with adjudication withheld and thus could not be considered a conviction for purposes of determining the driver to be a habitual traffic offender. The appellate court held that the trial court failed to apply the correct law in issuing a ruling that was at odds with the clearly established law articulated in Raulerson. The driver's second DWLS offense was not an offense for which adjudication was withheld under Fla. Stat. ch. 318.14(10). The disposition sheet established that the driver's second DWLS offense was a knowing offense subject to a criminal penalty pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 322.34(2) and therefore not subject to disposition as a noncriminal traffic infraction under Fla. Stat. ch. 318.


OUTCOME: The petition was granted, and the order was quashed.

Rogers v. Hood


CASE NO. 1D04-4609


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


906 So. 2d 1220; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 11098; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1761



July 21, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 8, 2005.
Review denied by Rogers v. Hood, 919 So. 2d 436, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2590 (Fla., Dec. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal the Circuit Court for Leon County. L. Ralph Smith, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant registered Florida voters sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which granted the motion to dismiss filed by appellees, the Florida Secretary of State and the Florida Director of Elections, and dismissed the voters complaint which alleged causes of action for declaratory relief, injunctive relief, and for writ of quo warranto.


OVERVIEW: The voters sought to prevent the destruction of unused punch card ballots from the 2000 presidential election, claiming that they were public records under Fla. Const. art. I, § 24 and Fla. Stat. ch. 119.01 (2003). The voters also contended that Fla. Stat. ch. 101.545 (2003), which governed the retention and destruction of certain election materials, violated Fla. Const. art. I, § 24. The trial court ruled that the unused ballots were not public records and that Fla. Stat. ch. 101.545 (2003) did not violate any portion of the state constitution. The court agreed. The unused ballots did not fit into Florida's concept of public records because the did not perpetuate, communicate, or formalize knowledge. The ballots did not become public records until they were actually voted. Because the ballots were not public records, ch. 101.545's grant of discretion to the Secretary of State and election supervisors concerning retention or destruction of the ballots did not violate the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Fla. Dep't of Revenue v. Naval Aviation Museum Found., Inc.


CASE NO.: 1D03-3570


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


907 So. 2d 586; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 11013; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1711



July 18, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 3, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Escambia County. Linda Nobles, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Escambia County (Florida) granted a final summary judgment to appellee foundation, and against appellant, the Florida Department of Revenue (Department), holding that the foundation was exempt from collecting Florida sales tax. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The determinative issue in the instant appeal was whether the foundation was a federal instrumentality for state tax immunity purposes. The appeals court held that it was not. The foundation was a charitable corporation under the laws of Florida created solely for the purpose of fostering and perpetuating the U.S. Naval Museum, unfettered by government control. Further, the foundation was not operated by federal employees and, although federal law and U.S. Navy regulations governed the Navy's acceptance of the foundation's gifts to it and impacted the finances and budget of the foundation, the federal government did not regulate, supervise or appoint members of the governing board of the foundation. By this arrangement, the U.S. Navy and the foundation were independent legal entities. Third, the foundation did not fulfill an essential function of government, despite the fact that it raised significant financial support for the naval museum. Hence, due to the aforementioned, the court declined to address the Department's alternative argument that even if the foundation were a federal instrumentality, it would not be immune from the obligation to collect state sales taxes.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Bradshaw v. State

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Daryl E. Trawick, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 01-018454.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, we affirm in part, vacate in part, and remand with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance and trafficking an illegal drug and sentenced him to five years in prison for the former and to a concurrent 15-year minimum mandatory sentence for the trafficking conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment entered against him, first contending that the trial court abused its discretion by admitting certain photographs as impeachment evidence during the State's rebuttal as the trial court had excluded the photographs earlier as a remedy for the State's Richardson violation. Second, with the State's concession, defendant's convictions and sentences for both possession and trafficking in the same heroin violated double jeopardy. Accordingly, the conviction and sentence for simple possession could not stand and had to be dismissed on remand. Finally, the sentence for the trafficking count did not unconstitutionally violate Fla. Stat. ch. 835.135, as amended by 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 188, the single-subject rule, as the Florida Supreme Court affirmed the instant court's decision that there was no constitutional impairment to this statute.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for simple possession was vacated, and the matter was remanded with instructions to dismiss that count. However, in all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

Riopelle v. Dep't of Fin. Servs., Div. of Workers' Comp.


CASE NOS. 1D04-1347 & 1D04-2908


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


907 So. 2d 1220; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 10001; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1601



June 28, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Released for Publication August 17, 2005. Rehearing denied by Riopelle v. Dep't of Fin. Servs., 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 13575 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Aug. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from orders of the Department of Financial Services.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Florida Department of Financial Services (Department), affirmed two stop-work and penalty-assessment orders issued against appellant employer for failing to provide workers' compensation coverage to eight employees at two job sites. The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employer claimed on appeal that Fla. Stat. ch. 440.107 (2001) violated the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution and Fla. Const. art. I, § 9, because it did not provide for notice or an opportunity to be heard before or immediately upon issuance of a stop-work order, and instead only permitted an employer to contest an order under Fla. Stat. ch. 120, which did not provide expedited review. The appeals court disagreed. The employer was advised that she had the right to request an expedited, summary hearing pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 120.574 (2001). But, she instead sought relief under Fla. Stat. ch. 120.57(1) (2001), and never informed the judge or the Department that she was being harmed by the less expeditious proceeding. Thus, she failed to show that Fla. Stat. ch. 440.107 was unconstitutional by denying due process to an employer found to be in violation of Fla. Stat ch. 440. Finally, the employer failed to provide any argument that showed why $ 2,200 in penalties, as authorized by Fla. Stat. ch. 440.107, was disproportionate to her conduct in allowing eight employees to engage in new-home construction without workers' compensation coverage.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Estevez v. State


CASE NO.: 1D03-5497


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


915 So. 2d 185; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9736; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1581



June 23, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An appeal from the Circuit Court for Duval County. Michael R. Weatherby, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part, REVERSED in part, and REMANDED for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest to possession of a firearm by a convicted felon and resisting arrest without violence. Earlier, the Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida) denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was asked to leave a department store by store employees. At the same time, a police officer, who happened to be in the store investigating an unrelated incident, advised defendant that he was to be issued a trespass warning. The officer instructed defendant to come with him to his patrol car, where the trespass warning forms were kept. At the patrol car, the officer patted down defendant and discovered a gun. At the suppression hearing, the officer's testimony showed that he conducted the pat-down search not out of any particularized concern for his safety, but as a matter of routine. The officer also testified that, prior to the pat-down, he had no intention of arresting defendant. The appellate court held that an officer needed to have probable cause to believe a suspect was armed before the officer was allowed to conduct a pat down search or frisk of the suspect to ascertain the presence of a weapon. Pat-down searches performed routinely or for safety purposes only were constitutionally impermissible.


OUTCOME: The conviction for possession of a firearm by a convicted felon was reversed and the sentence therefor was vacated. The conviction for resisting arrest without violence was affirmed. The case was remanded.

Smallridge v. State


CASE NO. 1D03-4751


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT

Review denied by Smallridge v. State, 918 So. 2d 293, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2522 (Fla., 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smallridge v. Fla., 126 S. Ct. 2871, 165 L. Ed. 2d 897, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 4551 (U.S., June 12, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Santa Rosa County. Michael G. Allen, Judge.

Wright v. State


CASE NO. 4D04-499


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


920 So. 2d 21; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9212; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1495



June 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Wright v. State, 915 So. 2d 1198, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2327 (Fla., Oct. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert Fogan, Judge; L.T. Case No. 03-14938 CF.
Wright v. State, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6499 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., May 4, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction for possession of cocaine by the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida). He challenged, on substantive due process grounds, the facial constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.101, amended to remove guilty knowledge as an element of possession of a controlled substance and adding lack of knowledge of the illicit nature of a controlled substance as an affirmative defense.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found a rational relationship between the legitimate governmental interest in addressing the drug problem and the elimination of the difficult-to-prove element of knowledge of a substance's illicit nature. Defendant characterized the statute as removing an element of a crime, the mens rea of guilty knowledge, and making the lack of it an affirmative defense, thereby improperly shifting to a defendant the burden to disprove. The appeals court disagreed. The statute removed guilty knowledge as an element but did not require a defendant to prove or disprove knowledge. It was optional to raise lack of knowledge as a defense. The statute simply provided that once the defense was utilized, a permissive presumption attached allowing the jury to draw an inference from the facts. Only mandatory and conclusive presumptions were prohibited. Further, there was a rational purpose for this presumption, and it was tied to a legitimate governmental interest. Accordingly, the court rejected defendant's substantive due process challenge. The affirmative defense of lack of knowledge would have been available to defendant, but he was still required to request the instruction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Rehearing granted by, in part, Rehearing denied by, in part Dep't of Hwy v. Griffin, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 14777 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Aug. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Consolidated petitions for writ of certiorari to the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Miette K. Burnstein and Barry E. Goldstein, Judges; and to the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Catherine M. Brunson, Kenneth D. Stern and Elizabeth T. Maass, Judges: L.T. Case Nos. 03-14122 CACE (Broward), 03-19957 11 (Broward), 04-4107 (Broward), and 502004CA003141XXXXM (Palm Beach).



DISPOSITION: Certiorari Denied as to all Four of the Petitions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Hearing officers upheld the driver's license suspensions of appellants, three motorists, and appellee motorist. The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida) and the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida) upheld three and reversed one of the suspensions. Appellant/appellee state department and three motorists petitioned for certiorari review. The cases were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: In each proceeding, the motorists contended that the use of non-lawyers as hearing officers, in formal hearings pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 322.2615(6) (2004), violated the due process rights of the motorists, who were arrested for driving under the influence. The state supreme court found that the procedural scheme employed by the state department of using non-lawyer hearing officers did not run afoul of the Florida or United States Constitutions nor the due process rights of the motorists. Additionally, the state department contended that a circuit court erred in quashing a hearing officer's order of suspension, setting aside and vacating the suspension of a motorist's license, and directing the state department to expunge the suspension from the motorist's driving record because the court found that the hearing officer acted as an advocate for the state department and departed from her neutral role as magistrate during the administrative proceeding when she stopped the hearing, located a missing document, and entered it as evidence. The state supreme court found that the hearing officer departed from her neutral role as magistrate during the hearing and should have been recused.


OUTCOME: The state department's petition for writ of certiorari was denied as to the issue of the hearing officer departing from her neutral role during the hearing. The three motorists' petitions for writ of certiorari were denied in their entirety.

Akridge v. Crow


Case No. 2D03-5146


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


903 So. 2d 346; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9141; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1480



June 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus to the County Court for Polk County; Mary Catherine Green, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition for habeas corpus is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmates sought a writ of habeas corpus challenging as unconstitutional their confinement pursuant to Polk County, Fla., Cir. Ct. Admin. Order 7-12.0, which established a collections court program for the collection of fines, fees, and costs in all criminal cases. This matter followed.


OVERVIEW: The inmates challenged the county's collections program, first contending that it was unconstitutional on its face because it provided for the incarceration of individuals who were unable to pay. The appeals court agreed. Moreover, this aspect of the county's program was inconsistent with Fla. Stat. ch. 938.30(2), which expressly provided for court-ordered community service where a defendant was unable to pay. The appeals court also agreed that Polk County, Fla., Cir. Ct. Admin. Order 7-12.0 violated the inmates' right to due process as it was debatable whether the inmates received sufficient notice requiring their appearance as provided for in Fla. Stat. ch. 938.30(3). What they received was a memorandum of sentence, better known in the county as a "snap out." Under these facts, some of the snap outs were not signed by a judge and were thus inadequate to serve as orders requiring the recipient to appear for a hearing. Further, the administrative order did not require that those arrested and jailed for failure to pay be brought before the court at the earliest Wednesday available. Based on these facts, the inmates were entitled to habeas relief.


OUTCOME: The writ was granted.

Scott v. State


No. 4D03-4860


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


903 So. 2d 289; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9097; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1444



June 8, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] DECISION WITHOUT PUBLISHED OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 24, 2005.

S.K.R. v. Dep't of Children & Family Servs. (In the Interest of S.M.A.L.)


Case No. 2D04-1704


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


902 So. 2d 328; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 8061; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1345



May 27, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Frank Quesada and Irene H. Sullivan, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) terminated appellant legal father's parental rights to his child. The legal father appealed in an action involving appellees, the Department of Children and Family Services and an adoption corporation.


OVERVIEW: Upon the legal father's challenge to the judgment entered against him, the appeals court held that the trial court erred in its interpretation of the statutes governing the executions of consent to adoption. Under the facts presented, the legal father's consent to adoption was required pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 63.062(1) (2003). Additionally, the trial court's interpretation of the statute as denying a legal father standing to object to the termination of his parental rights was contrary to the legal interest afforded a legal father. A presumption of legitimacy to children born of a marriage existed and was based on the policy of protecting the welfare of the child. In the instant action, there was no apparent indication that the legislature intended to change the law with regard to the presumption of legitimacy, a result produced by the trial court's ruling.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1715 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wolland


CASE NO. 3D04-1380


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


902 So. 2d 278; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 7898; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1315



May 25, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 10, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Mary Barzee, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 02-14283.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with 115 counts of making false statements to a state health care agency in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 409.920(2)(a) (2001). The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charges. The State appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the charges after finding that Florida's Medicaid Provider Fraud Statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 409.920(2)(a) (2001), was preempted by the federal Social Security Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1320a-7b(a). The federal act required that the crime be done "knowingly and willfully" while the Florida act required only that the act be done "knowingly." Based on a recent precedent, the trial court determined that the state law was preempted by the federal statute. The appellate court held that considering the objective of Congress to limit and punish health care fraud and considering the language used in Fla. Stat. ch. 409.920(2)(a) (2001), notwithstanding the failure of Fla. Stat. ch. 409.920(2)(a) (2001) to contain the term "willfully," the federal and state enactments regarding false claims were in harmony in purpose and effect and the charges at issue should not have been dismissed as preempted by federal law. The fear articulated in the earlier precedent that the Florida statute might criminalize activity that the federal statute intended to protect was not present in the instant case.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the cause was remanded with directions to reinstate the charges.

Green v. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles


CASE NO. 1D04-4668


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


905 So. 2d 922; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 7656; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1301



May 23, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 22, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Green v. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 11918 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., July 6, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of certiorari denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner driver sought certiorari review of the Florida circuit court's denial of his petition for writ of certiorari. An administrative law judge upheld the administrative suspension of his driver's license. The driver sought certiorari review in the circuit court. He argued that his breath alcohol test results did not constitute proof of an unlawful blood alcohol level and that he was denied adequate notice of the charge against him.


OVERVIEW: The driver's license was administratively suspended when his breath-alcohol test, administered after his arrest for driving under the influence (DUI), revealed blood alcohol levels of .100 and .102. The citation the driver was issued indicated he was arrested for driving with an unlawful blood alcohol level and that his license was suspended for that reason. The driver requested formal review of the suspension pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 322.2615 (2003). During the administrative review of his license suspension, his breath test results were admitted into evidence. The appellate court held that even without judicially including the term "breath alcohol" in the statute, the breath alcohol test results provided competent, substantial evidence that the driver had an unlawful blood alcohol level. The driver's application for formal review indicated he received notice of the license suspension and the reason for it, i.e., because he received a citation for DUI. The driver knew no blood test had been given, and that he had an unlawful breath alcohol. Consequently, he had actual notice of the reason his license was suspended.


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of certiorari was denied.

Staten v. Gonzalez-Falla


CASE NO.: 1D03-5185


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


904 So. 2d 498; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 7276; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1253



May 18, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Staten v. Gonzales-Falla, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 11449 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., June 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Madison County. Thomas J. Kennon, Jr., Judge.
Staten v. Gonzalez-Falla, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 3592 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Mar. 17, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Madison County (Florida) awarded appellee trustee a statutory way of necessity across a decedent's property without restriction as to its use. Appellant personal representative sought further review and the trustee moved for clarification, which was granted. The instant matter followed.


OVERVIEW: Because the trial court did not restrict the easement at issue to the uses which were permitted in Fla. Stat. ch. 704.01(2) (2001), it committed reversible error. The personal representative had previously permitted the trustee to use the road across his property, but the trustee had created a nuisance on the property by leasing it to a hunt club whose tenants were loud and annoying at all hours of the day and night and used the property in an unsanitary and unhealthy manner. Moreover, the legislature permitted a statutory way of necessity to allow the dominant tenement to be used only for those purposes which were set forth in Fla. Stat. ch. 704.01(2) (2001). If landlocked property was to be used for a purpose other than the statutory purpose, a lawful easement or access had to be obtained other than through Fla. Stat. ch. 704.01(2) (2001).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Smith v. State

Bostic v. State


Case No. 5D03-3270


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


902 So. 2d 225; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6954; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1235



May 13, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 2, 2005.
Review denied by Bostic v. State, 912 So. 2d 1217, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1959 (Fla., Sept. 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Putnam County, Edward E. Hedstrom, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Putnam County (Florida) denied defendant's motion to dismiss the information filed against him, charging possession of a firearm by a convicted felon, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 790.23(1)(a) (2001) or, in the alternative, his motion to declare Fla. Stat. ch. 790.23 (2001) unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the denial of his motion to dismiss a possession of a firearm by a convicted felon charge, arguing that the rifle he possessed was an "antique firearm," as such was defined in Fla. Stat. ch. 790.001(1) (2001), and thus exempted under the Florida Statutes. To support his position, he claimed that because his rifle used black powder instead of fixed ammunition and its ignition system was a form of percussion cap, the weapon was an antique firearm. The trial court first ruled that dismissal was not warranted because it interpreted Fla. Stat. ch. 790.23 (2001) as prohibiting any firearm, whether antique or otherwise, from being possessed by a convicted felon. This ruling was incorrect as the statute provided that the firearm a convicted felon was prohibited from possessing excluded an antique firearm. However, because the rifle possessed by defendant included visible differences from an antique firearm such as a fiber optic sight, it was not a replica. Thus, dismissal of the charge was not warranted. Finally, the statute was constitutional because the term "replica" was not so vague as to render the statute unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Menuto


Case No. 2D03-4838


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


912 So. 2d 603; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6454; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1173



May 4, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Menuto v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1634 (Fla., July 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Brandt C. Downey, III, Judge.
State v. Menuto, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1024 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Feb. 4, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Pinellas Count (Florida), which dismissed an information against defendant charging him with illegally possessing a weapon in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 790.23(1)(b) (2002) and which held that statute unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: An information alleged that defendant violated Fla. Stat. ch. 790.23(1)(b) (2002) because he was 24 years old and had been found as a juvenile to have committed a burglary. He successfully moved to dismiss, arguing that an adjudication of delinquency was withheld and that ch. 790.23 was incongruous by requiring an adjudication of guilt to prove a violation of ch. 790.23(1)(a), yet still permitting a violation of ch. 790.23(1)(b) without an adjudication of delinquency. The trial court also held that ch. 790.23(1)(b) was unconstitutional. The State appealed. The court found that the differences in classification between ch. 790.23(1)(a)'s requirement of a prior guilt adjudication for criminal liability and ch. 790.23(1)(b)'s requirement of merely facts constituting a delinquent act to impose criminal liability was rationally related to preventing juvenile recidivism. Therefore, it did not violate equal protection. Moreover, since defendant's conduct fell squarely within the statute, it was not vague as applied to him. Finally, the statute was in pari materia with the headings of Fla. Stat. ch. 985.228(7), so it could be interpreted in accordance with its plain meaning.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing the information against defendant and remanded for further proceedings.

Michelson v. State


CASE NO. 4D02-4810


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


927 So. 2d 890; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6494; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1128



May 4, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 2, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Daniel True Andrews, Judge; L.T. Case No. 98- 7433 CF10A.
Michelson v. State, 805 So. 2d 983, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 17096 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit in Broward County (Florida), which convicted him for third-degree felony murder and vehicular homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted and tried for first-degree felony murder and vehicular homicide (VH) after a person died in a car accident caused by defendant evading police after escaping from prison. A jury convicted him of the lesser-included offense of second-degree murder and for VH. The murder conviction was reversed due to lack of evidence on an essential element, and remand for a conviction on third-degree felony murder was ordered. The trial court complied with that mandate, but defendant appealed, arguing he was denied his constitutional right to a trial by jury by entering a conviction without proof of an essential element. The State initially argued that review was barred by the law of the case doctrine, but the court found that conviction of a crime where a jury did not find all essential elements was a manifest injustice that required review. Moreover, the jury's findings supported a conviction for manslaughter by culpable negligence. However, defendant was also convicted of VH. While a single death could not support both convictions and only one conviction could stand, the sentencing order was unclear on whether defendant was sentenced for VH or manslaughter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for third-degree murder and remanded for a determination whether defendant was already convicted and sentenced on the vehicular homicide offense. If so, that conviction and sentence would stand and would preclude the conviction and imposition of sentence on manslaughter by culpable negligence. Otherwise, discretion was allowed to convict and impose sentence on either crime.

Wright v. State


CASE NO. 4D04-499


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6499; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1231



May 4, 2005, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL DISPOSITION OF ANY TIMELY FILED MOTION FOR REHEARING.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing granted by Wright v. State, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9212 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., June 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert Fogan, Judge; L.T. Case No. 0314938 CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Seventeenth Judicial Circuit Court, Broward County (Florida), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of possession of cocaine. The trial court then sentenced him to two years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of cocaine. Pertinent to that charge was Fla. Stat. ch. 893.101, which had been amended to remove guilty knowledge as an element of the possession of a controlled substance and which added lack of knowledge of the illicit nature of a controlled substance as an affirmative defense. Defendant was tried and convicted. On appeal, he challenged on substantive due process grounds the facial constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.101. He claimed that it improperly shifted the burden of proving lack of knowledge to him. The appellate court found that defendant did not challenge the constitutionality of that statute at trial, but could challenge it for the first time on appeal because a conviction for the violation of a facially invalid statute qualified as fundamental error. The appellate court then found that the statute did not impermissibly shift the burden to defendant to prove lack of knowledge, but merely allowed the jury to draw an inference from the facts if such a defense was raised. It also found that he was required to request a jury instruction on lack of knowledge, but in any event did not offer any evidence of lack of knowledge.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment and sentence were affirmed.

Curry v. Hadi


Case No. 2D03-5540


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


903 So. 2d 242; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6056; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1110



April 29, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 11, 2005. Released for Publication July 5, 2005.
Review denied by Curry v. Hadi, 928 So. 2d 334, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 594 (Fla., Mar. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for DeSoto County; James S. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, who was a detainee under the Jimmy Ryce Act (Act), Fla. Stat. chs. 394.910-.931 (2003), challenged a decision by the Circuit Court for DeSoto County (Florida), which dismissed his petition for habeas corpus relief (HCR) from his detainment by appellees, the Secretary of the Department of Children and Family Services and the executive director of a state civil commitment center.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the detainee's petition for HCR, finding that he failed to meet the exhaustion requirement of Fla. Stat. ch. 394.9215 (2003) and that none of the claims fell under the grounds in ch. 394.9215 that permitted a HCR petition. On appeal, the detainee argued that the trial court imposed an unconstitutional limitation on his right to seek habeas corpus relief. The court agreed that the trial court erroneously interpreted ch. 394.9215, which did not limit habeas corpus rights. However, the court affirmed dismissal since the detainee's claims were facially without merit. The court rejected the claim that the State violated a negotiated plea in his underlying criminal case by bringing the civil commitment proceeding because neither a negotiated plea nor equitable estoppel barred the State from bringing civil commitment proceedings under the Act. The detainee could not receive resentencing, even if his claim that the prison sentence in his criminal case was illegal. Since that challenge could have been made on direct appeal or by postconviction motion in the criminal case, the claim was not cognizable in a habeas corpus petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the detainee's petition.

Burnette v. State


Case No. 2D04-482


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


901 So. 2d 925; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5946; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1064



April 27, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 20, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pasco County; Daniel D. Diskey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Pasco County (Florida) adjudicated defendant guilty of possession of diazepam, driving under the influence, driving while his license was suspended or revoked, and refusing to allow alcohol testing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment entered, first contending that Fla. Stat. ch. 893.101 required him to prove that he lacked knowledge of the illicit nature of the substance, thereby relieving the State of its burden to prove each element of the crime beyond a reasonable doubt. However, knowledge of the nature of a substance was not an element of the offense of possession. A defendant charged under that section could concede all the elements of the offense and still be able to assert the defense that he did not know of the illicit nature of the specific substance. Thus, the affirmative defense created by ch. 893.101 did not violate due process by abrogating the State's burden of proving the defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. Second, the trial court gave an incomplete instruction on the law by failing to inform the jury that defendant's lack of knowledge of the illicit nature of the substance was a defense to the possession charge. Further, though the trial court instructed the jury that defendant's knowledge of the illicit nature of the substance was an issue, it failed to provide any indication that lack of knowledge was a defense to the charge.


OUTCOME: While a jury instruction given regarding the lack of knowledge affirmative defense was reversible error, the court rejected defendant's constitutionality argument as to the statutory elements of the possession of a controlled substance. Hence, the possession of diazepam conviction was reversed, and the matter was remanded for a new trial on this offense. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

 

1726 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Dempsey v. Dempsey


Case No. 2D04-2392


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


899 So. 2d 1272; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5960; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1067



April 27, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 13, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lee County; G. Keith Cary, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, individually and as the personal representative of a decedent's estate, sought review of a probate order of the Circuit Court for Lee County (Florida), which determined that appellee, the decedent's widow, was entitled to an elective share of the decedent's estate. The personal representative was directed to show cause why the appeal should not be dismissed for lack of jurisdiction because the order on appeal was a nonfinal order.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's will made no provision for the widow. The probate court entered its order determining that the widow was entitled to an elective share, but it had not yet determined the amount of the elective share. The court dismissed the appeal because the probate court's order was a nonfinal order that could not be reviewed under Fla. R. App. P. 9.110(a)(2). Under Fla. Prob. R. 5.360, determination of an elective share was a two-step process. The first step, in which the probate court determined a surviving spouse's entitlement to the elective share, was a non-adversarial proceeding. Once the probate court found entitlement to the elective share, it would proceed to the second adversarial step of determining the amount of the share. It was only after completion of the second step that judicial labor with regard to the rights and obligations of the personal representative could come to an end and a final, appealable order be entered. As the probate court had only completed the first step, the court was without jurisdiction to hear the appeal.


OUTCOME: The personal representative's appeal was dismissed.

State v. Higby


Case No. 2D04-2641


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


899 So. 2d 1269; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5964; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1068



April 27, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 20, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Susan W. Roberts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss his Fla. Stat. Ch. 812.155 (2000) charge of failure to return leased equipment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found ch. 812.155(4)(b) created a mandatory presumption of intent, which relieved the State of its burden to prove an essential element of the offense, in violation of the due process clauses of the federal and Florida Constitutions. The appellate court reversed. The trial court had improperly relied on a decision by another division of the circuit court. The trial court's decision should have been based on prior precedent from the appellate court, which held that the language in ch. 812.155(4)(b) that the failure to return property within five days after receipt of a demand for its return was prima facie evidence of fraudulent intent, created a permissive inference, not a mandatory presumption. As the statute created a permissive inference, the statute could not be found facially unconstitutional. Rather, defendant was required to make an "as-applied" challenge to the statute. If the statute was found unconstitutional "as-applied," the remedy would not be dismissal of the information. Rather, the State would have the right to take the case to trial without the benefit of the statutory presumption.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Cortina v. Dep't of HRS


CASE NO. 1D04-2452


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


901 So. 2d 273; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6003; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1094



April 27, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 20, 2005. As Corrected May 16, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Judge of Compensation Claims. Kathryn S. Pecko, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant appealed the final order of the Florida Judge of Compensation Claims (JCC), which denied the claimant temporary partial disability (TPD) benefits.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the claimant raised three issues: (1) whether the JCC erred by finding that no dispute existed for which the claimant was entitled to an independent medical examination (IME); (2) whether the JCC erred in rejecting a doctor's medical opinion and accepting his report for fact purposes only; and (3) whether Fla. Stat. ch. 440.13(5)(e) constituted an unconstitutional violation of separation of powers. As to the first issue, the appellate court found that there was a dispute concerning whether the claimant had reached psychiatric maximum medical improvement (MMI) and as to the claimant's entitlement to TPD benefits. The dispute arose because the claimant disagreed not only with the medical care she received by the authorized psychiatrist provided, but also with his determination that she had achieved MMI. Because the employer denied the claim for TPD benefits in part on the basis that the claimant had achieved overall MMI, the claimant's request to present medical opinion evidence from a psychiatric IME was directly related to demonstrating her entitlement to TPD benefits. Thus, the claimant was entitled to a psychiatric IME pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 440.13(5)(a).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed as to the second and third issues. The appellate court reversed as to the first issue and remanded for the approval of a psychiatric IME.
