Sch. Bd. v. State Bd. of Educ.


Case No. 5D04-2008


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


903 So. 2d 963; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5540; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1050



April 22, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Sch. Bd. v. State Bd. of Educ., 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 11424 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., June 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Non-Final Appeal from the Circuit Court for Osceola County, R. James Stroker, Judge.
Sch. Bd. v. UCP, 905 So. 2d 909, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5541 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school board sought review of the non-final order of the Circuit Court for Osceola County (Florida), which granted appellee State Board of Education's motion to change venue to Leon County.


OVERVIEW: The school board filed suit against the State Board in Osceola County, Florida, and sought a judgment declaring Florida's charter school statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 1002.33 (2003), facially unconstitutional and unconstitutional as applied. In addition, the school board sought to declare invalid certain actions and orders of the State Board regarding three charter school applications submitted to the school board. Lastly, the school board sought an injunction. The State Board moved to change venue to Leon County based on its home venue privilege as its principal office was located in Leon County. The appellate court held that a county school board was not "an individual" within the meaning of the "sword-wielder" exception whose constitutional rights had been directly threatened by the State Board's actions. Any claimed invasion of the school board's constitutional rights was secondary. Consequently, the sword-wielder exception did not apply to excuse compliance with the home venue rule. Finally, there was no showing of particularized harm to the school board separate and apart from the generalized harm suffered by other school boards in Florida.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1730 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rygwelski


Case No. 2D03-3877


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


899 So. 2d 498; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5533; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1053



April 22, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 17, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Circuit Court for Polk County; Dennis P. Maloney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted; order quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought certiorari review of an order of the Circuit Court of Polk County (Florida), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss a charge of failure to return leased equipment, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 812.155 (2001), but which held that ch. 812.155(4)(b) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with a violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 812.155(3). The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charge. However, it found that ch. 812.155(4)(b) created a mandatory presumption that relieved the State of its burden to prove fraudulent intent, which was an essential element of the offense. The trial court held that ch. 812.155(4)(b) was unconstitutional, as it violated the due process clauses of the U.S. and Florida Constitutions. On appeal, the court held that pursuant to Florida judicial precedent, the language of ch. 812.155(4)(b) was construed to create a permissive inference, not a mandatory presumption. The court found that the trial court departed from the essential requirements of the law when it reached the opposite conclusion. On remand, the trial court was to determine whether the presumed fact of a fraudulent intent was rationally connected to the proven fact of defendant's failure to return the property within five days of receipt of a demand for the return.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition and quashed the order of the trial court. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1731 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Parrish v. Pier Club Apts., LLC


CASE NO. 4D03-2458


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


900 So. 2d 683; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5440; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 1014



April 20, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 6, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Ilona M. Holmes, Judge; L.T. Case No. 00-16410 (18).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayer petitioned the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), to challenge appellant county property appraiser's denial of an ad valorem tax exemption under Fla. Stat. ch. 296.1978 (2000) to the taxpayer. The trial court found that the taxpayer was entitled to the exemption. The appraiser appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer purchased an apartment complex that provided affordable housing to low and very low income tenants. The purchase was financed through public housing revenue bonds. As a condition of the funding, the taxpayer entered into a Land Use Restriction Agreement (LURA) with the county housing finance authority. The LURA required that by a set date, 20 percent of the apartment units would be occupied by very low income tenants and an additional 55 percent by low income tenants. The remaining 25 percent were available for rent to the general public. The taxpayer took the position that if a unit was previously occupied by a low or very low income tenant but vacant on January 1st, the unit applied towards the Fla. Stat. ch. 196.1978 exemption. The appraiser argued that January 1st was the only relevant date and that if a unit was not occupied by a low or very low income tenant on January 1st, then the unit was not being used to provide affordable housing. On appeal, the court found that the taxpayer was not entitled to the affordable housing exemption as the occupancy of a unit by a low or very low income tenant on January 1st was necessary to trigger the ch. 196.1978 exemption.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1732 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Anderson Columbia v. Brown


CASE NO. 1D04-3963


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


902 So. 2d 838; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 4954; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 949



April 12, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 29, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Anderson Columbia & Commer. Risk Mgmt. Inc. v. Brown, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9861 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., May 31, 2005)Released for Publication June 16, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Certiorari - Original Jurisdiction.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of certiorari is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners employer and insurer brought an original action against respondent worker, seeking certiorari relief from an order of the Judge of Compensation Claims (JCC) compelling disclosure of the hourly fee paid to, and the total hours expended by, an attorney representing the employer and the insurer in the underlying workers' compensation case.


OVERVIEW: The worker argued that he needed the information to support a constitutional challenge on appeal to Fla. Stat. ch. 440.34(7) (2003). The worker asserted, inter alia, that the statutory cap on attorney's fees was a denial of due process and equal protection since employers and carriers were able to engage in excessive litigation to discourage representation of injured workers with low value claims. The court found that the challenged order compelled only disclosure of the rate charged by defense counsel and the hours expended. Counsel was not required to reveal information containing descriptions of the services. A bare accounting of hours worked and rates charged did not provide any insight into counsel's thought processes, and so did not violate the work product privilege. There was no showing of how the disclosure had any chilling effect on communication regarding the client's circumstances or its legal rights and obligations, so there was no violation of the attorney-client privilege. The information was relevant to the anticipated constitutional challenge. There was no showing that the JCC departed from the essential requirements of law in compelling the limited disclosure.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

1733 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. State


CASE NO. 4D03-1379


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


901 So. 2d 213; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 4659; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 907



April 6, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 22, 2005.
Review denied by Anderson v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1870 (Fla., Aug. 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Alfred J. Horowitz, Judge; L.T. Case No. 02-4716 CF 10A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County, Florida, convicted defendant of escape, battery on a law enforcement officer, resisting arrest with violence, and petit theft, and sentenced him as a habitual offender and a prison releasee reoffender under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084. Defendant appealed the habitual offender sentencing claiming he had inadequate notice of the State's intent to seek that sentence.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a notice of intent to declare defendant a habitual offender pursuant to ch. 775.084 shortly after charges were filed. The notice advised him that the State was seeking designation as a habitual felony offender, a habitual violent felony offender, a three-time violent felony offender, and/or a violent career criminal. The notice was not too general. That type of "shotgun" notice had previously been upheld and was valid. Defendant received that notice almost a full year before trial. The notice's language put defendant on guard as to the potential sentencing against him. Defendant knew he had been released from prison less than one year before he engaged in the new crimes charged against him. Defendant also knew the nature of the pending charges. Therefore, the notice was adequate. The notice did not violate Apprendi v. New Jersey.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment.

 

1734 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Best v. Lakeland Reg'l Med. Ctr.


Case No. 2D04-3009


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


899 So. 2d 424; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 4482; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 879



April 1, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 13, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Harvey A. Kornstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a final summary judgment by the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) entered in favor of appellee hospital. Because the hospital's alleged malpractice occurred no later than 1993, noting that appellant did not file suit until 2002, the trial court concluded that the four-year statute of repose contained in Fla. Stat. ch. 95.11(4)(b) applied, barring his claims.


OVERVIEW: After treatment at the hospital, appellant suffered what an expert opined were radiation burns. Appellant first argued that the record supported a claim for ordinary negligence. The appeals court disagreed. The record established that his injury occurred in connection with medical diagnosis, treatment, and care provided by health care providers. Second, appellant contended that he did not learn he had been injured as a result of excess radiation exposure until 2001. He asserted that if the statute of repose was applied, then his cause of action was extinguished before he knew of his injury and before his cause of action accrued. The Florida Supreme Court had held that the statutory repose period for medical malpractice actions did not violate the constitutional mandate of access to courts, even when applied to a cause of action which did not accrue until after the period had expired. Based on the controlling precedent, the appeals court concluded that the trial court properly entered summary judgment in favor of the hospital.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Schwenn v. State


CASE NO. 4D03-2171


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


898 So. 2d 1130; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 4342; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 864



March 30, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Peter M. Weinstein, Judge; L.T. Case No. 02-5205 CF10A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), that convicted him of eight counts of armed sexual battery, one count of burglary with a battery, one count of false imprisonment, and one count of battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of eight counts of armed sexual battery, one count of burglary with a battery, one count of false imprisonment, and one count of battery. On appeal, he claimed that the eight sexual battery charges violated double jeopardy because there was no spatial or temporal break between the acts alleged in the counts. The court disagreed because defendant committed different acts of sexual battery that were distinct from one another and temporally separated. Even though there were three events of vaginal penetration and three of anal penetration, each was separated from a similar event by another type of sexual battery. Thus, they were distinct in character and temporally separated, which gave defendant sufficient time between each penetration to reflect and form a new criminal intent. The court also found no double jeopardy violation in defendant's convictions for both burglary with a battery and battery. The burglary with a battery involved the sexual battery, while the separate battery charge consisted of other conduct of touching the victim's breasts and kissing her against her will. The battery was for conduct separate and apart from the sexual battery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. Ratner


No. 4D04-2513


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 4678; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 851



March 30, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Ratner, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 8174 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Mar. 30, 2005)
Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, On rehearing at State v. Ratner, 902 So. 2d 267, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 7401 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., May 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of a non-final order from the County Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Sheree Davis Cunningham, Judge; L.T. Case No. 03-14582 MMA02.



DISPOSITION: Appeal transferred.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a non-final order of the County Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County (Florida), which denied the State's motion in limine. The county court certified a question for review, as one of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: The court held that it needed to dismiss the appeal because the court did not have jurisdiction to review the type of non-final order of the county court that certified a question of great public importance. Fla. Const. art. V, § 4(b), and Fla. R. App. P. 9.030(b)(4) only allowed the court to review those non-final orders of a county court that were appealable to the circuit court under Fla. R. App. P. 9.140(c). The county court's order denying a motion in limine was not such an order that would have been appealable under Rule 9.140(c). The court rejected the State's contention that Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07(1)(h) or (l) made the order reviewable by the court, because those provisions of Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07 cited by the sState had not been adopted by Rule 9.140(c). The court did find, pursuant to Fla. Const. art. V, § 5(b) and Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07(1)(h), that the circuit court had jurisdiction to hear the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction. The court transferred the matter to the circuit court.

State v. Hanna


Case No. 5D03-4109


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


901 So. 2d 201; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 3952; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 816



March 24, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 16, 2005.
Rehearing denied by State v. Hanna, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 7838 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Apr. 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Stan Strickland, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Florida charged defendant in the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), with racketeering, conspiracy to commit racketeering, operating an organized scheme to defraud, filing a false or fraudulent tax return, grand theft, sale of obscene material, and four counts of operating an unlicensed adult book store. The trial court dismissed the four counts of operating an unlicensed adult book store. The State of Florida appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant arose from the operation of a business, which the State alleged was an unlicensed adult book store. Defendant moved to dismiss the charges, contending that the definition of "adult book store" in the Orange County, Florida, Adult Entertainment Code was unconstitutionally vague, and that the code failed to provide for prompt judicial review in the event an application for an adult entertainment license was denied. Finding merit in the arguments, the trial court dismissed the four counts of operating an unlicensed adult book store. On appeal, the court found that the definition of adult book store found in Orange County, Fla., Code § 3-6 (2002) was not unconstitutionally vague. Further, any ambiguity in the meaning of the terms as applied in the code was readily subject to a narrowing construction by the Florida courts. Finally, while under the code neither a direct appeal, nor certiorari review was available to an unsuccessful adult entertainment license applicant, an original action brought in the circuit court for a declaratory judgment under Fla. Stat. ch. 86.021 (2004) provided judicial review sufficient to pass constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed, and the matter was remanded with directions that the four counts of operating an unlicensed adult book store be reinstated.

Staten v. Gonzalez-Falla


CASE NO.: 1D03-5185


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 3592; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 770



March 17, 2005, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Motion granted by Staten v. Gonzalez-Falla, 904 So. 2d 498, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 7276 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., May 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Madison County. Thomas J. Kennon, Jr., Judge.
Staten v. Gonzalez-Falla, 855 So. 2d 247, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 14559 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2003)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Madison County (Florida) granted a statutory way of necessity to petitioner, a property owner, over property owned by respondent, an estate, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 704.01(2). The personal representative of the estate appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The property owner alleged that he needed the way of necessity in order to use his landlocked property for timber raising, for agricultural purposes, and for dwellings. The estate claimed that the owner had been allowed to use the road across the property, and had created a nuisance by leasing the property to a hunt club whose tenants were loud and annoying at all hours of the day and night and used the property in an unsanitary and unhealthy manner. The trial court denied the estate's request to limit the use of the way of necessity in order to exclude the hunters. The appellate court held that when Fla. Stat. chs. 704.01(2) and 704.04 were read in pari materia, it was clear that the legislature had permitted a statutory way of necessity for only those uses which were enumerated in Fla. Stat. ch. 704.01(2), specifically for a dwelling or dwellings, agricultural, timber raising or cutting or stock raising purposes. Thus, the appellate court held that the trial court erred in failing to restrict the use of the easement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Humana Med. Plan, Inc. v. State


CASE NO.: 1D04-1855


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


898 So. 2d 1040; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 3456; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 765



March 16, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 1, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Janet E. Ferris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant managed health care company challenged a summary final judgment from the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida), which was in favor of appellee, the Florida Agency for Health Care Administration (AHCA), and which ruled that Fla. Stat. ch. 409.9122(13) (2003) was a general law and not a special or local law that would be subject to the notice requirements of Fla. Const. art. III, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Due to the enactment of Fla. Stat. ch. 409.9122(13), which required the AHCA to adjust enrollee assignments for Medicaid-managed prepaid plans operating in a certain county, the company suffered a significant loss of Medicaid-eligible assignments. The company filed a complaint alleging that ch. 409.9122(13) was unconstitutional because it was a local law that was enacted without compliance with the notice requirements of Fla. Const. art. III, § 10. On counter-motions for summary judgment, the trial court ruled that the statute was constitutional, and it entered final summary judgment for the AHCA. The company appealed. The court found that while the statute, on its face, applied only to one county, it was a general law that was not subject to constitutional notice requirements because it had a material statewide impact on the state's Medicaid program. Fla. Stat. ch. 409.9122(13) was enacted as part of a statewide program. Also, due to the significant size of the Medicaid population in the county affected by the statute, the legislature could have reasonably determined that restructuring there would impact the Medicaid program on a statewide basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment ruling in the AHCA's favor.

Behl v. State


Case No. 2D03-184


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


898 So. 2d 217; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 3546; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 733



March 16, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Nancy Moate Ley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions and designation affirmed; sentences affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) of one count of sexual battery on a child under the age of 12 years and two counts of sexual battery by a person in familial or custodial authority as well as designated as a sexual predator. The court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment for the first offense and concurrent terms of 337.5 months for the other offenses. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentences for the two first-degree felony sexual battery by a person in familial or custodial authority offenses far exceeded the applicable maximum sentence under the Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.991(a) sentencing guidelines scoresheet absent points for penetration. He contended that the trial court's determination, in enhancing the sentence, that penetration occurred violated the Sixth Amendment under the Apprendi rule. The State of Florida countered that, in finding defendant guilty, the jury necessarily concluded that penetration occurred. On appeal, the court found that, while the jury found that sexual penetration occurred regarding one of the sexual battery by a person in familial or custodial authority offenses, the jury's verdict finding defendant guilty of the other sexual battery by a person in familial or custodial authority offense did not, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(1)(h) (1997), embody a factual determination by the jury that the offense involved sexual penetration. Therefore, the sentences imposed for those two convictions violated defendant's Sixth amendment right to trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the sexual predator designation; the court affirmed defendant's life sentence for the capital felony of sexual battery on a child under the age of 12 years; the court reversed defendant's sentences for first-degree felony of sexual battery by a person in familial or custodial authority; and the court remanded the case for resentencing utilizing a corrected scoresheet.

Schindler v. Schiavo (In re Schiavo)


Case No. 2D05-968


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


916 So. 2d 814; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 3574; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 743



March 16, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Injunction denied by, Writ of habeas corpus denied Schiavo ex rel. Schiavo v. Greer, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 4182 (M.D. Fla., Mar. 18, 2005)
Motion dismissed by, Sub nomine at Fla. Dep't of Children & Families v. Schiavo, 900 So. 2d 553, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 577 (Fla., Mar. 24, 2005)
Subsequent appeal at Dep't of Children & Family Servs. v. Schiavo (In re Schiavo), 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 4362 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Mar. 30, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; George W. Greer, Judge.
Bush v. Schiavo, 885 So. 2d 321, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1539 (Fla., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; motion for stay denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Pinellas County, Florida, ordered a hospice facility to cease supplying nutrition and hydration to an incapacitated person. Appellants, the parents of the incapacitated person (daughter), filed a motion for relief from judgment pursuant to Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.540(b)(4). The trial court denied the motion; the parents appealed and filed a motion for a stay pending appeal. Appellee guardian was also involved in the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that clear and convincing evidence established that the daughter, who had suffered a heart attack, was in a persistent vegetative state and that, if able to do so, would have elected to forego the use of a feeding tube. It ordered that nutrition and hydration no longer be provided. In response to that order, the state legislature passed an act pursuant to which the governor ordered a stay of the order. The Florida Supreme Court found the act to be unconstitutional. A guardian appointed at the request of the governor opined that the daughter's movements were merely reflexive and that she was in persistent vegetative state. The instant court rejected the parents' claim that the judgment was void for lack of jurisdiction. The trial court was empowered under Fla. Stat. ch. 765.401(3) to determine what the daughter would have decided in light of her persistent vegetative state, and the procedures followed did not violate her right to due process or privacy. The parents were allowed to present evidence as they were guardians and were allowed, contrary to precedent, to file successive and repetitive Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.540(b) motions, none of which had merit.


OUTCOME: The order denying the motion was affirmed; the parents' motion for a stay was denied.

City of Tampa v. McAfee


Case No. 2D04-3870


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


896 So. 2d 943; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 3056; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 655



March 9, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 15, 2005. Released for Publication March 29, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from nonfinal order of the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Herbert J. Baumann, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee arrestee sued appellant city, challenging the legality and constitutionality of Tampa, Fla., Code § 14-27 (2002), which allowed police to impound a vehicle upon probable cause to believe it was used to facilitate drug crimes or prostitution. The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County, Florida, granted the arrestee's motions for summary judgment, class certification, and a preliminary injunction. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city claimed it impounded the arrestee's car after an accident, found marijuana in an inventory search, charged him with possession, and impounded his car under § 14-27. He paid a bond for the release of the car and towing and storage charges. After a hearing master found probable cause, the arrestee forfeited these funds. He argued that § 14-27 was preempted by the Florida Contraband Forfeiture Act, Fla. Stat. chs. 932.701-.707 (2003), and violated due process. The appellate court held it could not review the non-final order granting summary judgment, and that, based on district court precedent, the injunction was properly granted. However, the order certifying a class of all owners of vehicles impounded under the ordinance was defective as it did not contain the findings of fact required by Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220(d)(1) and the trial court had no testimony or affidavits to permit it to enter adequate factual determinations. The trial court did not give sufficient consideration to the arrestee's adequacy as class representative and the disturbing effect on persons once accused of drug or prostitution crimes of having opt-out notification mailed to their homes under Rule 1.220.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the temporary injunction, but reversed the order granting the motion for class certification and remanded for further consideration of that motion.

Wiccan Religious Coop. of Fla., Inc. v. Zingale


CASE NO. 1D03-3324


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


898 So. 2d 134; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 2932; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 651



March 8, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 2, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Wiccan Religious Coop. of Fla., Inc. v. Zingale, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6759 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Apr. 14, 2005)
Review granted by Wiccan Religious Coop. of Fla., Inc. v. Zingale, 915 So. 2d 1198, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2390 (Fla., 2005)
Dismissed by Wiccan Religious Coop. of Fla. v. Zingale, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2531 (Fla., Oct. 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Honorable P. Kevin Davey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant religious cooperative brought an action against appellee department of revenue, challenging, inter alia, Fla. Stat. ch. 212.06(9) and alleging that it was improperly denied a renewal of its certificate of exemption from state sales and use tax. The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) granted the department's motion for summary judgment. The religious cooperative appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the religious cooperative had standing and that Fla. Stat. ch. 212.06(9) was constitutional. The trial court also ruled that the religious cooperative failed to exhaust its administrative remedies regarding obtaining a renewal of its certificate of exemption. As part of its response, the department argued that the religious cooperative was without standing to bring its challenge. The appellate court found that the religious cooperative, as a religious organization, benefited from the sales tax exemption. Accordingly, the religious cooperative failed to have the adverse interest necessary for standing and was not the proper party to assert the instant constitutional challenge. Both parties briefed the standing issue without objection. Furthermore, standing was argued, almost exclusively, during oral argument without objection. Accordingly, the issue was before the appellate court and it was not barred from considering standing, despite the fact that the trial court's standing determination was not cross-appealed by the department.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court with directions to enter final summary judgment in favor of the department on the basis that the religious cooperative did not have standing.

Delorme v. State


Case Nos. 5D04-594, 5D04-596, 5D04-597, 5D04-598, 5D04-599

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three defendants, who had entered into nolo contendere pleas, appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida) which denied a motion to dismiss the information charging them with keeping a gambling house. Defendants alleged that Fla. Stat. chs. 849.01 and 849.15 were unconstitutionally vague when read in conjunction with Fla. Stat. ch. 849.161(1)(a)1.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were all represented by the same counsel, entered pleas of not guilty, and filed identical motions to dismiss the information pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.190(c)(4). The trial court denied defendants' motions to dismiss and agreed that its ruling had the effect of rendering the seized machines illegal under Florida Statutes. The appellate court began by noting that the bulk of defendants' arguments had been recently rejected. Also, Fla. Stat. chs. 849.01, 849.15 and 849.161 were not impermissibly vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

R.K. v. Dep't of Children & Families

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida), which terminated her parental rights pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 39.806(1)(c), (i).


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the mother had admitted that she had a 15-year history of drug abuse and criminal activity. The appellate court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in terminating the mother's parental rights where the mother demonstrated that the risk of future neglect was high, considering her past conduct and her current conduct.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

Schultz v. Time Warner Entm't Co.

Dep't of Children & Families v. Fellows


Case No. 5D03-3261


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


895 So. 2d 1181; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1672; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 496



February 18, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 9, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lake County, Mark J. Hill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of children and families filed a shelter petition for a child and his sibling. After placement of the child with appellee aunt in New Hampshire was unsuccessful, the department sought placement in Florida. The Circuit Court for Lake County (Florida) ordered that the child be returned to the aunt's custody in New Hampshire and terminated supervision of the child. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The department argued that the trial court violated the Interstate Compact on the Placement of Children (ICPC), Fla. Stat. ch. 409.401 (2001), by returning the child to the aunt over the opposition of the New Hampshire authorities. Florida initially placed the child in New Hampshire with the aunt after it received a positive home study as required by Fla. Stat. ch. 409.401 art. III(d) (2001). However, New Hampshire subsequently recommended that the child be returned to Florida because it was believed that the aunt could no longer meet the child's needs. In essence, New Hampshire rescinded its placement approval. Florida retained jurisdiction, and the child was returned to the department's custody in Florida. The appellate court held that the ICPC applied to the aunt, and that the trial court had no authority to return the child to New Hampshire without a reapplication of Fla. Stat. ch. 409.401 art. III(d) (2001).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

Paresky v. Miami-Dade County Bd. of County Comm'rs


CASE NO. 3D04-1479


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


893 So. 2d 664; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1627; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 462



February 16, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 4, 2005. As Corrected February 18, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Maxine Cohen Lando, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 03-11139.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Miami-Dade County (Florida), entered a judgment that granted defendant government entities' motions to dismiss and for partial summary judgment after plaintiff former litigant filed a two-count complaint seeking declaratory relief regarding parking non-use variances that were approved pursuant to an ordinance, which was a matter he had litigated and lost several years earlier. On appeal, the appellate court found that the challenge to the constitutionality of the county ordinance was barred by the four-year statute of limitations applicable to declaratory judgment actions and the challenge to the omissions of the variances from the resolution was barred by the doctrine of collateral estoppel.

Hilton v. State


CASE NO. 2D02-5346


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


901 So. 2d 155; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1646; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 453



February 16, 2005, Decided  
February 16, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 14, 2005.
Later proceeding at Hilton v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2115 (Fla., Mar. 17, 2005)
Review granted by Hilton v. State, 919 So. 2d 435, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 25 (Fla., 2006)
Quashed by, Remanded by, Certified question answered by Hilton v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1196 (Fla., July 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Mark I. Shames, Judge.
Hilton v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 8555 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., June 18, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest to possession of marijuana after the Circuit Court for Pinellas County, Florida, denied his dispositive motion to suppress. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police stopped defendant's car after noticing that it had a seven-inch crack in the passenger's side of its windshield; they intended to issue him a traffic citation for the cracked windshield. Upon stopping the vehicle, however, they observed a gun in plain view. The resulting search of the car produced over 40 bags of marijuana. The appellate court held that because a windshield was required by Fla. Stat. ch. 316.2952, it was a violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.610 to drive a vehicle with a windshield that was not in proper condition and adjustment. Ch. 316.610(1) expressly authorized an officer to stop and inspect a vehicle if the officer had reasonable cause to believe that it was not equipped as required by law. Therefore, whether the crack created any immediate hazard was immaterial. Ch. 316.610(1) did not violate the Fourth Amendment because owners and operators of cars were expected to know the legal requirements for vehicle equipment and could not expect their sense of personal privacy to prevent police from briefly stopping a car that reasonably appeared to have an equipment violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1752 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nichols


CASE NO. 1D04-4287


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


892 So. 2d 1221; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1441; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 446



February 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 3, 2005. As Corrected March 4, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the County Court for Franklin County. Van P. Russell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The County Court for Franklin County (Florida) ruled that Fla. Stat. ch. 370.093(2)(b) (2000), which penalized the unlawful use of a grill or entangling net made of monofilament, was unconstitutionally vague and unenforceable under Fla. Const. art. V, § 4(b)(1). Thus, both defendants' convictions and sentences were vacated. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county court concluded that Fla. Stat. ch. 370.093(2)(b) was unconstitutionally vague for failure to give reasonable notice of the conduct it prohibited. The appeals court first held that the validity of the statute turned on whether it was unconstitutionally vague because the term "monofilament" was ambiguous. The appeals court held that it was not, as the dictionary definition of the term as a single untwisted synthetic filament made in varying diameters for use in textiles, hosiery, and screens or as bristles, fishing lines, and sutures was neither obscure or perplexing as applied in the statute. Further, the term had a fixed and definite meaning. Thus, the statute was not so vague that persons of ordinary intelligence must guess at its meaning, it was sufficiently clear to allow reasonable and uniform enforcement, and defendants had adequate notice of the statute and what it prohibited. Finally, because the State presented direct evidence that defendants were using a net to fish, and adequate, circumstantial evidence that the net used was not the legal net on deck, defendants were not entitled to an acquittal, even if Fla. Stat. ch. 370.093(2)(b) (2000) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the convictions and fines imposed were reinstated.

Fla. Dep't of Educ. v. NYT Mgmt. Servs.


CASE NO. 1D04-2707


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


895 So. 2d 1151; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1430; 33 Media L. Rep. 1317; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 434



February 14, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 5, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Fla. Dep't of Educ. v. NI/T Mgmt. Servs., 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 5737 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Mar. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Honorable Nikki Ann Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee newspaper sought disclosure of Florida teachers' social security numbers through public records requests. The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) ruled that appellants, the Florida Department of Education (DOE) and its Commissioner, did not fully comply with the newspaper's requests and that the information the newspaper sought in its 2003 and 2004 requests constituted public record with no applicable statutory exemption.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the DOE argued that it was not required to produce social security numbers in response to the newspaper's April 2004 request for updated and historical data because the request was not verified as Florida law required. The appellate court agreed. The newspaper's April 2004 requests were not verified as required by Fla. Stat. ch. 119.0721(3). In addition, the DOE argued that although applicants for certification were required to submit social security numbers, disclosure of those numbers was expressly limited to the administration of child support enforcement pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 1012.56(1) (2003). The appellate court concluded that because the newspaper's request did not further the program of enforcing child support obligations, locating noncustodial parents, establishing paternity, or obtaining child support, the DOE properly denied the request. Finally, the DOE had provided data from the staff database pursuant to the June and September 2003 requests, including social security numbers, but the data omitted information for two counties. The DOE was required to produce the same information for these two counties.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed in part as to the June and September 2003 requests, but was reversed in part as to all other requests.

In re Mullin


Case No. 2D04-2313


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


892 So. 2d 1214; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1390; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 413



February 11, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 2, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Mary Catherine Green, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida), which denied his petition under Fla. Stat. ch. 68.07 (2003) for a change of name.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought a name change, alleging that he was convicted of a felony in 1980, that he sought to change his name in accordance with his religious beliefs, and that he had no illegal or ulterior motive in seeking such a name change. After a telephonic hearing, the circuit court, citing Fla. Stat. ch. 68.07, denied the petition. The circuit court found that, under ch. 68.07(2)(k), a petition for name change had to be denied if the petitioner was a convicted felon and had not had have his civil rights restored. On appeal of that denial, petitioner contended that denying his petition was error because his felony conviction occurred before the effective date of ch. 68.07(2)(k) and thus that paragraph did not apply. The court agreed. There was no indication that the 1995 amendment at 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 283, § 1 that added Fla. Stat. ch. 68.07(2)(k) applied retroactively. Because petitioner's felony conviction occurred in 1980, which was before the effective date of ch. 68.07(2)(k), the trial court erred when it retroactively applied that section to the name change petition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the name change petition and the court remanded for further proceedings.

 

1755 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Amber Glades, Inc. v. Leisure Assocs. Ltd. P'ship


Case No. 2D04-1884


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


893 So. 2d 620; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1360; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 379



February 9, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from nonfinal order of the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Crockett Farnell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On behalf of all mobile homeowners in a park, appellant mobile homeowners' association sued appellee park owners. The Circuit Court for Pinellas County, Florida, certified a class, designated the association as class representative, required notification of the class, and allowed class members out. The notice had to caution the homeowners that they could be liable for attorneys' fees if the association did not prevail. The association appealed.


OVERVIEW: The association alleged the park did not enforce rules barring people under 55 from living there or rules restricting pets. Under Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.222, mobile homeowners' associations could file suits on behalf of all mobile homeowners without complying with the requirements for general class action suits in Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.220. The appellate court noted that Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.222 did not specify what procedures had to be followed. Under Fla. Stat. ch. 723.075 (2003), only two-thirds of the mobile homeowners in a park had to join a mobile homeowners' association. Although neither party appealed the certification of a class consisting of all mobile homeowners in the park as of a certain date, the appellate court was concerned that the association might be unable to represent the interests of owners with pets or who were under 55. Whether owners who did not opt out of the suit could be liable for attorneys' fees was also unclear. However, these issues were not ripe for review. The trial court had discretion to enter the order requiring notice to all affected mobile homeowners of the action, in the absence of more specific procedures in Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.222.


OUTCOME: The appellate court approved the trial court's decision to notify the mobile homeowners of the lawsuit and expressed no opinion on the content of that notification. It granted the owners' motion for appellate attorneys' fees, contingent upon their prevailing in the trial court, only against the association and not against the mobile homeowners because they were not parties and had not been formally noticed concerning the appeal.

Williams v. State


Case No. 5D03-1114


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


892 So. 2d 1185; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1021; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 355



February 4, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 24, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Volusia County, Joseph G. Will, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Volusia County (Florida), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of lewd and lascivious battery on a person 12 years of age or older but less than 16 years of age. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 24-year-old male, was accused of having intercourse with a 14-year-old girl. She later identified defendant to police as the person with whom she had intercourse. Thereafter, at his workplace, defendant agreed to talk with a detective. They spoke in the detective's car. The detective secretly recorded the conversation. The detective then told defendant two falsehoods, to the effect that the victim was claiming forcible rape and that the detective had forensic evidence of a sexual encounter between the victim and defendant. The detective invited defendant to tell "his side of the story" and defendant admitted having sex with the victim. At trial, defendant's counsel did not move to suppress the confession. Defendant was convicted. On appeal, defendant claimed the confession was coerced and the admission of it was fundamental error. The appellate court found that any error in admitting it was not fundamental, and, therefore, that issue was not cognizable on appeal. It so concluded because it found that, even though, defendant had not raised the issue in the trial court, the guilty verdict could have been obtained even without the assistance of the alleged error.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Menuto


Case No. 2D03-4838


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 1024; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 358



February 4, 2005, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Rehearing denied by, Rehearing denied by, En banc, Motion denied by State v. Menuto, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6457 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., May 4, 2005)
Substituted opinion at, Remanded by State v. Menuto, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 6454 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., May 4, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Brandt C. Downey, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss an information alleging he violated Fla. Stat. ch. 790.23 (2002) by unlawfully possessing a firearm.


OVERVIEW: By information the State alleged that defendant violated Fla. Stat. ch. 790.23(1)(b) because he was under 24 years old, in possession of a firearm, and was found to have committed the delinquent act of felony burglary while a juvenile. The trial court dismissed the information after finding the statute was unconstitutional. The State appealed. The court rejected defendant's contentions that the statute violated either due process or equal protection, that the statute was vague, or that ch. 790.23(1)(b) required an adjudication of delinquency (AD) and his AD was withheld. The statute properly distinguished between adults convicted of a felony and juveniles found to have committed delinquent acts that would be a felony for an adult because there were fundamental differences between criminal adult proceedings and juvenile proceedings. Under the rational relationship test, both procedural due process and equal protection were satisfied. Because defendant's conduct fell squarely within ch. 790.23(1)(b), the statute was not vague. Finally, there was no basis to read beyond the plain meaning of ch. 790.23(1)(b), which encompassed juveniles whose AD was withheld.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing the information and remanded for further proceedings.

Whipple v. Dep't of Corr.


CASE NO. 3D03-2877


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


892 So. 2d 554; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 966; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 333



February 2, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Whipple v. Dep't of Corr., 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 2647 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Feb. 2, 2005)
Review denied by Whipple v. Fla. Dep't of Corr., 909 So. 2d 863, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1627 (Fla., July 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Stuart M. Simons, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 01-16368.
Whipple v. Dep't of Corr., 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 19636 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Dec. 22, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former penal inmate sued appellee state corrections department in the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida), for false imprisonment. The trial court granted the corrections department's motion for summary judgment. The former inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The former inmate claimed that he was imprisoned by the corrections department longer than his court-imposed sentences in three unrelated cases. He argued that the corrections department held him after the expiration of one sentence, and then made no attempt to ascertain the intent of a sentencing judge where there was confusion about the concurrent and coterminous language of another one of his three sentences as to which of the other sentences the concurrent and coterminous language applied. On appeal, the court found that the corrections department properly treated the concurrent and coterminous language of one of the former inmate's sentences as a nullity. The corrections department then had before it an otherwise valid sentence, which did not mention the former inmate's other sentence. Under the circumstances, the corrections department was then required to run the sentence consecutive to the former inmate's remaining sentence pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 921.16(1) (1995). Further, the rule of lenity, under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.021 (1988), had no applicability. Finally, there was no violation of the separation of powers doctrine under Fla. Const. art. II, § 3.


OUTCOME: The order of summary judgment was affirmed.

Kerper v. Dep't of Envtl. Prot.


Case No. 5D04-1182


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


894 So. 2d 1006; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 188; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 215



January 14, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 21, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Kerper v. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 4495 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Mar. 2, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Administrative Appeal from the Department of Environmental Protection.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the judgment of appellee Florida Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) which found it liable for failing to clean up used oil discharges. The corporation argued, inter alia, that the finding by and administrative law judge (ALJ) that he discharged oil was not supported by competent, substantial evidence.


OVERVIEW: The corporation operated an auto parts salvage operation on some land owned by the land owner. After discovering environmental problems on the property, the corporation extricated itself from an agreement to purchase the property. The DEP subsequently inspected the property. The land owner told DEP inspectors that the corporation was responsible for a 55 gallon drum that was tipped over and leaking what appeared to be used oil. The inspection also revealed other unlabeled drums, containers, oil filters, battery casings, and areas of dark-stained soil in the area where the corporation had operated. The ALJ found the corporation failed to respond to used oil discharges. The court held that the only direct evidence presented by DEP that the corporation was responsible was the objected-to hearsay testimony of the land owner. There was no evidence regarding the age of the spills. Thus, DEP failed to present competent substantial evidence that the corporation was responsible for the discharges. In addition, DEP's policy of requiring a person cited to conduct testing to prove his innocence improperly shifted the burden of proof. The DEP lacked authority to impose an unpromulgated rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the DEP was reversed.

 

1760 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Phantom of Clearwater, Inc. v. Pinellas County


Case No. 2D03-5408


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


894 So. 2d 1011; 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 184; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 205



January 14, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 29, 2005. Rehearing denied by Phantom of Clearwater v. Pinellas County, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 9055 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Mar. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; W. Douglas Baird, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fireworks seller challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida), which dismissed its action seeking a declaration that appellee county's ordinance restricting the sale of fireworks under Pinellas, Fla. County Ordinance 03-48 (ordinance) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The seller objected to the ordinance, arguing it was unconstitutional because it was preempted by Fla. Stat. ch. 791 (2003) either expressly or by implication. In the alternative, it argued that the ordinance, or portions of it, facially conflicted with ch. 791. When the seller's declaratory judgment action was dismissed, the seller appealed. The court found that ch. 791 contained no express preemption and the statute was not so pervasive to justify implied preemption. As to conflict, one sentence in the ordinance, § 2, conflicted with Fla. Stat. ch. 791.06 (2003) because it imposed additional fines or terms of imprisonment to what were proper penalties for violating Fla. Stat. ch. 791.06. However, the ordinance, § 7, allowed any part that was found unconstitutional to be severed from the rest of the ordinance. A person or entity could comply with the requirements of the ordinance without violating ch. 791, and vice versa. While the ordinance imposed additional burdens on those engaged in the fireworks business in the county, the additional burdens were not prohibited by ch. 791. The burdens supplemented, rather than contradicted, ch. 791.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment only to the extent of holding that one sentence of the ordinance that conflicted with a state statute was unconstitutional and had to be severed from the ordinance. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects and remanded the case.

 

1761 of 2516 DOCUMENTS

State v. Monroe

1763 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


River Place Condo. Ass'n at Ellenton, Inc. v. Benzing


Case No. 2D04-1489


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


890 So. 2d 386; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 19516; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 14



December 22, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 11, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Manatee County; Paul E. Logan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Manatee County (Florida) entered final summary judgment determining that defendant owners were the proper owners of lands formerly submerged beneath the Manatee River and subsequently exposed by dredge and fill activities. Plaintiff, a condominium association, appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The association argued that it was the proper owner under Fla. Stat. ch. 253.12(9) (2003), because it was the record owner of the property immediately upland of the filled lands. In the alternative, the association argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 253.12(9) (2003) was unconstitutional. The owners argued that they were the proper owners under Fla. Stat. ch. 253.12(9) (2003) because they were the record title holders of the filled lands. Fla. Stat. ch. 53.12(9) divested the State of its ownership of lands filled before July 1, 1975. A developer recorded a quit claim deed to the filled land in question prior to the effective date of the statute, and the land was subsequently transferred to the owners. The appellate court held that the developer's quit claim deed became effective with the enactment of Fla. Stat. ch. 253.12(9) (2003). It was clear from the record that the deed to the developer was prepared and filed in good faith, and was not an attempt to steal land from the State. As the developer's successor in interest, the owners thus were the proper owners of the land. The appellate court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 253.12(9) (2003) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1764 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Whipple v. Dep't of Corr.


CASE NO. 3D03-2877


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 19636; 30 Fla. L. Weekly D 53



December 22, 2004, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Whipple v. Dep't of Corr., 892 So. 2d 554, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 966 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Feb. 2, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Stuart M. Simons, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NO. 01-16368.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former inmate sued defendant Florida Department of Corrections (DOC) in the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) for negligence and false imprisonment for allegedly imprisoning him for longer than his court-imposed sentences. The inmate and DOC each moved for summary judgment, and the trial court granted DOC's motion and denied that of the inmate. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate received three sentences at various times. The last sentence was to be concurrent with the first, but the first was served when the last was imposed, and the last sentence did not mention the second sentence. The appellate court held the Department of Corrections (DOC) correctly gave no effect to the concurrent language in the last sentence. Because the last sentence did not mention the second sentence, Fla. Stat. ch. 921.16(1) (1995) required the last sentence to be consecutive to the second. A failure to implement concurrent language of the last sentence did not violate separation of powers in Fla. Const. art. II, § 3 as that language was a nullity. The last sentence did not have to be construed in the inmate's favor, under the rule of lenity, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.021(1) (1988), because instead of being ambiguous, the sentence's concurrent language had no effect. As the sentencing court's stated no intent that the last sentence be concurrent to the second, DOC statutorily had to run it consecutively to the second sentence, and the rule of lenity did not apply. Double jeopardy was not violated as the sentences were for different crimes in different cases.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1765 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


CASE NO. 1D03-2620


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


892 So. 2d 518; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 19104



December 15, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Review dismissed by Davis v. State, 895 So. 2d 404, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 277 (Fla., 2005)
Review dismissed by State v. Davis, 902 So. 2d 792, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1032 (Fla., Apr. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Alachua County. Judge Peter J. Sieg.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part, REVERSED in part, and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Alachua County (Florida), which convicted defendant of burglary, aggravated, battery, and false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On the burglary charge, the trial court charged on the "remaining in" portion of the burglary instruction. Under the Delgado decision, the facts in the case did not support that portion of the instruction. Thus, defendant could not be convicted of burglary unless he had the requisite intent to commit theft or robbery when he entered the dwelling. The court then certified three questions of great public importance. The first dealt with whether an amendment to Fla. Stat. ch. 810.02 legislatively overruled the Florida Supreme Court's decision in Delgado as to cases not final at the time of that decision in which offenses were committed before February 1, 2000, thereby permitting a trial court to instruct a jury that it might find a defendant guilty of burglary despite evidence showing a legal entry into a premises and that an offense was committed therein while the defendant remained within non-surreptitiously? The other two questions asked whether Fla. Const. art. X, § 9 applied to changes in law based on judicial opinions and if so, how could art. X, § 9 be reconciled with giving changes in law application in pipeline cases when a crime was committed before a change in the law?


OUTCOME: Defendant's burglary conviction was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial on that charge. The remaining convictions were affirmed without comment. On remand, the trial court was directed to consider whether the outcome of the burglary charge necessitated resentencing on the aggravated battery and false imprisonment charges. If so, the trial court was to resentence defendant accordingly.

Mincey v. State


CASE NO. 4D03-3018


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


889 So. 2d 211; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 19126; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2824



December 15, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 3, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County; Robert Makemson, Judge; L.T. Case No. 96-308 CF A.
Mincey v. State, 704 So. 2d 537, 1997 Fla. App. LEXIS 14128 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for the Nineteenth Judicial Circuit, Martin County (Florida), which denied his motion to correct an illegal sentence under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the State conceded that defendant was improperly sentenced on a violation of probation by an increase on his guidelines scoresheet for the primary offense, from level 8 to level 9. The increase in scoresheet level was based on a law that was struck down by Heggs. Applying Heggs, the increase should not have been applied to defendant. Rather, the 1994 scoresheet had to be applied. However, the State argued that relief was not properly sought under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a). The appellate court concluded that even though defendant should have employed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b) motion in the trial court to challenge his unconstitutional sentence, the sentence imposed, in excess of the statutory maximum, was the type of fundamental sentencing error that could be raised on appeal absent preservation.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded for re-sentencing.

 

1767 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Strazdins


Case No. 2D03-4335


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


890 So. 2d 334; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 18815; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2777



December 10, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 4, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; Jack A. St. Arnold, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida), which imposed a sentence on defendant for the offense of trafficking in methylenedioxymetheamphetamine (MDMA) following a no contest plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded no contest to the offense of trafficking in MDMA. The trial court sentenced defendant. The State appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in not imposing the three-year mandatory minimum sentence for trafficking in MDMA weighing between 10 and 200 grams. The court held that at the time the trial court imposed the sentence, the district had decided that a mandatory minimum sentence for the offense of trafficking in MDMA was unconstitutional. Thus, the trial court lacked the discretion to impose a mandatory minimum sentence on defendant. Thereafter, the state's highest court decided to allow the minimum sentence. Accordingly, a mandatory minimum sentence for trafficking in MDMA, imposed under 2000 Fla. Laws ch. 320, was a legal sentence. The trial court had a nondiscretionary duty to impose the three-year mandatory minimum sentence pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 893.135(1)(k)(2) (2001). On remand, defendant should be permitted to withdraw his plea to the charge of trafficking in MDMA.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's sentence of defendant and remanded the matter for further proceedings where defendant could have the opportunity to withdraw his plea.

1769 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Branch v. State (In re Branch)


Case No. 2D01-2087


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


890 So. 2d 322; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 18821; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2779



December 10, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 28, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hillsborough County; Jack Espinosa, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Hillsborough County (Florida) entered an involuntary civil commitment order against appellant patient as a sexually violent predator under Fla. Stat. chs. 394.910-394.931 (2001). The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: During the hearing, the patient's counsel repeatedly objected to the admission of hearsay concerning alleged prior uncharged bad acts, claiming that while the hearsay might have been admissible under Fla. Stat. ch. 394.9155, the patient had no ability to defend himself because he was incapable of assisting her in disputing the factual allegations due to his incompetence. The instant court agreed, as not only did that deny the patient his due process right to present a defense, but it also denied him his right to counsel because counsel could not effectively defend him without his assistance. The appointment of a guardian ad litem was no substitute for a competent defendant. The court's concern was not with the patient's substantive due process rights, but with his procedural due process rights. Not every Ryce Act respondent had to be competent during a Ryce Act proceeding, but a Ryce Act respondent had a due process right to be competent only when the State intended to present hearsay evidence of alleged facts that were neither admitted by way of a plea nor subjected to adversarial testing at trial, and thus subject to dispute and counterevidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Smalley v. State


CASE NO. 5D03-2513


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


889 So. 2d 100; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17815; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2626



November 19, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 8, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, John M. Griesbaum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida), which convicted him of second degree murder pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 782.04(2) (2002) following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant testified that he was being threatened by the victim and that the gun accidentally fired, several state witnesses testified that the victim was not threatening defendant and that defendant went to his room and got a gun, shot it into a wall, and then followed the victim to his car and shot him at close range. Affirming the conviction, the court held that (1) although the witnesses' testimony presented at trial concerning the shooting of the victim were in conflict, the evidence presented by the State was sufficient to create a jury issue regarding defendant's state of mind at the time of the shooting; (2) the jury's rejection of "intentional discharge of a firearm" was not truly inconsistent with its conviction of defendant for second degree murder because second degree murder did not require the finding of an intentional discharge of a firearm; and (3) Fla. Stat. Ann. § 943.325 (2002) was not unconstitutional under the Fourth Amendment because a convicted person had no reasonable expectation of privacy with respect to blood samples for DNA testing which outweighed the State's interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

J.J. v. Dep't of Children & Families


CASE NOS. 4D04-762, 4D04-822, 4D04-906


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


886 So. 2d 1046; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17354; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2598



November 17, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Consolidated appeals and cross-appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Richard B. Burk, Senior Judge; L.T. Case No. CJ99-300381JK.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Florida Department of Children and Families, sough to terminate the parental rights of appellant parents. The Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County, Florida, did not do so, nor did it readjudicate the children dependent or dismiss the petition. Instead, it authorized the Department to "re-notice" the matter for further proceedings. The parents and appellant guardian ad litem sought review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the Department had proved that the parents were unable to substantially comply with the case plans, and that there were no further services that the State could provide the parents to successfully reunite them with their children. However, it held that the Department had not proved that termination was the least restrictive resolution or was in the best interests of the children. The appellate court held that while the parents completed many of their case plan tasks, this did not equate to "substantial compliance" with their case plan under Fla. Stat. ch. 39.01(68). But as the Department failed to prove termination was in the manifest best interests of the children, under Fla. Stat. ch. 39.811, the trial court had to either declare the children dependent or return them to the parents with the opportunity to retain jurisdiction or end the Department's jurisdiction over the parent-child relationship. The trial court erred in ruling that Fla. Stat. ch. 39.811 was unconstitutional for acting as an improper limit on its powers to fashion a proper remedy for the children.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to fashion an order that complied with the termination of the parental rights statute.

Simmons v. State


CASE NO. 1D02-4977


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


886 So. 2d 399; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17297; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2565



November 15, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 30, 2004. Released for Publication December 1, 2004.
Review granted by Simmons v. State, 898 So. 2d 81, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 597 (Fla., 2005)
Approved by Simmons v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2684 (Fla., Nov. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Columbia County. Paul S. Bryan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Florida) to luring or enticing a child by use of an on-line service, Fla. Stat. ch. 847.0135 (2002), and transmission of materials harmful to a minor, Fla. Stat. ch. 847.0138 (2002), after the trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the counts as unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant engaged in Internet chat room and on-line conversations about sex with a Florida deputy sheriff, who posed as a 13-year-old Florida girl named Sandi. Defendant sent nude photographs of himself and eventually traveled to Florida to meet "Sandi" in a hotel room and engage in sexual relations with her. Defendant was arrested upon his arrival at the hotel. Defendant argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 847.0138 was overbroad because it limited communications on the Internet to those which would only be suitable for children, thereby depriving adults of their constitutional right to engage in protected speech. On appeal, the court found that ch. 847.0138 was not unconstitutional as it only pertained to harmful images, information, or data sent to a specific individual known by the defendant to be a minor, via electronic mail. Therefore, under ch. 847.0138, adults were not deprived of their constitutional right to engage in protected speech as only communications to a minor were prohibited.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed.
