Envtl. Confederation of Southwest Fla., Inc. v. Dep't of Envtl. Prot.


CASE NO. 1D03-0784, CASE NO. 1D03-1717


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


886 So. 2d 1013; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 16079; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2421



October 28, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 15, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from final orders of the Department of Environmental Protection.
Envtl. Confederation of Southwest Fla., Inc. v. IMC Phosphates, Inc., 857 So. 2d 207, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11571 (Fla. 1st DCA 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant companies sought review of the final orders of appellee Florida Department of Environmental Protection (DEP). The issues were (1) whether an amendment to Fla. Stat. ch. 403.412(5) relating to standing to challenge decisions of DEP was violative of the single subject requirement and (2) whether the alleged single subject violation was rendered moot by the subsequent readoption of the revised Fla. Stat. ch. 403.412.


OVERVIEW: The DEP dismissed two petitions on the ground that the companies could not establish standing under the requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. 403.412(5). The Florida Legislature did not expressly state in 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 261 that the amendment was to apply retroactively. The changes to Fla. Stat. ch. 403.412(5) made by 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 261 eliminated the companies' previous right to initiate a proceeding upon notice of DEP's intent to issue a permit. Essentially a class of people no longer had a right where one existed before. The provisions contained within 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 261 did not violate the single subject requirement. Each provision in the act was logically related to environmental protection and was specifically related to Everglades restoration. Each provision in the act was germane to the overall purpose stated in the act. All of the provisions related to the protection of the environment and to the policies and practices of the DEP. The act also promoted the clear purpose of the legislation. The legislation was valid on its face, and the title of the bill was sufficiently broad to encompass the subject matter of the bill.


OUTCOME: The decision of the DEP was affirmed.

Turner v. State


CASE NO. 5D03-684


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


888 So. 2d 73; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 16216; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2437



October 27, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Turner v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 20592 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Dec. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Brevard County, John M. Griesbaum, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida), which designated him a sexual predator under Florida's Sexual Predator Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21(4) (2002), after he pled guilty to sexual battery and kidnaping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant posed as a police officer and threatened alleged prostitutes over the age of 18 with arrest in order to gain sexual favors. He was charged with sexual battery and kidnaping. He pled nolo contendere in four cases and agreed to a sentence of 10 years' imprisonment followed by 45 years of sex offender probation. The State subsequently filed a notice in each of the four cases that defendant qualified as a sexual predator. Prior to accepting the plea agreement, the trial court advised defendant that in all likelihood he would be declared a sexual predator. The trial court subsequently entered orders in each case declaring that he was a sexual predator. On appeal, defendant challenged his sexual predator designation and asserted that the trial court's ruling violated his substantive due process rights. The court found that defendant's designation as a sexual predator did not influence the merits of his criminal conviction or affect the foundation of his case. Because the trial court's designation was a collateral matter and did not constitute fundamental error, defendant's failure to present his argument to the trial court precluded appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Dep't of State, Div. of Elections v. Martin


CASE NO. 1D04-4517


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


885 So. 2d 453; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15734; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2380



October 25, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As corrected October 26, 2004. Released for Publication November 10, 2004.
Affirmed by Fla. Dep't of State, Div. of Elections v. Martin, 916 So. 2d 763, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2207 (Fla., Nov. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. Janet E. Ferris, Judge.
Fla. Dep't of State v. Martin, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1984 (Fla., Oct. 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Florida Department of State, Division of Elections sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) which entered a mandatory injunction directing the Division to, inter alia, permit a Democratic candidate for Congress to withdraw and notify appellee Democratic Party Executive Committee officials of their right to designate a nominee to fill the vacancy.


OVERVIEW: A congressional candidate stated that he wished to withdraw as a candidate. The Division informed him that, in the interest of avoiding disruption and confusion, he would not be permitted to withdraw. The Democratic Executive Committee obtained a mandatory injunction requiring the Division to declare that a vacancy was created by the candidate's withdrawal. The appellate court held that the Florida Legislature intended that Fla. Stat. ch. 101.253 (2004) governed when and how a candidate could seek to withdraw his or her name from nomination and be removed from the ballot. Fla. Stat. ch. 100.111 (2004) was intended to address the next step. Because the second sentence of Fla. Stat. ch. 101.253(2) vested unbridled discretion in the Florida Department of State, Division of Elections, it violated Fla. Const. art. II, § 3 and was, therefore, unconstitutional. Accordingly, Fla. Stat. ch. 101.253(2) was unconstitutional in its entirety. The candidate's withdrawal had to be recognized. Fla. Stat. ch. 100.111(4)(b) was then the applicable procedure to be employed for the selection of a replacement nominee.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1779 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Burton v. State (In re Burton)


Case No. 2D01-223


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


884 So. 2d 1112; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15602; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2365



October 22, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 18, 2004.
Review denied by Burton v. State, 913 So. 2d 595, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2019 (Fla., Sept. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Polk County; Harvey A. Kornstein and Cecelia M. Moore, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; question certified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Polk County (Florida) committed defendant as a sexually violent predator under the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 394.910-.931 (1999). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took issue with several pretrial rulings of the trial court, several evidentiary rulings that took place during the course of trial, the State's closing argument, and the jury instructions. The trial court allowed use of the Rapid Risk Assessment for Sex Offense Recidivism (RRASOR), Psychopathy Checklist-Revised (PCL-R) and the Sexual Violence Risk-20 (SVR-20) tests. The appellate court ruled that the RRASOR and PCL-R tests met the requirements of Frye. Given the nature of the SVR-20, it was not the type of objective scientific principle or test with which Frye was concerned. Any testimony regarding the use and application of the SVR-20 was tantamount to pure opinion testimony, which was admissible without having to satisfy Frye. The State did not violate its plea agreement to a term of incarceration followed by probation by seeking civil commitment under the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 394.910-.931 (1999), after the term of incarceration was served. The trial court's use of the term "sexually violent predator" was not improper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and a question certified.

Cirelli v. Ent


Case No. 5D03-1493


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


885 So. 2d 423; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15352; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2350



October 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 4, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Volusia County, William D. Palmer, Acting Circuit Judge. John W. Watson, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlocked owners appealed from two partial summary judgments entered by the Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida) in favor of appellee property owners in the landlocked owners' suit seeking to establish a statutory way of necessity under Fla. Stat. ch. 704.01(2) (2002).


OVERVIEW: The landlocked owners argued that the Florida Marketable Record Titles to Real Property Act (MRTA), Fla. Stat. ch. 712, did not preclude relief. The appellate court held that statutory ways of necessity did not require a common source of title and were dependent upon factors not required for common law ways of necessity. Further, statutory ways of necessity were based on public policy, while common law ways of necessity were not. Thus, language in prior case law on statutory ways of necessity did not control. The right to a statutory way of necessity was a present right that came into existence when the necessary factors existed. As it was a present right, it was not a right, claim, or interest that would predate the root of title to the servient estate and was not extinguishable by the MRTA. Further, the constitutional validity of Fla. Stat. ch. 704.01(2) (2003) was based on public policy concerns, as was the constitutional validity of eminent domain proceedings. As the right to acquire property by eminent domain proceedings could not be extinguished by the MRTA, the right to acquire access to landlocked property via ch. 704.01(2) could not be extinguished by the MRTA.


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings. Conflict with a Florida Court of Appeal, Second District, decision was noted and the Second District's question of a matter of great public importance was certified.

 

1782 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Crist v. Presidential Women's Ctr.


CASE NO. 4D02-4485


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


884 So. 2d 526; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15011; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2290



October 13, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 29, 2004.
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Presidential Women's Ctr., 2006 Fla. LEXIS 555 (Fla., Apr. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the Fifteenth Judicial Circuit, Palm Beach County; Ronald V. Alvarez, Judge; L.T. Case No. CL 97-5796 AG.
State v. Presidential Women's Ctr., 707 So. 2d 1145, 1998 Fla. App. LEXIS 1372 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifteenth Judicial Circuit Court, Palm Beach County (Florida), granted summary judgment to appellees, two clinics and a doctor, finding that Fla. Stat. ch. 390.0111 (1997), 1997 Fla. Laws ch. 151, § 1, also known as the Women's Right to Know Act (Act), was unconstitutional. Appellants, the State of Florida through the Attorney General and the Secretary of the Department of Health (the State), sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the Act impermissibly intruded upon the woman's right to choose at every stage of her pregnancy without furthering a compelling State interest. The trial court also held that: (1) the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it required the physician performing the abortion to satisfy a unique and confusing reasonable patient standard; and (2) the issue was ripe for summary judgment since the Act was unconstitutional on its face. The State argued on appeal that summary judgment was improper because a factual record could be developed to demonstrate that the Act did not result in an increased cost to the woman, caused no intrusion on the physician's practice, and allowed the physician discretion. The appeals court disagreed. Even if the State could support its positions, the Act was unconstitutional because it imposed significant obstacles and burdens intruding upon a woman's choice between abortion and childbirth. Further, to sever the challenged portions of the statute would sever subsections of the informed consent section. To do so reduced the section to being nonsensical and incomplete.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gaudet v. Fla. Bd. of Prof'l Eng'rs


CASE NO. 4D03-340


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


900 So. 2d 574; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15012; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2283



October 13, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 6, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the State of Florida, Board of Professional Engineers; L.T. Case No. BPR 2003-00007.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Florida Board of Professional Engineers (Board) entered a final order denying appellant applicant's petition for licensure as an engineer by endorsement, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 471.015(3)(a), (b) (2002). The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Board concluded that the applicant was ineligible for a license by endorsement under Fla. Stat. ch. 471.015(3)(a), because he did not receive a degree from a Board-approved engineering program. It also held that when the applicant received his Pennsylvania license, that state did not require accreditation from the Board of Engineering and Technology (ABET). So, Pennsylvania did not have a statute that was substantially the same as Florida's and therefore the applicant was not eligible for licensure under Fla. Stat. ch. 471.015(3)(b). On appeal, the court first held, and the Board conceded, that a scrivenor's error existed as to the state in which the applicant was licensed. Thus, this was to be corrected. Second, while the Board promulgated a rule specifying criteria for approval of schools and curricula for applicants having degrees for foreign schools where ABET accreditation was unavailable, it failed and refused to promulgate a similar rule where ABET accreditation was available, contrary to the intent of Fla. Stat. ch. 471.013(1)(a). Thus, the Board was ordered to promulgate said rules. Due to this holding, the applicant's equal protection argument was not addressed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Homer & Bonner, P.A. v. Miami-Dade County


CASE NO. 3D04-1752


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, THIRD DISTRICT


884 So. 2d 425; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 14292; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2170



September 29, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 15, 2004.
Review denied by McGrath v. Homer & Bonner, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 215 (Fla., Jan. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County, Margarita Esquiroz, Judge. LOWER TRIBUNAL NOS. 99-21456 99-23765.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Miami-Dade County (Florida) approved an amended settlement in a class action suit filed against appellee city, challenging the validity of parking surcharges paid at city parking facilities. Appellant class counsel and others sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The amended settlement agreement created a common fund of $ 14 million from which class members could claim a surcharge refund. The appeals court found that this portion of the judgment was proper. However, the trial court also awarded $ 3.6 million in attorney's fees. Using the lodestar method, the trial court awarded counsel hourly rates of $ 400 and $ 450 per hour. The trial court then applied a 3.8 multiplier. While the trial court correctly used the lodestar method to determine the amount of attorney's fees, it was inappropriate to apply a multiplier because the instant case was neither complex nor uncertain. Once the statute was declared unconstitutional, the attorneys simply had to negotiate the best deal. Additionally, the class attorney admitted in open court that an hourly fee of between $ 400-$ 450 per hour was a more than adequate hourly wage. The trial court, along with every attorney in the courtroom, agreed.


OUTCOME: That portion of the amended settlement which did not deal with the attorney's fees awarded was affirmed. But, the attorney's fees were reversed, and the matter was remanded for a redetermination of the same.

 

1787 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Gill v. State


Case No. 2D03-2229


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


886 So. 2d 988; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 14102; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2154



September 24, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 17, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Gill v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 21298 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Nov. 18, 2004)
Review denied by Gill v. State, 909 So. 2d 861, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1625 (Fla., July 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal and cross-appeal from the Circuit Court for Manatee County; Peter A. Dubensky and Marc B. Gilner, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Manatee County (Florida) imposed an upward departure sentence against defendant under the 1994 Florida Sentencing Guidelines in a resentencing proceeding. Defendant appealed that order, and the State cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The sentencing court imposed an upward departure sentence of 13 years in state prison, followed by five years on probation, based on its determination that defendant exhibited a flagrant disregard for the safety of others, supported by the fact that: (1) the volume of alcohol in defendant's system was nearly three times the legal limit; and (2) the crime occurred on one of the busiest roadways the county. But, the State conceded that there was no evidence that the intersection was under heavy traffic conditions at the time of the accident and that the extent of intoxication standing alone was an invalid reason to depart because it was already an element of the offense. Accordingly, the trial court's reasons for departing upward from the 1994 guidelines were invalid. The 1996 amendment to the offense severity ranking chart operated as an amendment to the 1994 guidelines. The 1996 legislation, establishing a level 9 severity ranking for the offense of DUI manslaughter with failure to provide information and to render aid, was thus a valid legislative enactment. Hence, defendant should have been sentenced with a scoresheet on which his offense was scored as a level 9 offense.


OUTCOME: The sentence was reversed and the case was remanded for the imposition of a guidelines sentence using a corrected scoresheet.

Rabin v. Dep't of Revenue


CASE NO. 4D03-3494


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FOURTH DISTRICT


884 So. 2d 983; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 13882; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 2142



September 22, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Rabin v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 18609 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., Nov. 16, 2004)
Review denied by Rabin v. Fla. Dep't of Revenue, 901 So. 2d 874, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 915 (Fla., Apr. 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of a non-final order from the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County; Robert Lance Andrews, Judge; L.T. Case No. 02-22977-09.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit, Broward County (Florida), which transferred the venue of the taxpayers' action seeking a declaration that the sales and use tax on certain computers and their components was unconstitutional. Venue was transferred to Leon County, the home venue of defendant Florida State Department of Revenue.


OVERVIEW: The action was originally filed by a computer software company, which challenged a notice of a proposed tax assessment. Venue for that action was properly in Broward County. An amended complaint was filed, which for the first time included the taxpayers' action. The software company voluntarily dismissed its action, leaving the taxpayers as the only parties. The Department then filed its motion for change of venue. The court affirmed the transfer. As the payment of the sales tax was not an "assessment," the venue provisions of Fla. Stat. ch. 72.011(4)(a) did not apply. Therefore, once the software company was no longer in the case, venue in Broward County was not appropriate. Under the "home venue" privilege, the Department had the right to demand venue in Leon County. The "sword wielder" exception to that privilege did not apply.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order transferring venue from Broward County to Leon County was affirmed.

ACLU of Fla., Inc. v. Hood


CASE NO. 1D04-3693


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


881 So. 2d 664; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 12515; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1953



August 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Review granted by ACLU of Fla., Inc. v. Hood, 882 So. 2d 384, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1464 (Fla., 2004)
Judgment entered by ACLU of Fla., Inc. v. Hood, 888 So. 2d 621, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1514 (Fla., Sept. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Leon County. Jonathan Sjostrom, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Certified to Supreme Court


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Leon County (Florida) dismissed a complaint filed by plaintiffs, a civil liberties organization and others, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief, which alleged the ballot title and summary did not adequately communicate the effect of a proposed amendment to Fla. Const. art. X, § 22. Plaintiffs appealed, seeking certification to the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: In response to plaintiffs' contention, the instant court first found that a final appealable order had been issued by the circuit court. After considering the proposed amendment regarding parental notice of termination of a minor's pregnancy, it then decided that the issues presented in the appeal were of great public importance or were likely to have a great effect on the proper administration of justice throughout the state. Third, it recognized that on two prior occasions, the Florida Legislature enacted legislation on this subject and both were found to unconstitutionally interfere with a minor's right to privacy. Further, circumstances existed which required that the supreme court immediately resolve the issues, rather than allow the normal appellate process to run its course. Fourth, it found that the apparent intent of the proposed constitutional amendment was to remove this barrier to the legislature's authority to require parental notification when a minor sought termination of a pregnancy. Therefore, the instant litigation presented a question of great public importance to be decided by the supreme court.


OUTCOME: Certification of the instant action, requiring immediate resolution by the supreme court, was granted.

Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Fountain


CASE NO. 1D03-5488


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


883 So. 2d 300; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 12466; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1937



August 24, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 9, 2004.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ certiorari granted and circuit court's order is quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, The Florida Department of Highway Safety and Motor Vehicles, sought a writ of certiorari to quash an order rendered by the circuit court (Florida) requiring it to issue respondent driver a hardship driver's license.


OVERVIEW: The Department permanently revoked the driver's driving privileges because he had four prior DUI convictions. However, the circuit court granted the driver a hardship license, relying on the 1997 version of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.271. After reviewing the facts in the record, the instant court held that the circuit court erred in doing so. Based on the plain language of the 1997 version of ch. 322.271, it was within the Department's discretion to decide whether to reinstate the license of a driver who met the statutorily specified requirements under Fla. Stat. ch. 322.271(4)(a)-(b). Thus, had the 1997 version of the statute been applicable, the circuit court should have remanded the case for the Department to conduct a hearing to determine whether the driver met said requirements. Moreover, under the 1998 version of the statute, neither the circuit court nor the Department had discretion to issue the hardship license.


OUTCOME: The writ was granted, and the circuit court's order was quashed.

Henderson v. Crosby


CASE NO. 1D03-2367


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


883 So. 2d 847; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 12468; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1937



August 24, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 9, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Henderson v. Crosby, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 16034 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Sept. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the circuit court for Leon County. Nikki Ann Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoners filed an action against defendant prison officials, arguing that the prisoners had been deprived of their right of access to courts pursuant to Fla. Const. art. I, § 21. The parties eventually filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) granted the officials' motion for summary judgment and entered a final declaratory judgment. The prisoners appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner's argued that actions taken by the prison officials, which limited access to prison law libraries, violated Fla. Const. art. I, § 21. These actions included the removal of books, limiting inter-library loan, and restricting hours of operation. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in applying a federal test, which was narrower than the Florida Mitchell test. Section 21 required that the Department of Corrections provide affirmative assistance as to all types of claims that might be filed in Florida's courts, including those based on federal law, not merely those claims challenging convictions, sentences, or conditions of confinement, or seeking to vindicate a fundamental constitutional right. Furthermore, the Department's justification for its action or inaction had to satisfy the strict-scrutiny test when such action or inaction resulted in a significant impediment to inmates' access to the courts. However, the appellate court held that the prisoners were not entitled to relief. As a matter of law, either individually or collectively, the actions complained of did not constitute significant impediments to the right of access to Florida courts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Ducharme


Case No. 5D03-3433


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Belvin Perry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Motion GRANTED; discretionary stay ENTERED; Conflict CERTIFIED; Question CERTIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee filed a motion to vacate an automatic stay entered by the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) pursuant to Fla. R. App. P. 9.310(b)(2). The stay was imposed upon an order entered by the trial court that dismissed a civil commitment petition appellant State had filed against appellee under the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. chs. 394.910-394.931 (2000).


OVERVIEW: Appellee sought dismissal from civil commitment, citing to Atkinson. Upon review, the trial court granted the motion and directed appellee's release. The State filed its notice of appeal and invoked the stay provisions set forth in Rule 9.310. Appellee challenged his continued detention, arguing the automatic stay provisions of Rule 9.310(b) were not applicable to cases involving detention under the Act. The State responded by arguing that Mitchell supported its position that the automatic stay provisions of Rule 9.310(b)(2) were applicable. The appeals court found the dissent's reasoning in Mitchell, that Rule 9.310(b)(2) was never intended to apply to matters involving involuntary civil commitments, to be more persuasive than the majority's position. Due to the appeals court's disagreement with the majority opinion on the issue, it certified conflict with Mitchell, and certified the following question to the Florida Supreme Court as being a matter of great public importance: whether the automatic stay provision set forth in Rule 9.310 applied to civil commitment proceedings instituted under the Act.


OUTCOME: The motion was granted, a discretionary stay was entered, conflict was certified, and a question was certified.

Hunsicker v. State


Case Nos. 5D03-373 & 5D03-527


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIFTH DISTRICT


881 So. 2d 1166; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 12201; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1924



August 20, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Hunsicker v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 15562 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Sept. 22, 2004)
Review denied by Hunsicker v. State, 894 So. 2d 970, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 193 (Fla., Jan. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Orange County, Reginald Whitehead, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Orange County (Florida) that convicted defendant of sexual battery, lewd or lascivious conduct, and burglary of a dwelling with an assault or battery, in violation of Fla. Stat. chs. 794.011(2), 800.04(5)-(7), and 810.02(2)(a), respectively. On appeal, defendant contended his sentences violated double jeopardy protections.


OVERVIEW: At no time during the sentencing hearing did defendant object that his sentences violated double jeopardy principles or that his dual sentence as a habitual offender and prison releasee reoffender were improper. Moreover, defendant did not avail himself of the procedure in Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b) to raise the alleged errors before the trial court. Nonetheless, the legislative intent was clear that separate punishments had to be imposed for each criminal offense created by the statute. Therefore, with respect to defendant's convictions for the separate crimes of lewd or lascivious molestation, lewd or lascivious conduct, and lewd or lascivious exhibition, there was no double jeopardy violation. Specifically, defendant was charged with enticing the victim to touch his penis and was charged with putting his mouth on the victim's breast. Although there was no legislative intent to punish separately each act, there was a sufficient temporal break between the two acts to have allowed defendant to pause, reflect, and form a new criminal intent for each offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Moore v. State


CASE NO. 1D03-3880


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


880 So. 2d 826; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 12092; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1896



August 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 3, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court of Leon County. James Hankinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the Circuit Court of Leon County (Florida) which designated him a sexual predator in accordance with the Florida Sexual Predators Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.21 (2003).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the Florida Sexual Predator Act was unconstitutional in several ways, and argued that the trial court lost jurisdiction to enter the order once 60 days had elapsed after sentencing. The appellate court rejected defendant's contention that the Act violated the separation of powers clause in Fla. Const. art. II, § 3. The appellate court further held that the Act did not violate defendant's right to privacy pursuant to Fla. Const. art. I, § 23. Even if a sexual predator's address could be viewed as non-public information, its dissemination under the Act did not violate the sexual predator's constitutional right to privacy. The appellate court further held that the Act did not violate equal protection requirements merely because it did not apply to offenses which took place before Oct. 1, 1993. It was not a requirement of equal protection that every statutory classification be all-inclusive. The appellate court finally held that Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(c) did not divest the trial court of jurisdiction to enter the order. That rule plainly dealt with the reduction and modification of sentences, and did not govern a post-sentence designation under the Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bush v. Holmes


CASE NOS.: 1D02-3160, 1D02-3163 and 1D02-3199


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, FIRST DISTRICT


2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 12479; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1877



August 16, 2004, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at Bush v. Holmes, 886 So. 2d 340, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17242 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., Nov. 12, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court for Leon County. P. Kevin Davey, Judge.
Bush v. Holmes, 867 So. 2d 1270, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 3598 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; QUESTION CERTIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two consolidated actions, defendants, the state governor and other state officials, as well as members of the state department of education (governor) appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Leon County (Florida) which entered a final summary judgment and ruled that the Florida Opportunity Scholarship Program (OSP), Fla. Stat. ch. 229.0537 (1999), facially violated Fla. Const. art. I, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, various parents of children in Florida elementary and secondary schools and several organizations, filed a complaint seeking declaratory and injunctive relief challenging the facial constitutionality of the OSP. The trial court declared Fla. Stat. ch. 229.0537 facially unconstitutional and enjoined the governor from taking any action to implement the OSP. Initially, the vast majority of students participating in the OSP (47 of 51) enrolled in sectarian institutions of learning. Further, the vast majority of the schools receiving state funds from OSP vouchers at the time of the hearing were operated by religious or church groups. As such, for a court to interpret the no-aid provision as adding nothing substantive to Fla. Const. art. I, § 3 would have required that court to ignore the clear meaning of the text of the provision and its formative history. Finally, nothing in the Florida no-aid provision created a constitutional bar to state aid to a non-profit institution that was not sectarian in nature simply because the institution was affiliated with a religious order or religious organization.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the question of the constitutionality of a statute was certified for appellate review.

 

1800 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. Smith


Case No. 2D02-4018


COURT OF APPEAL OF FLORIDA, SECOND DISTRICT


882 So. 2d 1037; 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 11856; 29 Fla. L. Weekly D 1863



August 13, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 27, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Pinellas County; W. Douglas Baird, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Pinellas County (Florida) that dismissed their complaint with prejudice. The taxpayers contended that Fla. Stat. ch. 196.011(1)(b) violated their right to privacy under various clauses of both the Florida and the United States Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed a timely application for ad valorem tax exemption. They declined to make the required disclosure of their social security numbers. Their application was denied based on their refusal to make the required disclosure. As such, their property was assessed for that year and in each subsequent year without the homestead exemption. The taxpayers claimed that by reason of the assessment of taxes against the property without the benefit of the homestead tax exemption, they paid higher amounts of property taxes than they would have paid otherwise. In dismissing the claim, the trial court failed to determine whether a compelling state interest-not a legitimate state interest-warranted the intrusion into the taxpayers' privacy. The court should first have determined whether the taxpayers had a legitimate expectation of privacy in their social security numbers without regard to other considerations such as the necessity to submit an application in order to obtain the benefit of the homestead tax exemption. The trial court erred in concluding that the taxpayers had no legitimate expectation of privacy in their social security numbers.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded with respect to the taxpayers' state privacy rights claim, and affirmed in all other respects.
